     - [x] **Test surface (5 new e2e tests in `tests/codegen.rs`, gated `--features llvm`).** `test_e2e_match_owned_struct_destructure_smoke` (closes the predecessor gap), `test_e2e_match_ref_struct_field_passes_to_ref_param` (struct shorthand under `ref Foo`), `test_e2e_match_ref_option_payload_passes_to_ref_param` (tuple-variant payload under `ref Option[i64]`), `test_e2e_match_owned_struct_field_owned_call_unaffected` (regression-pin: owned scrutinees never touch the shim), `test_e2e_match_mut_ref_struct_field_passes_to_mut_ref_param` (`mut ref` mode ABI parity; explicitly does not exercise mutation propagation).

     **Slice 3a caveats addressed by slice 3b.**
     - [x] **Mutation-propagation gap closed in slice 3b.** Slice 3a's shim aliased a _copy_ of the scrutinee data, so `mut ref`-scrutinee write-through silently dropped on the floor. Probe tests (written 2026-05-14 to convert the silent miscompile into a known-failing pin) all confirmed the divergence — e.g., `match b { Bag { n } => set_to(n, 99) }` under `mut ref b` left `b.n` at its pre-match value. Slice 3b's GEP-based path closes this; mutation now flows back to the scrutinee storage.
     - [x] **Slice rest binding intentionally not in scope.** `bind_slice_pattern` already materializes Array rest as a `Slice[T]` header (per design.md § Slice patterns — Mutability propagation), and slice headers are already borrow-shaped at the LLVM level. The leaf-binding shim does not apply to slice rest. Slice 3b's GEP path also does not retarget slice-rest bindings — `bind_slice_pattern` is structurally orthogonal and the existing slice-header layout already supports write-through via header GEP + element-pointer arithmetic.

     **Slice 3b — true GEP-based aliasing into scrutinee storage (shipped 2026-05-14).**
     - [x] **`compile_match` ref-mode routing.** At entry, when the scrutinee is an `Identifier` in `ref_params` whose pointee is a `StructType` (covers `ref Foo` plain-struct and `ref Option[T]` / `ref Result[T,E]` / user-enum cases via `enum_layouts.llvm_type`), capture `(scrut_ptr, pointee_ty)` via `get_data_ptr`. Pattern conditions still run against the value-form scrutinee (tag/field checks are identical between value and pointer); only the binding side routes through the pointer path. Routing dispatch is per-arm with a graceful fallback to slice 3a's value-source path for pattern shapes that the pointer path doesn't yet handle (or-patterns, at-bindings, multi-word enum payloads with aggregate sub-patterns).
     - [x] **`bind_pattern_values_via_ptr(pattern, scrut_ptr, pointee_ty) -> Result<Option<()>, String>`** at `src/codegen.rs`. Pointer-source binder. Coverage:
       - [x] `PatternKind::Wildcard` — bind nothing.
       - [x] `PatternKind::Binding` — the scrutinee pointer IS the binding's alias target; emit a leaf shim at that pointer.
       - [x] `PatternKind::Struct` (plain non-enum struct, `struct_types.get(name) == pointee_ty`) — GEP into each field by name-resolved index; recurse on nested `Struct` sub-patterns whose field type is `StructType`; emit leaf shim for shorthand or `Binding` / `Wildcard` sub-patterns.
       - [x] `PatternKind::TupleVariant` (non-shared enum, single-word payload OR padded primitive payload) — locate the layout via the layout's `llvm_type == pointee_ty` (with fallthrough to variant-name match); GEP into the payload word; emit leaf shim. Recognizes `Option[i64]`'s "padded primitive" case where the seeded layout reserves `option_payload_words` slots but the actual payload occupies only word 0 — checked via `num_words > 1 && sub_is_leaf && first_word_is_primitive`.
       - [x] Other shapes (or-patterns, at-bindings, slice patterns, range patterns, literals, aggregate-payload variants) return `Ok(None)` and defer to the value-source `bind_pattern_values`. Correctness under those shapes still holds via the slice 3a shim (with the copy-alias semantic for mutation, which the deferred shapes don't surface in any current test or stdlib use).
     - [x] **`emit_ref_leaf_binding_at_ptr(name, field_ptr, inner_ty, label)`** helper. Allocates a `ptr` shim alloca, stores `field_ptr` into it, registers `variables[name]` (slot type `ptr`) + `ref_params[name] = inner_ty`. The shim mechanic is identical to slice 3a's; only the stored pointer changes — slice 3b stores a GEP into the scrutinee, slice 3a stored the address of a local value-alloca. `load_variable`'s existing auto-deref path and `compile_call`'s existing `is_ref` arg path both work unchanged.
     - [x] **Reused `pattern_binding_borrow_modes`** — the slice 3a side table still flags which leaf bindings need the ref-binding ABI shape. Slice 3b only changes _what pointer_ the shim alloca stores.
     - [x] **Test surface (3 new probe tests in `tests/codegen.rs`, gated `--features llvm`).** `test_e2e_match_mut_ref_struct_field_write_through_propagates` (single field), `test_e2e_match_mut_ref_option_payload_write_through_propagates` (Option payload), `test_e2e_match_mut_ref_struct_two_fields_independent_write_through` (two-field independent write-through). All three failed under slice 3a (silent miscompile, returned pre-mutation values), all three pass under slice 3b.
     - [x] **Touched files.** `src/codegen.rs` (`bind_pattern_values_via_ptr` + `emit_ref_leaf_binding_at_ptr` helpers, ref-mode routing at `compile_match` entry, per-arm dispatch with fallback), `tests/codegen.rs` (3 new probe tests). No typechecker / lowering changes — the existing `pattern_binding_borrow_modes` table from slice 3a is sufficient.

     **Out of scope at slice 3b — punted to future work when triggered.**
     - [ ] **Or-patterns under ref scrutinee.** Falls back to slice 3a's value-source path (correct match condition, copy-aliased binding). Pull when a real program needs write-through across or-pattern alternatives — would require unifying alternative-specific bind targets into a phi node of pointers.
     - [ ] **At-bindings under ref scrutinee.** Same shape as or-patterns. Pull when needed.
     - [ ] **Multi-word aggregate enum payloads under ref scrutinee** (e.g., `Result.Ok(MyStruct)` where `MyStruct` spans >1 payload word, OR `Some(String)` where the String spans 3 words). The single-word + padded-primitive branches cover the common case; the multi-word aggregate case requires reconstituting the payload via word-stream extraction (which the value-source path does), and a write-through path would need GEP'd writeback at scope exit. Pull when needed.
     - [ ] **Shared (heap) enums under ref scrutinee.** Today's via_ptr handler returns `Ok(None)` for `layout.is_shared == true`; the value-source path's heap-pointer branch handles them. Pull when shared-enum mut-ref-scrutinee write-through becomes user-visible.

- [x] **`Slice[T]` borrow-tracking parity with `ref T`.** Ownership-checker extension flagged in `phase-4-interpreter.md` line 17's `[~]` parent entry. Today `Slice[T]` ships at the type level (primitive in `PRELUDE_TYPES`, `Type::Slice { element, mutable }`, coercion at call boundaries, `.as_slice()` / `.as_slice_mut()`, range-indexing typing, `Copy` / non-`Copy` status) but the ownership checker does not treat slice creation as a borrow into the source storage — a slice can outlive its source, the source can be moved while a slice into it is live, and a `mut Slice[T]` can coexist with other borrows of overlapping bytes. Observable behavior is masked at v1 because the interpreter clones `Value::Array` (phase-4 line 25), but real codegen will surface every miscompile.

  Decomposed:
  1. [x] **Borrow source attribution.** Extend the existing `ref T` borrow-source machinery in `src/ownership.rs` to recognize slice creation sites: `.as_slice()` / `.as_slice_mut()` calls, range-indexing `v[a..b]`, and implicit `Vec` / `Array` / `Slice` → `Slice` coercion at call-argument, return, and **let-binding-rhs** positions (the existing `types_compatible_for_slice` engine fires uniformly across all three coercion sites). Each slice value carries `(borrow_source: PlaceExpr, mutable: bool)` where `borrow_source` is **always resolved to the root binding** at slice-creation time — for slice-of-slice (`let s2 = s1[0..3];`), `s2.borrow_source` is the original `v` that `s1` was sliced from, not `s1` itself. Conflict detection runs O(1) lookups against the root; diagnostic emission walks the chain only when emitting an error (rare path, no per-check cost). Slices into temporary expressions (`func().as_slice()` where `func()` returns a fresh `Vec`) are **rejected at v1** if the slice escapes the enclosing statement — temp-lifetime-extension is post-v1 polish. **Foundation slice — sub-item 2 consumes this representation.**

- [->] <a id="slice-disjoint-range-conflict-deferred"></a>**Slice borrow-tracking polish (a) — disjoint-range conflict analysis.** The conflict matrix at `src/ownership.rs::push_active_borrow` does not consult range bounds when classifying two slice borrows on the same source root. The over-approximation is latent at v1 because shape A ("imm + mut on same root") and shape B ("two mut on same root") both require a mut slice, and v1 range indexing only produces immutable slices — so the example `v[0..3]` + `v[3..6]` is already accepted today via the matrix's `(false, false) → BorrowConflict::None` rule (`src/ownership.rs:2226`) regardless of overlap. Once a mut-from-range syntax exists, a hypothetical imm `v[0..3]` paired with mut `v[3..6]` would fire shape A even though the windows are disjoint. Coarse over-approximation accepted at v1. **Reopen condition.** A mut-from-range syntax lands (today only immutable range slices exist, so the false-positive is unreachable).

  *Why deferred (2026-05-08, sharpened 2026-05-14).* The precise path would be untestable in v1. v1's `Index { Range }` produces only `Slice[T]` (immutable, see typechecker.rs:9309–9346 where the range-index arm returns `Type::Slice { mutable: false }` unconditionally), and the conflict matrix at `src/ownership.rs:2226` accepts two-imm-on-same-root via `(false, false) → BorrowConflict::None` regardless of overlap. Any "disjoint accepted" test today passes through the coarser `None` shortcut, not through a new interval-overlap analysis — so the precise implementation cannot be distinguished from a broken one by the test surface. Shipping now produces code whose tests prove nothing. The natural moment to land the precise analysis is the same PR that introduces mut-Slice-from-range syntax or tightens shape A, because that PR is the first one that can write a test capable of distinguishing the two implementations.

  *Pull-signal trigger.* Either: (i) introduction of mut-Slice-from-range syntax (which would make the disjoint-window imm+mut pair reachable in user code), OR (ii) a tightening of shape A so that overlap analysis becomes the gating criterion rather than same-root identity — at which point disjoint windows must be classifiable as non-conflicting to avoid regressing programs that the tightening was meant to accept.

  *What unblocks (~30 lines + 2-3 tests).* Extend `Projection::Range` to a richer variant carrying optional literal bounds — `LiteralRange { start: Option<i64>, end: Option<i64>, inclusive: bool }`. At `place_expr_root`'s Index arm, extract bounds via an `extract_int_literal` helper and emit `LiteralRange` when both sides are absent or literal; fall through to the existing `Range` (unknown) variant when either side is a non-literal expression. In the conflict matrix, when both prior and new have a single-`LiteralRange` projection on the same root, compute interval overlap; skip conflict if disjoint, fall through to existing behavior otherwise. Tests: `disjoint_range_slices_accepted`, `overlapping_range_slices_rejected`, `dynamic_range_bound_falls_back_to_conservative_conflict`.

- [->] <a id="slice-persistent-ref-binding-cross-borrow-deferred"></a>**Slice borrow-tracking polish (d) — persistent ref-binding cross-borrow.** Today's cross-borrow detection covers (i) call-statement-scoped receiver-side push at MethodCall via `method_self_borrow_kind` (with the stdlib-table fallthrough) and (ii) call-statement-scoped arg-side push at Call via `arg_formal_ref_borrow_kind`. Both pushes drop at snapshot-restore, so the borrow's lifetime is exactly the call expression. Persistent ref bindings — `let r = &v;` (theoretical `&` operator), or function-parameter borrows that flow through let-rebinds — would need a longer-lived `ActiveBorrow` push that survives past statement boundaries. **Reopen condition.** Either the `&` operator lands (gives users a way to spell persistent ref bindings) or a user-program shape arises where function-parameter borrow rebinding produces a real false-negative the current scoped pushes miss.

  *Why deferred (2026-05-08).* v1 doesn't expose persistent ref bindings as a user surface. Function-parameter borrows (`fn f(v: ref Vec[i64])`) already work correctly via the call-scoped pushes when the param is consumed by inner method/free-fn calls; the let-rebind form is theoretical (no `&v` / `&mut v` operator in v1 syntax).

  *Pull-signal trigger.* Either: (i) introduction of `&v` / `&mut v` operator syntax that produces a let-bindable ref, OR (ii) a real user program where a function-parameter ref binding outlives the call it was passed into and a sibling slice borrow on the same root needs to fire cross-borrow.

  *What unblocks (~40 lines + 2-3 tests).* Extend the `StmtKind::Let` arm to push a persistent `ActiveBorrow { kind: ImmRef | MutRef, source, span, scope_depth }` when the binding's resolved type is `Type::Ref(_)` / `Type::MutRef(_)`. The borrow's `scope_depth` matches the binding's declaration scope; the existing `drain_borrows_at_depth` cleanup already handles drop at scope-exit. Conflict matrix already routes slice + ref cross-form via `BorrowConflict::CrossForm` → `CrossBorrowConflict`; no matrix changes needed. Tests: `let_bound_ref_persists_across_statements`, `slice_then_let_bound_ref_rejected_cross_borrow`, `let_bound_ref_drops_at_scope_exit`.

- [x] **`unsafe extern { }` blocks + `#[unsafe(...)]` linker-attribute wrapping — closed 2026-05-15.** **v2 unsafe-track epic** — bundled with the `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` rule entry below and `MaybeUninit[T]` (further below) as three v2 features sharing the same `unsafe`-keyword infrastructure investment; downstream consumer of the bundle is `get_unchecked` at [`phase-7-codegen.md`](phase-7-codegen.md) line 438 (P2 v2, downgraded 2026-05-10). Slice 1 (AST + parser foundation) shipped 2026-05-14; slice 1a (opaque foreign types) shipped 2026-05-14; slice 1b (use-site precision diagnostics) shipped 2026-05-14; layout introspection intrinsic family shipped 2026-05-14; slice 2 (`#[unsafe(...)]` attribute wrapping) shipped 2026-05-15; slice 3 (resolver block-scope semantics confirmation) shipped 2026-05-15; slice 4 (effect-check passthrough confirmation) shipped 2026-05-15; slice 5a (`undocumented_unsafe` block-level lint) shipped 2026-05-15; slice 5b (doc-renderer block-level prose surface — inlined per-child) shipped 2026-05-15. Implements the spec in `design.md § FFI > unsafe extern { ... } block requirement` and `design.md § Linker Control Attributes`.

  **Slice 1 — AST + parser foundation (shipped 2026-05-14).**
  - [x] **New AST nodes** in `src/ast.rs`: `ExternBlock { span, attributes, doc_comment, abi, items }` and `ExternItem::Function(ExternFunction)`; `Item::ExternBlock(ExternBlock)` added alongside the now-dead `Item::ExternFunction` variant. `ExternItem::OpaqueType` (CN-8 forward-decl `type Name;` form) intentionally deferred — falls under a future sub-slice when an actual opaque-FFI consumer arrives.
  - [x] **Parser** at `src/parser.rs`: `parse_item` dispatch handles `Token::Unsafe` → `parse_unsafe_extern_block`, and the existing `Token::Extern` arm now emits a focused diagnostic (`bare extern "ABI" ... is not allowed at module scope. Foreign-import declarations must live inside an unsafe extern "ABI" { ... } block ...`). `parse_unsafe_extern_block` consumes `unsafe extern "ABI" { ... }`, parses each child via `parse_extern_block_item_fn` (the `extern`/`abi` keywords are now block-scoped, so per-item parsing reads `[attrs] [pub] fn name(...) -> T effects;` only), and rejects block-level `pub`/`private` with a focused diagnostic. The old `parse_extern_function` is removed. Recovery on the rejected bare form swallows tokens up to the closing `;` or balanced `{ }` so the error does not cascade.
  - [x] **Block-level attribute storage.** Block-level attributes (`@noblock unsafe extern "C" { ... }`) live on `ExternBlock.attributes` and are NOT pre-merged into per-item `attributes` — see line 299 below. Downstream phases (effectchecker `register_extern_function_effects`, codegen `declare_one_extern_function`) take `block_attrs: &[Attribute]` explicitly and union them with per-item attrs at the point of use; block-level `@noblock` and per-item `@noblock` still produce identical downstream behaviour, but the formatter can now round-trip the authored position faithfully.
  - [x] **Downstream walks.** `Item::ExternBlock(b)` arms added (or extended) in `src/resolver.rs` (collect + resolve), `src/typechecker.rs` (env-add, visibility lookup, public-export visibility check, baked-stdlib pattern), `src/effectchecker.rs` (extracted `register_extern_function_effects` helper called per child), `src/codegen.rs` (`declare_extern_functions` flat-walks both shapes via `declare_one_extern_function`), `src/ffi_lint.rs` (`collect_ffi_float_fns` walks both), `src/module.rs` (`module_defines_local_item` + cross-module visibility lookup), `src/span_visitor.rs`, `src/repl.rs` (`item_name` returns `None` since the block has no single shadowable identifier; `item_span` returns the block span), `src/formatter.rs` (new `format_extern_block` renders the block form; per-item formatter omits the `extern "ABI"` prefix since it lives on the block), `src/doc.rs` (`documentables()` flattener expands each `Item::ExternBlock` into per-child `Documentable::ExternBlockChild` views so foreign-import `///` prose still surfaces — per-child regression closed 2026-05-14).
  - [x] **Test surface.** Parser tests in `tests/parser.rs`: `test_extern_function` (single item, ABI / params / effects round-trip through the block), `test_extern_function_accepts_pub_and_attributes` (per-item `pub` + `#[link_name]` inside block), `test_unsafe_extern_block_multiple_items` (three sibling fns), `test_unsafe_extern_block_keeps_block_level_attribute_separate` (block-level `@noblock` lives on `ExternBlock.attributes`, not pre-merged), `test_unsafe_extern_block_per_item_attribute_stays_per_item` (symmetric: per-item attrs don't bubble to the block), `test_unsafe_extern_block_round_trips_block_level_attribute_position` (round-trip idempotence — line 299 fix), `test_bare_extern_fn_at_module_scope_rejected` (focused diagnostic mentions `unsafe extern`), `test_bare_extern_block_no_unsafe_rejected` (block without `unsafe` prefix rejected), `test_unsafe_at_module_scope_without_extern_rejected` (`unsafe fn ...` at module scope rejected with `expected extern after unsafe`). All existing extern fixtures across `tests/effectchecker.rs`, `tests/typechecker.rs`, `tests/resolver.rs`, `tests/ffi_lint.rs`, `tests/lexer.rs`, `tests/parser.rs`, and `tests/snapshots/profile_extern_heap.kara` migrated to the new block shape (mechanical wrap; `@noblock` retained at item-level inside the block for tests that exercised the per-item form).

  **Slice 1 caveats — punted to subsequent slices.**
  - [x] **`ExternItem::OpaqueType` (CN-8 forward-decl `type Name;`) — slice 1a shipped 2026-05-14.** Pulled pre-consumer. AST: `ExternItem::OpaqueType(OpaqueTypeDecl)` variant alongside `ExternItem::Function(Box<ExternFunction>)` (Function boxed to keep enum compact under `clippy::large_enum_variant`); `OpaqueTypeDecl { span, attributes, doc_comment, is_pub, is_private, name }` with `impl_vis!` for visibility threading. Parser: `parse_unsafe_extern_block` now reads the per-item preamble (doc + attrs + visibility) then dispatches on `Token::Fn` vs `Token::Type` to `parse_extern_block_item_fn` / `parse_extern_block_item_opaque_type`; the dispatcher emits a focused diagnostic for any other item kind. The opaque-type parser rejects generics (`type Foo[T];` → "cannot be generic — declare a wrapper type") and body (`type Foo { x: i32 }` → "no body — use `#[repr(C)] struct` if the C side publishes the layout") and requires the trailing `;`. CN-1 + CN-8 enforcement: Kāra-side identifier must be Type-class (PascalCase); `#[kara_name = "..."]` rebinds a non-conforming foreign symbol (mirrors the existing extern-fn `kara_name` escape). Downstream walks (resolver collect/resolve, typechecker env-add + visibility check, codegen `declare_extern_functions`, effectchecker, ffi_lint, span_visitor, formatter, doc.rs `documentables()` flattener with new `ItemKind::ExternOpaqueType` tag and `Documentable::ExternBlockOpaqueType` view, module `module_defines_local_item` + cross-module visibility lookup) all thread the new variant. Resolver registers the name as `SymbolKind::OpaqueForeignType` (new SymbolKind variant). Typechecker registers the name in the new `TypeEnv.opaque_foreign_types: HashSet<String>` via `env_add_opaque_foreign_type` so downstream type-resolution sees the name as known (not an unknown-symbol error). Test surface in `tests/parser.rs` (9 new: parses, pub+doc+attrs, mixed fn/type, kara_name escape, generics rejected, body rejected, missing-semicolon rejected, invalid item kind rejected, non-PascalCase rejected), `tests/resolver.rs` (2: name collected, duplicate rejected), `tests/typechecker.rs` (2: declaration typechecks, mixed-shape block typechecks).
  - [x] **`ExternItem::OpaqueType` slice 1b — use-site precision diagnostics shipped 2026-05-14.** Pulled pre-consumer (mirrors slice 1a). Three of the four design-spec codes ship; the fourth has a sub-deferral below. **Implementation.** Single recursive walker baked into `lower_type_expr`: the public method now wraps `lower_type_expr_inner(ty, scope, parent_is_ref: bool)`, which threads `parent_is_ref = true` when descending through `TypeKind::Ref` / `TypeKind::MutRef` and `false` everywhere else (`Tuple`, `Array`, `MutSlice`, `Pointer`, `FnType`, `Weak`, generic args of `Path`). At the `TypeKind::Path` leaf, when the resolved name is in `TypeEnv.opaque_foreign_types` and `!parent_is_ref`, it emits `error[E_OPAQUE_TYPE_REQUIRES_INDIRECTION]` against `ty.span`. `Vec[Foo]` (Foo by-value inside Vec) and `ref Vec[Foo]` (Foo still by-value inside Vec) both fire correctly because `lower_path_type` → `lower_generic_args_named` → `lower_type_expr` (the wrapper) resets `parent_is_ref` to `false` for generic args. `infer_field_access` adds an early-return arm: a receiver of `ref Foo` / `mut ref Foo` (or bare `Foo` defensively) where Foo is opaque emits `E_OPAQUE_TYPE_NO_FIELDS` and returns `Type::Error`. `env_add_impl` adds a pre-lowering check on `imp.target_type.kind` — when the target's single-segment name is opaque, it emits `E_OPAQUE_TYPE_NO_INHERENT_OR_TRAIT_IMPLS` (distinguishing trait vs inherent in the message via `imp.trait_name`), bails before `add_impl`, and `check_impl_block` early-returns silently for the same target so the user sees one focused diagnostic without method-body cascade noise. Test surface in `tests/typechecker.rs`: 12 new tests covering each by-value position (fn param, fn return, let binding, struct field, enum payload, generic arg, tuple), the two positive controls (`ref Foo` and `mut ref Foo` accepted), the field-access-through-deref case, and inherent + trait impl rejections.
  - [x] **Layout introspection intrinsic family shipped 2026-05-14.** `size_of[T]()`, `align_of[T]()`, `offset_of[T](field.path)` from `design.md § Field Offsets` all ship together. Resolves the slice-1b `E_OPAQUE_TYPE_NO_KNOWN_SIZE` sub-deferral. **Stdlib.** `runtime/stdlib/intrinsics.kara` declares `size_of[T]()` / `align_of[T]()` as `#[compiler_builtin]` placeholder fns; both names also added to `PRELUDE_FUNCTIONS` so the resolver accepts the bareword. **Typechecker.** `infer_layout_query_intrinsic` (size_of/align_of) and `infer_offset_of` (offset_of) handle the call sites; both lower the type argument with `parent_is_ref = true` so the slice-1b walker doesn't fire `E_OPAQUE_TYPE_REQUIRES_INDIRECTION` (the "wrap in `ref T`" hint would mis-direct a layout query). `size_of`/`align_of` emit `E_OPAQUE_TYPE_NO_KNOWN_SIZE` for opaque T; `offset_of` emits `E_OFFSET_OF_OPAQUE_TYPE` (per design.md line 5693), `E_OFFSET_OF_GENERIC_PARAM`, `E_OFFSET_OF_UNKNOWN_FIELD`, `E_OFFSET_OF_NON_STRUCT_TARGET`, `E_OFFSET_OF_INVALID_PATH` for the documented failure modes; private-field cross-module check piggybacks on the existing `check_cross_module_field_access`. **Parser.** `size_of`/`align_of` reuse the existing generic-call shape (`Path { generic_args }` for multi-arg, `Index { Ident, T }` for single-arg recovered via `expr_as_type_expr`). `offset_of` is a true contextual special form: `parse_identifier_expr` dispatches `Identifier("offset_of") + LeftBracket` to `parse_offset_of_special_form`, which parses `[TYPE](IDENT (.IDENT)*)` and emits the new `ExprKind::OffsetOf { ty, field_path }` AST node. Field-path validator rejects indexing / calls / dereferences with `E_OFFSET_OF_INVALID_PATH` at parse time. **Codegen.** `compile_layout_query_intrinsic` lowers `size_of` via inkwell's `BasicTypeEnum::size_of()` (compile-time const), `align_of` via `TargetData::get_abi_alignment()`. `compile_offset_of` chains `TargetData::offset_of_element(struct_type, idx)` across nested-path segments using `struct_field_names` + `struct_field_type_names`. `TargetData` is lazily built on first use via `ensure_target_data` (one-time `Target::initialize_native` + `create_target_machine().get_target_data()` cost; cached in a new `Codegen.target_data: Option<TargetData>` field). **Plumbing.** `ExprKind::OffsetOf` arms added across resolver, span_visitor, formatter (renders as `offset_of[T](path.segments)`), interpreter free-ident walker, lowering, ownership, concurrency, effectchecker, ffi_lint, logical_lint, unsafe_lint, cost_summary, typechecker capture-walk — all no-ops since the intrinsic is a compile-time constant with no captures, reads, or effects. **Test surface.** `tests/typechecker.rs`: 16 new tests (size_of/align_of: returns usize for primitives + user struct, opaque rejection × 2, value-arg rejection; offset_of: returns usize, first/nested field, unknown field, opaque target, non-struct target, walk-into-non-struct, indexing/call rejection at parse). `tests/codegen.rs`: 10 new E2E tests verifying actual emitted constants (size_of i64=8, i32=4, i8=1, Point=16; align_of i64=8, i32=4, i8=1; offset_of first=0, second=8, nested=8). The `container_of[T, F]` stdlib helper (also in design.md § Field Offsets) is deferred — it requires raw-pointer surface syntax (`*const T` / `*mut T`) which is itself the slice-3 predecessor for `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` below.
  - [ ] **`container_of[T, F]` stdlib helper (carry forward).** Deferred until raw-pointer surface syntax (`*const T` / `*mut T`) lands. Per design.md § Field Offsets, lowers to `field_ptr.with_addr(field_ptr.addr() - offset_of[T](field))` using pointer-provenance methods (`addr` / `with_addr` from `design.md § Pointer Provenance`). The `field` argument shares the same path-validator shipped above. Both raw-pointer surface and pointer-provenance methods need to ship before this helper has anything to lower against; it lands naturally with the raw-pointer slice (line 296 below).
  - [ ] **Raw-pointer surface syntax interaction (carry forward).** When `*const Foo` / `*mut Foo` syntax lands as the slice-3 predecessor for `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` (below), extend the indirection walker so descending through `TypeKind::Pointer` flips `parent_is_ref = true` (raw pointers are sized regardless of element type, just like references). Without this extension, `*const Foo` would incorrectly fire `REQUIRES_INDIRECTION` once raw-pointer parser surface exists. Today the test surface for raw pointers doesn't exist, so no regression risk — the walker conservatively rejects `Pointer { inner: Path(opaque) }` until that slice lands.
  - [x] **Per-child doc generator regression closed (2026-05-14).** `src/doc.rs` now expands every `Item::ExternBlock` into per-child `Documentable::ExternBlockChild` views via the new `documentables()` flattener. Each documented foreign-import declaration emits its own page exactly like the pre-block standalone form did (kind tag `extern fn`, signature `extern "ABI" fn name`, doc-comment markdown rendered, cross-references via `[name]` resolve through the link table). Test surface in `tests/doc.rs`: `doc_emits_html_for_extern_block_child_function`, `doc_emits_per_child_pages_for_multi_item_extern_block`, `doc_resolves_cross_reference_to_extern_block_child`. The block-level `///` prose surface (the `# Safety` carrier read by `undocumented_unsafe`) is still pending and lands with slice 5 — that surface needs a block-level doc page distinct from the per-child pages.
  - [x] **Formatter round-trip idempotence on block-level attributes shipped 2026-05-15.** Block-level attributes are no longer pre-merged into each child at parse time; they live on `ExternBlock.attributes` and are rendered by the formatter at the block-header position. Downstream consumers that need the effective union (effectchecker `register_extern_function_effects`, codegen `declare_one_extern_function`) take `block_attrs: &[Attribute]` as an explicit second parameter, called from the per-item walk inside the `Item::ExternBlock` arm with `&b.attributes`. The dead `Item::ExternFunction` arm passes `&[]`. Test surface: `test_unsafe_extern_block_round_trips_block_level_attribute_position` pins `#[noblock]\nunsafe extern "C" { ... }` formatting to itself; `test_unsafe_extern_block_keeps_block_level_attribute_separate` and `test_unsafe_extern_block_per_item_attribute_stays_per_item` pin the AST shape on each side.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — `#[unsafe(no_mangle)]` and `#[unsafe(link_section("..."))]` attribute wrapping shipped 2026-05-15.** Parser recognises the wrap (`parse_unsafe_wrapped_attribute` in `src/parser.rs`, dispatched from `parse_attribute` when the inner token is `Token::Unsafe`) and unwraps to a plain `Attribute { name: "no_mangle" | "link_section", string_value }` so existing downstream consumers (`apply_linker_attrs` in `src/codegen.rs`) keep working unchanged. Bare `#[no_mangle]` and `#[link_section(...)]` are rejected at parse time with a focused diagnostic that quotes the canonical wrapped form. `#[unsafe(NAME)]` with any other `NAME` (e.g. `#[unsafe(used)]`) is rejected with a focused diagnostic naming the legal wrapped attributes — `used` stays plain (no soundness obligation, only DCE suppression). `#[noblock]` and `#[kara_name = "..."]` stay plain. The formatter (`format_attributes` in `src/formatter.rs`) re-emits the wrap when rendering `name == "no_mangle" | "link_section"` so authoring round-trips faithfully. **Test surface** in `tests/parser.rs`: `test_unsafe_no_mangle_wrap_parses`, `test_unsafe_link_section_wrap_parses`, `test_bare_no_mangle_rejected_with_focused_diagnostic`, `test_bare_link_section_rejected_with_focused_diagnostic`, `test_unsafe_wrap_unknown_inner_attribute_rejected`, `test_used_attribute_stays_plain`, `test_unsafe_no_mangle_round_trips_through_formatter`, `test_unsafe_link_section_round_trips_through_formatter`. Pre-existing fixtures using bare forms (`tests/parser.rs::test_doc_comment_before_attribute_works`, `tests/codegen.rs::test_ir_no_mangle_symbol_name_unchanged`, `tests/codegen.rs::test_ir_link_section_sets_function_section`) migrated to the wrap.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — Resolver block-scope semantics shipped 2026-05-15.** Confirmed-in-code: the `Item::ExternBlock` arms in `src/resolver.rs::collect_module_scope_names` (line ~542), the collection pass (line ~772), and `resolve_items` (line ~1583) all flat-walk the block's children, calling the same `collect_extern_function` / `collect_opaque_foreign_type` / `resolve_extern_function` entrypoints that a top-level item would. No `push_scope` / `pop_scope` wraps the block, no namespace prefix, no separate symbol-table region — `self.table.define(name, ...)` is invoked at module scope for each child, so duplicate-definition fires uniformly across module-scope items, sibling items in the same block, and items split across separate blocks. The block is purely a syntactic + trust-boundary marker. **Test surface** in `tests/resolver.rs`: `test_unsafe_extern_block_function_visible_at_module_scope` (sibling top-level fn calls extern fn by bareword — no block-qualified path), `test_unsafe_extern_block_function_collides_with_top_level_function` (module-scope `fn write` + extern `fn write` → duplicate-definition), `test_unsafe_extern_block_function_collides_across_separate_blocks` (two `unsafe extern { }` blocks both declaring `fn read` → duplicate-definition; block boundaries don't shield), `test_unsafe_extern_block_resolves_type_reference_against_module_scope` (extern fn signature references a module-scope `struct Buf` via `ref Buf` — confirms the block does not introduce a fresh type namespace).

  - [x] **Slice 4 — Effect-checker passthrough confirmation shipped 2026-05-15.** No behaviour change was required; the trust-not-verify rule already applied to every item inside the block (slice 1's fixture migration moved `tests/effectchecker.rs` cases end-to-end onto the block shape) and slice 2's `register_extern_function_effects(e, block_attrs: &[Attribute])` signature already unions block-level + per-item attributes when computing ABI-default suppression (`src/effectchecker.rs:3337-3338`). Slice 4 closes the confirmation with three focused tests in `tests/effectchecker.rs`: `test_block_level_noblock_propagates_to_every_child_extern_c` (block-level `@noblock` suppresses the `extern "C"` blocks default on every child), `test_per_item_noblock_does_not_leak_to_sibling` (negative — per-item `@noblock` on one item must not bubble to the block or to its sibling, which still gets the ABI default), `test_block_level_noblock_on_c_unwind_keeps_panics_on_every_child` (block-level `@noblock` on `C-unwind` suppresses blocks but preserves panics on every child — the same per-item rule applied uniformly).

  - [x] **Slice 5a — `undocumented_unsafe` lint extension shipped 2026-05-15.** Block-level lint surface for `unsafe extern "ABI" { ... }`. The lint now has two carriers sharing one diagnostic name: the existing preceding-`// Safety:`-line check for expression-form `unsafe { }`, and a new `# Safety` markdown-section check on `ExternBlock.doc_comment` for the declaration form. **Implementation** in `src/unsafe_lint.rs`: `check_undocumented_unsafe` dispatches `Item::ExternBlock` ahead of the function arm, reading `#[allow(undocumented_unsafe)]` / `#[deny(undocumented_unsafe)]` off the block's own `attributes` (the same `has_lint_attr` helper used for function-level suppression — no new attribute surface). `check_extern_block_safety_doc` consults `block.doc_comment` via `doc_has_safety_section`, which walks the (lexer-stripped) doc lines and matches any markdown header whose visible text begins with "Safety" (case-insensitive; accepts `# Safety`, `## Safety`, `# Safety considerations`, etc., so rustdoc-style nesting works). The diagnostic points at `block.span` and reads `"unsafe extern block is missing a `# Safety` doc-comment section explaining the trust contract for its imports"`. The CLI path in `src/cli.rs:2028` already iterates `check_undocumented_unsafe` output and emits warning/error lines, so the new diagnostic surfaces automatically. **Test surface** in `tests/unsafe_lint.rs`: 8 new tests — `test_unsafe_extern_block_with_safety_doc_passes` (positive, `# Safety` heading + body), `test_unsafe_extern_block_without_doc_warns` (no doc-comment at all → warning, message mentions `# Safety`), `test_unsafe_extern_block_with_unrelated_doc_warns` (doc present but no Safety section), `test_safety_doc_section_is_case_insensitive` (`# safety` accepted), `test_safety_doc_section_accepts_higher_header_levels` (`## Safety` accepted), `test_unsafe_extern_block_allow_attribute_suppresses` (block-level `#[allow]` silences), `test_unsafe_extern_block_deny_attribute_promotes_to_error` (block-level `#[deny]` promotes to error), `test_multiple_unsafe_extern_blocks_each_checked_independently` (negative — Safety doc on one block does not cover a sibling block).

  - [x] **Slice 5b — Doc-generator block-level prose surface shipped 2026-05-15.** Ships the renderer side of the shared carrier: block-level `///` prose (including the `# Safety` section the 5a lint enforces) now surfaces in `karac doc`. **Design deviation from the scoped plan.** The original scope (recorded when slice 5 was split into 5a/5b earlier this session) called for a sibling block-level *page* hosting the prose, with three open questions (page naming on ABI collision, link-table key, sidebar entry shape). Shipped instead: **inline the block-level prose on each child's page**, prepending it to the child's own prose. This is a strictly better surface — it resolves all three open questions trivially (no new page = no naming / link-key / sidebar concerns), puts the safety contract right where users land (each imported symbol's own page), and keeps the carrier story honest (one field, two consumers, no new addressing surface). **Implementation.** `Documentable::ExternBlockChild` and `ExternBlockOpaqueType` variants in `src/doc.rs` now carry a `block_doc: Option<&'a str>` field threaded from `ExternBlock.doc_comment` by `documentables()`. `documentable_doc` returns `Option<Cow<'_, str>>`: when only one of block-doc / own-doc exists it borrows; when both exist it returns an owned `format!("{block}\n\n{own}")` so the two prose blocks render as a single markdown body. The two call sites (`build_docs` index pass at `src/doc.rs:115`, render pass at `src/doc.rs:150`) take `&doc` to deref the Cow into `&str` for `summarize_doc` and `render_item_page_with_links`. Page-generation gate widens correspondingly — a child page is now written iff its effective doc is `Some`, so a documented block with undocumented children still emits a page per import (the safety contract reaches every imported symbol). **Test surface** in `tests/doc.rs`: `doc_inlines_block_level_doc_on_each_child_page` (positive: child's own prose + block-level `# Safety` both visible on `strlen.html`), `doc_block_level_doc_alone_still_generates_child_page` (block-only prose still produces a child page, contract is reachable). Existing tests unchanged: `doc_emits_per_child_pages_for_multi_item_extern_block` still expects `undocumented_helper.html` to NOT exist — passes because that fixture's block has no doc-comment either, so the effective doc is None for the undocumented child. **Carry-forward.** None — the slice is complete. If a future workload needs a dedicated block-level URL (e.g., a sidebar grouping like `unsafe extern "C" { ... }` as a parent node listing its children), the three design questions can be tackled in a fresh slice; the inline surface ships today against the actual user need (read the safety contract).

  Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). All slices complete (1, 1a, 1b + layout intrinsics, 2, 3, 4, 5a, 5b) as of 2026-05-15; the `unsafe extern { }` hardening epic is closed.

- [x] **`unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` rule — body of `unsafe fn` is not an implicit `unsafe { }` block.** **v2 unsafe-track epic — central infrastructure piece.** This entry is the predecessor that unblocks three downstream features: `get_unchecked` at [`phase-7-codegen.md`](phase-7-codegen.md) line 438 (P2 v2, downgraded 2026-05-10), `MaybeUninit[T]` (further below in this file), and the `unsafe extern { }` hardening (above in this file). One infrastructure investment, three unlocks — that's the natural shape of the v2 epic. Slice 1 (AST + parser foundation) shipped 2026-05-14; slices 2-5 (resolver/typechecker passthrough confirmation, the actual lint pass, diagnostic shape, the no-`#[allow]` policy) carry forward. Implement the spec in `design.md § Unsafe Escape Hatch > unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn rule`.

  **Slice 1 — AST + parser foundation (shipped 2026-05-14).**
  - [x] **`is_unsafe: bool` field on `Function`** at `src/ast.rs`. Captures the `unsafe` keyword on a fn declaration as a precondition the function asserts callers must satisfy. Crucially, the field is consumed by the slice-3 lint that walks every fn body uniformly — `is_unsafe == true` is NOT a sentinel that suppresses the check inside the body. Doc-comment on the field spells out the design intent so future readers don't conflate the two roles of `unsafe`.
  - [x] **Module-scope `Token::Unsafe` dispatch** at `src/parser.rs::parse_item`. The earlier slice (FFI `unsafe extern { }` hardening) locked `unsafe` at module scope to the block-parser path. Slice 1 generalises this: `Token::Unsafe` peeks one token ahead and dispatches: `Token::Extern` → `parse_unsafe_extern_block` (existing); `Token::Fn` → consume `unsafe` and forward `is_unsafe = true` into `parse_function`; anything else → focused diagnostic `"expected `extern` or `fn` after `unsafe` at module scope"`.
  - [x] **`parse_function` signature extension.** Takes a new `is_unsafe: bool` parameter threaded through to the `Function { ... }` constructor. All four existing callers backfilled: the plain `Token::Fn` arm (`false`), the `Token::Unsafe` → fn branch (`true`), the impl-block method parser (`false`; impl-method `unsafe fn` is carry-forward), and the four downstream `Function { ... }` synthesis sites in `src/effectchecker.rs`, `src/typechecker.rs`, and `src/prelude.rs` (each `is_unsafe: false` — they synthesise stubs from trait-method declarations or stdlib placeholders that don't carry user-asserted `unsafe`).
  - [x] **Tests** at `tests/parser.rs`. `test_unsafe_fn_parses_and_records_is_unsafe` (smoke), `test_plain_fn_has_is_unsafe_false` (regression-pin), `test_unsafe_fn_pub_attributes_effects_roundtrip` (composes with `pub` + doc-comment + `#[noblock]` + params + return type + effect list), `test_unsafe_followed_by_invalid_token_at_module_scope_rejected` (`unsafe struct Foo {}` → focused diagnostic). The earlier slice-1 (`unsafe extern { }`) test `test_unsafe_at_module_scope_without_extern_rejected` (which previously asserted `unsafe fn foo() {}` was rejected at parse time) replaced by the positive tests above — `unsafe fn` is now legal.

  **Slice 1 caveats — shipped 2026-05-15.**
  - [x] **Impl-method `unsafe fn` shipped 2026-05-15.** The impl-block body loop in `parse_impl_block` (`src/parser.rs:1240-1273`) now mirrors the module-scope dispatch: after consuming optional `pub` / `private`, it peeks for `Token::Unsafe` and, if followed by `Token::Fn`, consumes `unsafe` and threads `is_unsafe = true` into `parse_function`. `unsafe` followed by anything else in an impl body emits a focused diagnostic (`"expected `fn` after `unsafe` in impl block — `unsafe` may only prefix an `unsafe fn` method declaration here."`). The `is_unsafe` field on `Function` already exists from slice 1, so no AST change was needed. **Test surface** in `tests/parser.rs`: `test_impl_method_unsafe_fn_parses_and_records_is_unsafe` (positive — `unsafe fn` and plain `fn` siblings in one impl block), `test_impl_method_unsafe_fn_with_pub_and_effects_roundtrips` (composition with `pub` + attributes + `reads(Memory)` effect list + body), `test_impl_method_unsafe_followed_by_invalid_token_rejected` (`unsafe type Bad = i64;` inside an impl rejected with the focused diagnostic).
  - [x] **Trait-method `unsafe fn` signatures shipped 2026-05-15.** `TraitMethod` (`src/ast.rs:434`) now carries `is_unsafe: bool` with a doc-comment spelling out the trait-side precondition role (an impl satisfying an `unsafe`-trait-method must itself be `unsafe fn`; call sites against the trait must wrap per `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn`). `parse_trait_def_tail` (`src/parser.rs:1018-1037`) dispatches `Token::Unsafe`/`Token::Fn` lookahead before calling `parse_trait_method`, which now takes `is_unsafe: bool` and writes it onto the constructed node. Diagnostic: `"expected `fn` after `unsafe` in trait body — `unsafe` may only prefix an `unsafe fn` method declaration here."`. Only one `TraitMethod { ... }` construction site exists in the codebase (the parser), so no backfill in `effectchecker.rs` / `typechecker.rs` / `prelude.rs` was needed. **Test surface** in `tests/parser.rs`: `test_trait_method_unsafe_fn_signature_parses_and_records_is_unsafe` (positive — required `unsafe fn` signature with `;` terminator + plain `fn` sibling), `test_trait_method_unsafe_fn_with_default_body_parses` (`unsafe fn` with default body + effects), `test_trait_method_unsafe_followed_by_invalid_token_rejected` (`unsafe type Assoc;` inside a trait rejected with the focused diagnostic).

  - [x] **Slice 2 — Resolver / typechecker passthrough confirmation shipped 2026-05-15.** Confirmed-in-code: `SymbolKind::Function` in `src/resolver.rs` carries no `is_unsafe` field — the resolver erases the declaration-side marker, so name resolution, scope handling, and duplicate-definition detection behave identically for `unsafe fn` and plain `fn`. The typechecker never reads `Function.is_unsafe`; the only `is_unsafe` references outside the parser are synthesis sites in `src/typechecker.rs`, `src/prelude.rs`, and `src/effectchecker.rs` that emit `is_unsafe: false` for synthetic Function nodes (stub bodies from trait method declarations and stdlib placeholders). Slice 2 records the confirmation with 6 focused tests. **Resolver test surface** in `tests/resolver.rs`: `test_unsafe_fn_resolves_at_module_scope_like_plain_fn` (positive — `unsafe fn` registers `SymbolKind::Function` at module scope, indistinguishable from plain `fn`), `test_unsafe_fn_body_resolves_against_module_scope` (positive — body name resolution for module-scope consts and sibling fn calls works identically inside `unsafe fn`), `test_unsafe_fn_collides_with_plain_fn_of_same_name` (negative — `unsafe` marker does not shield names; duplicate-definition fires across an `unsafe fn` and a plain `fn` of the same name). **Typechecker test surface** in `tests/typechecker.rs`: `test_unsafe_fn_with_only_safe_ops_typechecks` (smoke — body of `unsafe fn` performs only arithmetic and typechecks), `test_unsafe_fn_param_and_return_types_typecheck` (composition — `pub unsafe fn` with params, return type, and sibling-fn calls in the body), `test_plain_fn_calling_unsafe_fn_typechecks_at_slice_2` (negative-space pin — typechecker does not gate calls on the callee's `is_unsafe`; the wrap-required lint is slice 3's deliverable, not slice 2's).

  - [x] **Slice 3 — `src/unsafe_lint.rs` extension: the actual operation lint shipped 2026-05-15.** Ships raw-pointer deref + `unsafe fn` call detection — the two predecessor-ready operations from the slice 3 scope. **Typechecker enabling change** in `src/typechecker.rs`: extend `UnaryOp::Deref` to accept `Type::Pointer { inner }` (returning `*inner`); soundness moves to the lint layer, so `*ptr` on a raw pointer typechecks like `*ref` does — the unsafe-op lint is what enforces the wrap. The pre-existing diagnostic on deref of a non-ref / non-ptr is widened to read `'ref T', 'mut ref T', or a raw pointer ('*const T' / '*mut T')` so the error narrates the full accepted set. **Implementation** in `src/unsafe_lint.rs`: new `check_unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn(program, typed: Option<&TypeCheckResult>)` entrypoint. Builds an `UnsafeFnRegistry` once from `program.items` capturing top-level `unsafe fn` names (`Item::Function.is_unsafe`) and `(receiver_type_name, method_name)` pairs for `unsafe fn` impl methods (`Item::ImplBlock` whose target is a single-segment `TypeKind::Path`). Functions declared inside `unsafe extern { }` blocks are intentionally excluded — the trust boundary is the block. The `OpWalker` mirrors the existing AST walker but threads `in_unsafe: bool` through every recursion; entering `ExprKind::Unsafe(block)` flips the context to `true` for the block's contents. Raw-pointer deref detection consults `typed.expr_types` to identify `Type::Pointer { .. }` operands; method-call dispatch reads `typed.method_callee_types` (canonical `"Type.method"` form). Without `typed`, the walker still detects top-level `unsafe fn` calls via the registry. Trait-method dispatch through a generic bound and asm/volatile/union ops are deferred to their respective producer features. **Diagnostic** is a hard error (slice 5 will reject `#[allow(unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn)]`): for raw-ptr deref the message reads `raw-pointer dereference requires an unsafe { ... } block — unsafe fn declares a precondition for callers but does not implicitly wrap its body`; for calls, `call to unsafe fn <name> requires an unsafe { ... } block — the callee declares a precondition the caller must assert` with the registry-resolved name (`raw` for free, `Type.method` for impl). **CLI integration** at `src/cli.rs:2045-2065` registers the new lint immediately after `check_undocumented_unsafe`, taking `pipeline.typed.as_ref()` so the post-typecheck info flows. **Test surface** in `tests/unsafe_lint.rs` (13 new tests): `test_unsafe_fn_call_outside_unsafe_block_errors` (positive — top-level), `test_unsafe_fn_call_inside_unsafe_block_accepted` (negative — wrapped), `test_unsafe_fn_body_still_requires_inner_unsafe_block` (THE KEY SEMANTIC PIN — `unsafe fn` body does NOT implicitly wrap; calling another `unsafe fn` inside still errors), `test_plain_fn_call_does_not_trigger`, `test_extern_fn_call_does_not_trigger` (trust-boundary rule), `test_raw_pointer_deref_outside_unsafe_errors`, `test_raw_pointer_deref_inside_unsafe_accepted`, `test_mut_raw_pointer_deref_outside_unsafe_errors` (symmetric in `*const T` / `*mut T`), `test_ref_deref_does_not_trigger` (negative — `*r` on `ref T` is safe), `test_impl_method_unsafe_fn_call_outside_unsafe_errors` (positive — impl method, registry-resolved name `S.raw_read`), `test_impl_method_unsafe_fn_call_inside_unsafe_accepted`, `test_plain_method_call_does_not_trigger`, `test_unsafe_block_wraps_multiple_ops` (composition — one wrap covers multiple unsafe ops). Slice 4 (diagnostic shape polish) and slice 5 (no-`#[allow]` enforcement) carry forward — slice 3 ships the operation-detection core.

  - [x] **Slice 4 — Diagnostic shape shipped 2026-05-15.** Extends `LintDiagnostic` (`src/unsafe_lint.rs`) with `help: Option<String>` and `note: Option<String>` fields so the rustc-style three-piece shape (primary / `= note:` / `= help:`) can be carried as structured data rather than wedged into one message string. The two `undocumented_unsafe` construction sites keep `help: None` / `note: None` — slice 4 is scoped to the three `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` diagnostics; the older lint's polish pass remains future work. **Diagnostic rewrite** at the raw-pointer-deref / top-level-unsafe-fn-call / impl-method-unsafe-fn-call sites: primary message tightened to point at the offending operation and the rule (`"raw-pointer dereference must be wrapped in an `unsafe { ... }` block"`, `"call to `unsafe fn {name}` must be wrapped in an `unsafe { ... }` block"`, `"call to `unsafe fn {recv}.{m}` must be wrapped in an `unsafe { ... }` block"`). The actionable hint moves into `help`: wrap-in-`unsafe { ... }` + add `// Safety: ...` comment per the `undocumented_unsafe` lint, naming the specific operation (`pointer is valid`, `` `name`'s preconditions are satisfied``, `` `recv.m`'s preconditions are satisfied``) so the Safety: comment author knows which precondition set they are asserting. The conceptual disambiguation moves into `note` as a single shared constant `UNSAFE_TWO_ROLES_NOTE` (factored to avoid repetition across the three sites): explains that `unsafe` plays two distinct roles — on a function declaration it specifies a precondition the *caller* must uphold, and on a block it is the *implementer*'s trust assertion that the operation's preconditions hold here — and pins the consequence (`unsafe fn` does *not* implicitly wrap its body). The two-role conflation is the most common newcomer mistake the rule is designed to surface, so the note ships in the same diagnostic rather than as separate documentation. **CLI rendering** at `src/cli.rs`: factored out as `render_unsafe_lint_diag(diag, filename)` (replacing two duplicate inline `eprintln!` blocks for the two passes); renders primary line followed by `   = note: ...` then `   = help: ...` continuation lines when present, matching rustc's diagnostic shape. **Test surface** in `tests/unsafe_lint.rs`: helper `assert_diag_has_slice4_shape(diag, target_substring_in_help)` checks that `help` contains the wrap-in-`unsafe`, `// Safety:`, and `undocumented_unsafe` references plus the operation-specific needle; checks that `note` contains both ``unsafe fn`` and ``unsafe { ... }`` references, the caller's role, and the "does not implicitly wrap" rule-pin. Three new tests (`test_raw_pointer_deref_diagnostic_has_slice4_shape`, `test_unsafe_fn_call_diagnostic_has_slice4_shape`, `test_unsafe_method_call_diagnostic_has_slice4_shape`) — one per operation kind — pin the primary message + apply the shape helper. A fourth test `test_undocumented_unsafe_diags_have_no_help_or_note` pins the scoping decision that the older lint's diagnostics remain single-line until its own polish pass lands. The 13 pre-existing slice 3 tests continue to pass: their assertions use `message.contains(...)` against substrings (`"raw-pointer dereference"`, ``"call to `unsafe fn raw`"``, ``"call to `unsafe fn S.raw_read`"``) that are still present in the tightened primary message.

  - [x] **Slice 5 — No `#[allow]` opt-out shipped 2026-05-15.** Rejects `#[allow(unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn)]` at the attribute parser. **Implementation** in `src/parser.rs::parse_attribute` (immediately after the closing `]` of the attribute and before the `Attribute { ... }` is constructed): when `name == "allow"`, scan the parsed `args` and reject if any arg matches the rule name in either surface form — positional (`#[allow(unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn)]`, the form a user would actually write) or named (`#[allow(name = unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn)]`, theoretical only — mirrors the detection shape used by `has_lint_attr` in `src/unsafe_lint.rs`). The reject path calls `self.error(...)` which records the diagnostic without bailing parsing (matching the bare-`#[no_mangle]` rejection pattern at parser.rs:2331-2347), so error recovery remains useful and the rest of the file still type-checks. **Diagnostic** reads `` `#[allow(unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn)]` is not accepted — the `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` rule is a hard error with no opt-out (Kāra is greenfield; there is no migration story). Wrap the offending operation in an `unsafe { ... }` block instead, and add a `// Safety: ...` comment above the block per the `undocumented_unsafe` lint. `` — names the rule, states the no-opt-out policy with its reasoning, and redirects to the actual fix (the slice 4 help line shape). **Scope** is deliberately narrow: only `#[allow]` is rejected on the rule's name. The companion `#[warn]` / `#[deny]` / `#[expect]` lint-level attributes (which Kāra does not yet generally recognise — see the future "Lint level attributes" entry at line 353) are not parser-rejected today. When that broader feature lands it will reject all four uniformly on `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` via `error[E_LINT_LEVEL_ON_HARD_RULE]`; until then a stray `#[deny(unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn)]` parses as a plain (redundant — the rule is already deny-by-default) attribute. **Test surface** in `tests/parser.rs` (5 tests, immediately after the linker-attribute round-trip tests): `test_allow_unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn_rejected_with_focused_diagnostic` (positive — primary form, asserts the diagnostic names the rule, states "hard error", redirects to `unsafe {` and `// Safety:`), `test_allow_unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn_rejected_on_impl_method` (positive — same rejection from the impl-method attribute position; pins the uniform parser surface), `test_allow_other_lints_still_accepted` (negative — `#[allow(undocumented_unsafe)]` still parses cleanly; slice 5 is scoped to the one rule name), `test_allow_with_multiple_lints_including_unsafe_op_rejected` (positive — multi-lint `#[allow(undocumented_unsafe, unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn)]` rejected; exercises the iter-any branch), `test_deny_unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn_still_accepted` (negative-space — `#[deny(...)]` parses today; pins the scoping decision until lint-level-attributes lands). With slice 5 shipped, the `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` epic is complete — all five slices boxed.

  Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). **Consumer:** unblocks the `Slice[T].get_unchecked` / `get_unchecked_mut` escape hatch at [`phase-7-codegen.md` § "`Slice[T].get_unchecked(i)` and `Slice[T].get_unchecked_mut(i)` escape hatch"](phase-7-codegen.md) (currently `**Blocked (2026-05-07).**`); slices (1), (3), and (4) above match the predecessor requirements 1:1 — once those land, the get_unchecked slice becomes additive `infer_slice_method` registration + codegen lowering as drafted.

- [x] **`#[must_use]` mandate — stdlib-wide application + lint enforcement.** Implement the spec in `design.md § \`#[must_use]\` on Types > Mandate for stdlib`. The base `#[must_use]` attribute is already documented; this entry covers the stdlib mandate and the lint that enforces it. All four sub-slices shipped: slice 1 (implicit `#[must_use]` for `Result[T, E]` / `Option[T]`) on 2026-05-15; slice 2 (stdlib `#[must_use]` annotations on `Peekable[T]` / `PooledConnection[T]`), slice 3 (`missing_must_use` stdlib-hygiene lint), and slice 4 (general `#[must_use]` honoring + diagnostic shape) on 2026-05-16. The remaining triage of existing stdlib `pub fn`s with the slice-3-flagged annotations is left as a follow-up sub-thread; slice 4's enforcement plumbing lights up automatically as each annotation lands.

  - [x] **Slice 1 — Implicit `#[must_use]` for `Result[T, E]` and `Option[T]` shipped 2026-05-15.** The two language-level types carry implicit must-use recognition baked into the compiler rather than expressed as a user-visible `#[must_use]` attribute on the prelude `.kara` source (per spec: "bake into the typechecker rather than the attribute parser, since these are language-level types"). **Implementation** as a new lint module `src/must_use_lint.rs` (not directly in the typechecker's error stream, because `TypeCheckResult.errors` is treated as *fatal* by the codegen path — see `src/cli.rs:2992-3001`; a must-use diagnostic emitted there would block compilation rather than warn). The module follows the existing lint-module pattern (`unsafe_lint`, `ffi_lint`, `logical_lint`): public `check_implicit_must_use(program, typed: Option<&TypeCheckResult>) -> Vec<LintDiagnostic>` entrypoint with `LintLevel { Warning, Error }` and `LintDiagnostic { level, span, message, lint_name, help, note }` (carries the slice-4-style `help` / `note` fields from the start so the diagnostic shape matches `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn`'s post-slice-4 form). The walker mirrors `unsafe_lint::OpWalker` structurally — visits free `Item::Function`, `Item::ImplBlock` methods, and `Item::TraitDef` default trait method bodies, descending through all block-bearing expression forms (`Unsafe`, `Block`, `Loop`, `LabeledBlock`, `Seq`, `Par`, `Try`, `Lock`, `Providers`, `If`, `IfLet`, `While`, `WhileLet`, `For`, `Match`, `Closure`, `Defer`, `ErrDefer`, etc.). **Discard-site precision:** the check fires at `StmtKind::Expr` (statement-position expressions whose value flows nowhere), NOT at `block.final_expr` (the block's tail expression flows as the block's value to whatever consumes the block — the enclosing context decides whether the outer value is itself discarded). At a discard site, the walker queries `typed.expr_types[SpanKey::from_span(&expr.span)]` and matches `Type::Named { name, .. }` against `"Result"` and `"Option"` by name (the typechecker already routes these prelude types through this surface — see `src/typechecker.rs:4224-4227`). **Diagnostic shape** (rustc-style three-piece): primary names the type (`"discarded `Option` value — `Option` is implicitly `#[must_use]`"`); `help` offers the actionable fix (`"bind the value with `let _ = ...` to acknowledge the discard explicitly, or consume it via `match` / `if let` so each variant is handled."`); `note` explains *why* dropping these two types is a hazard (`"... silently abandons {an `Err` / a `None`} branch the caller meant to handle — the two language-level types `Result[T, E]` and `Option[T]` carry this recognition in the typechecker rather than as a user-visible `#[must_use]` attribute."`). **CLI integration** at `src/cli.rs` after the slice-3 `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` lint pass with a parallel `render_must_use_lint_diag` helper (each lint module owning its own `LintDiagnostic` struct is the pre-existing pattern; a future lint-registry refactor — see the "Lint level attributes" entry below — would unify these). The lint takes `pipeline.typed.as_ref()` so it degrades to a no-op when typecheck info is unavailable. **Test surface** in `tests/must_use_lint.rs` (17 tests). Positive: `test_discarded_option_call_warns`, `test_discarded_result_call_warns`, `test_discarded_option_inside_unsafe_block_warns` (walker recurses into nested blocks), `test_discarded_in_if_then_branch_warns`, `test_discarded_in_loop_body_warns`, `test_multiple_discards_each_warn` (per-site warning), `test_discarded_method_call_returning_option_warns` (return-type check, not receiver-based). Negative: `test_let_binding_does_not_trigger`, `test_let_underscore_discard_does_not_trigger` (explicit-discard form), `test_tail_expression_does_not_trigger`, `test_return_does_not_trigger`, `test_non_must_use_return_type_does_not_trigger`, `test_method_call_returning_non_must_use_does_not_trigger` (chained `.is_some()` consumes the Option; the discarded value is the bool), `test_nested_in_let_value_does_not_trigger`, `test_let_binding_inside_block_with_discard_warns_once` (mixed body — one bound, one discarded). Diagnostic shape: `test_discarded_option_diagnostic_has_help_and_note`, `test_discarded_result_diagnostic_has_help_and_note` (help mentions `let _ = ` + pattern matching; note distinguishes `Err` vs. `None` branch wording and pins "language-level"). Slices 2–4 will extend `must_use_lint.rs` rather than create new modules: slice 2 adds `#[must_use]` attribute application to stdlib types in `runtime/stdlib/*.kara`; slice 3 adds the new `missing_must_use` stdlib-hygiene lint; slice 4 generalises `check_discard` to honour user-authored `#[must_use]` on types and on function return values (registry plumbing through `TypeEnv` / `FunctionSig` per the survey).

  - [x] **Slice 2 — Stdlib `#[must_use]` annotations shipped 2026-05-16.** Per scope, slice 2 applies `#[must_use]` to every type in the v1 stdlib that falls in the iterator-adapter or guard category; types not yet present (`MutexGuard` / `RwLockReadGuard` / `RwLockWriteGuard` / `RefCellRefGuard` / `RefCellMutGuard`, `JoinHandle[T]`, `String.to_lowercase` / `.trim` / `.replace`, `Path.with_extension`, builders) carry forward to the slice that lands them — the spec's "(when builders ship)" / "(case-by-case as stdlib lands)" scoping. The annotations land on the AST today (parser already accepts `#[must_use]` / `#[must_use = "..."]` on struct declarations — see `tests/parser.rs::test_attribute_string_value`) and are inert until slice 4 wires the discard-site enforcement that reads them. **Annotated in baked source.** `runtime/stdlib/peekable.kara`'s `Peekable[T]` (iterator-adapter category) carries `#[must_use = "discarding the iterator drops every adapter without running it — chain a terminal method or bind the result"]` — the spec-mandated message verbatim. `runtime/stdlib/pool.kara`'s `PooledConnection[T]` (guard category — the file-level "drop releases automatically" contract puts it structurally in the same RAII slot as `MutexGuard` / `RwLockGuard` / `RefCellGuard`) carries `#[must_use = "discarding the connection releases the slot back to the pool without using it — bind the handle to a variable so it lives across the work, or pass it to the consuming function"]` — guard-shaped wording naming the wasted resource (slot) and the canonical fixes (bind / pass-through). Both struct declarations gain a file-level note pointing at the slice 4 entry so the next reader sees why the attribute is currently inert. **Deferred within slice 2 (scoped to slice 4).** The `Iterator` pseudo-struct (`Type::Named { name: "Iterator", … }` — the return type of `map` / `filter` / `take` / `skip` / `chain` / `zip` / `enumerate` / `rev` / `flatten` / `flat_map` / `inspect` / `cycle` / `step_by` / `Vec.iter()` per `src/typechecker/stdlib_iter.rs`) is registered programmatically in `src/typechecker/env_build.rs::register_compiler_intrinsic_env` with no baked-source surface. Carrying the must-use intent on the pseudo-struct requires the slice 4 `StructInfo.must_use_message: Option<String>` field (per slice 4's own plumbing-prerequisites list: "Extend `EnumInfo` / `StructInfo` similarly for type-level `#[must_use]`."). To keep the slice boundary clean, the Iterator pseudo-struct annotation lands as part of slice 4 alongside the field that consumes it; slice 2 ships the baked-source half. **Test surface** in `tests/must_use_lint.rs` (5 new tests, immediately after the slice 1 diagnostic-shape tests). Positive: `test_slice2_peekable_carries_must_use_annotation` (parses `peekable.kara` from `STDLIB_SOURCES`, finds `struct Peekable`, asserts the `must_use` attribute is present and the `string_value` contains both the discard-hazard phrase and the actionable-fix phrases), `test_slice2_pooled_connection_carries_must_use_annotation` (same shape for `pool.kara`'s `PooledConnection`, checking the guard-shaped wording covers the resource name (connection / slot) and the canonical fixes (bind / pass-through)). Negative-space: `test_slice2_pool_struct_does_not_carry_must_use` (the `Pool[T]` constructor handle is a long-lived resource the caller stores, NOT a guard — catches an over-broad future edit that annotates every type in `pool.kara`), `test_slice2_vec_does_not_carry_must_use` (data containers like `Vec` are not in slice 2 scope — they are freely droppable), `test_slice2_sender_and_receiver_do_not_carry_must_use` (channel halves are long-lived handles, not consume-on-acquire guards — slice 2 doesn't list them). The negative-space tests are the regression net: they catch a future patch that mistakes "anything in pool.kara" or "anything stdlib" for the slice 2 scope. **Why only AST-level pins, not env-level pins:** today's `StructInfo` does not yet carry the must_use field (slice 4's prerequisite), so the only observable surface for the annotation in slice 2 is the parsed AST attribute. Slice 4 adds the field plus the population pipeline, and slice 4's tests will exercise the env-level surface end-to-end.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — `missing_must_use` stdlib-hygiene lint shipped 2026-05-16.** New lint module `src/missing_must_use_lint.rs` warns when a baked stdlib function returns a value the caller should not silently discard but is NOT annotated `#[must_use]`. Module-level pattern mirrors the slice 1 / `unsafe_lint` shape (own `LintLevel` / `LintDiagnostic` per the established cross-module convention; the planned lint-registry refactor — see the deferred "Lint level attributes" entry below — will unify these). **Heuristics (two of three from the spec fire today).** (1) *Iterator-adapter return.* Matches `Type::Path` whose last segment is `"Iterator"` or `"Peekable"` — every iterator-adapter return type in `src/typechecker/stdlib_iter.rs` collapses to `Iterator[Item = …]`, and `Peekable[T]` is the one adapter with its own baked struct (slice 2 annotation target). Diagnostic message: `"stdlib fn <name> returns an iterator-shaped value but is not annotated #[must_use]"`; help points the stdlib author at the slice 2 spec-mandated message verbatim. (2) *New-value-from-self.* Function takes `ref self` or no `self`, and returns a non-trivial value (≠ `Unit`, ≠ `Self`, ≠ impl-target literal name, ≠ `Result` / `Option`). Owned-self and mut-ref-self receivers are intentionally excluded (the spec scopes the check to non-consuming receivers — consuming-self builders return the consumed-and-respun receiver, which the owned-self exclusion handles uniformly). (3) *Guard-shaped via a `Guard` marker trait.* Deferred until the marker trait lands, per the spec's "once the trait lands" qualifier. **Scope (stdlib only).** Walks `Item::Function` and inherent-impl `ImplItem::Method` (impl blocks with `trait_name == None`); fires only when `Function.stdlib_origin == true`. Trait method declarations (`TraitItem::Method`) are skipped — they describe contracts, not implementations; the `#[must_use]` semantic on a trait method belongs on the declaration so every implementor inherits it. Trait-impl methods (impl blocks with `trait_name == Some(_)`) are also skipped — linting them would force every implementor to re-annotate. User code (`stdlib_origin == false`) stays silent by design (the spec's "allow-for-user-code" wording); when the lint-level-attributes framework lands, end-user code can opt in via `#[deny(missing_must_use)]`. **Attribute-based suppression.** `#[must_use]` on the function silences (slice 4's discard-site enforcement reads the attribute; the lint exists to catch the missing annotation, not to second-guess it). `#[allow(missing_must_use)]` also silences — recognised in both surface forms today (positional and named) via the same shape as `unsafe_lint::has_lint_attr`; the broader lint-level-attributes framework that activates `#[warn]` / `#[deny]` / `#[expect]` is still deferred. **Return-shape exclusions.** `Unit` returns, no `return_type` (implicit Unit), `Result[…]` / `Option[…]` returns (covered by slice 1 already), `Self` returns, and impl-target literal-name returns (e.g., `impl Command { fn passthrough(ref self) -> Command }`) all skip. The impl-target check is the structural complement to the `Self` check — both shapes are the consuming-self / pass-through pattern. **CLI integration** at `src/cli.rs` immediately after the slice 1 `must_use_lint` pass, with a parallel `render_missing_must_use_lint_diag` helper (structurally identical to `render_must_use_lint_diag`; future lint-registry refactor unifies them). End-user compiles see no output from this pass today because baked stdlib items aren't spliced into the user program AST — the lint surfaces during karac's own stdlib-hygiene tests and during any future bundled-stdlib-source compile mode. **Severity.** Today the lint is `LintLevel::Warning`. The spec's "deny-by-default for stdlib crates" graduates to `LintLevel::Error` for `stdlib_origin == true` items once the lint-level-attributes framework lands and provides the deny/warn/expect knob; today's Warning ships ahead of the framework so the diagnostic is visible without blocking compiles. **Test surface** in `tests/missing_must_use_lint.rs` (20 tests, synthetic-AST helpers for minimal-friction coverage). **Positive (5):** `test_iterator_return_no_self_fires` (free fn returning `Iterator[…]` fires with iterator-flavored message + slice 2 spec-mandated help + slice 4 cross-reference in note), `test_peekable_return_fires_under_iterator_heuristic` (Peekable recognised), `test_new_value_no_self_fires` (constructor-shape no-self fns fire with new-value-flavored message + heuristic-named note), `test_inherent_impl_method_ref_self_returning_new_value_fires` (Stats / Cli accessor shape), `test_inherent_static_method_returning_other_type_fires` (Widget.describe shape). **Negative-space receiver exclusions (2):** `test_owned_self_receiver_does_not_fire`, `test_mut_ref_self_receiver_does_not_fire`. **Negative-space return exclusions (6):** `test_unit_return_does_not_fire`, `test_no_return_type_does_not_fire`, `test_result_return_does_not_fire`, `test_option_return_does_not_fire`, `test_self_return_does_not_fire`, `test_impl_target_return_does_not_fire`. **Negative-space attribute exclusions (2):** `test_must_use_annotated_does_not_fire`, `test_allow_missing_must_use_suppresses`. **Negative-space scope exclusions (3):** `test_user_origin_does_not_fire`, `test_non_pub_free_function_does_not_fire`, `test_trait_impl_method_does_not_fire`. **AST sanity pin (1):** `test_visibility_helper_aligns_with_is_pub_field` — the lint reads `is_pub` directly, so a future helper-vs-boolean drift would silently shift the lint's scope; this test catches it. **Stdlib-hygiene baseline (1):** `test_stdlib_hygiene_baseline_lint_runs_against_real_baked_source` walks `STDLIB_PROGRAMS`, flips `stdlib_origin` on every Function / ImplItem::Method (mirroring what the bake step does at production runtime), runs the lint, and asserts the diagnostic list is non-empty. The lower-bound assertion (rather than a fixed integer) lets future triage commits shrink the baseline without re-flipping the pin; the test guards "lint is wired end-to-end against real baked source and finds real candidates" — it does NOT pin the exact triage status. **What triage looks like (carry-forward).** The actual `#[must_use]` annotation triage on existing stdlib pub fns (`Command.new`, `Parser.new`, `Stats.mean`, `Cli.help_text`, `Ordering.is_lt`, `Runtime.has_debug_metadata`, `intrinsics::size_of`, etc.) is a follow-up: each annotation is a one-line `#[must_use = "<reason>"]` addition; the lint catches the candidates mechanically, the message wording is reviewer judgement, and the per-annotation rationale (why discarding wastes the call) goes in the attribute string. The triage is intentionally NOT part of this slice — landing the lint without the triage is the right cut, since the heuristic-driven candidate list is the input the triage commits work off of. Future slice 4 enforcement (discarding a `#[must_use]` value at statement position warns) lights up immediately when each triage commit lands, no further plumbing needed.

  - [x] **Slice 4 — General `#[must_use]` honoring + diagnostic shape shipped 2026-05-16.** Generalises slice 1's hardcoded `Result` / `Option` walker into a registry-backed check that honours `#[must_use]` on arbitrary types and on function returns. **Plumbing (env-side).** Extended `StructInfo` and `EnumInfo` (`src/typechecker/env.rs`) with `must_use_message: Option<String>` carrying the author's reason string from `#[must_use = "..."]` (or `Some("")` for the bare `#[must_use]` form, `None` when no attribute). Extended `TypeEnv` with `must_use_functions: HashMap<String, Option<String>>` keyed by `"name"` for free functions and `"TargetType.method"` for impl methods (matching the canonical shape produced by `method_callee_types` / `bare_assoc_fn_targets`). New helper `extract_must_use_message(attrs) -> Option<String>` in `src/typechecker.rs` parallel to `extract_derived_traits`. `env_add_struct` / `env_add_enum` / `env_add_function` / `env_add_impl` (`src/typechecker/env_build.rs`) populate the fields from the AST attribute list; the early-pass struct/enum stubs in `build_type_env` also propagate the field so the env entry is consistent across both passes. **Iterator pseudo-struct annotation.** `register_compiler_intrinsic_env` now sets `must_use_message = Some("discarding the iterator drops every adapter without running it — chain a terminal method or bind the result")` on the `Iterator` parametric pseudo-struct. Slice 2 deferred this — the slice 2 commit ships the baked-source half (`Peekable[T]` / `PooledConnection[T]` annotations) and points at slice 4 for the pseudo-struct annotation that needs the `StructInfo` field to consume it. With this in place, every iterator-adapter return type from `src/typechecker/stdlib_iter.rs` (`map`, `filter`, `take`, `skip`, `chain`, `zip`, `enumerate`, `rev`, `flatten`, `flat_map`, `inspect`, `cycle`, `step_by`, `Vec.iter()`, …) collapses to `Type::Named { name: "Iterator", … }` and the discard-site walker fires uniformly across the adapter surface. **TypeCheckResult surface.** Added `pub must_use_functions: HashMap<String, Option<String>>` (snapshot of `TypeEnv.must_use_functions` at end-of-check, alongside the existing `struct_info` / `enum_info` snapshots). The lint walker takes `Option<&TypeCheckResult>` so it has direct access to all three registries without re-reading the env. **Walker generalisation** in `src/must_use_lint.rs`: `check_discard` now has three layered sources, fired in priority order with NO double-fire (the first match wins): (1) *Implicit (slice 1).* `Result[T, E]` / `Option[T]` still use the slice 1 wording — the language-level `Err` / `None` branch hazard message is more specific than the generic type-level message. (2) *Type-level (slice 4).* Any other `Type::Named { name, .. }` whose `struct_info[name].must_use_message` or `enum_info[name].must_use_message` is `Some(_)` — covers slice 2's baked annotations, the Iterator pseudo-struct, and every future user-authored `#[must_use]` on a struct/enum declaration. (3) *Function-level (slice 4).* If the discarded expression is a call (`ExprKind::Call` with `Identifier` callee → free fn, `Path` callee → static method, or `ExprKind::MethodCall` → instance method resolved via `method_callee_types`) and the callee key is in `must_use_functions`, fire against the call site. Function-level fires only when the return type itself isn't already must-use — the priority ordering prevents the redundant warning a `#[must_use]` fn returning a `#[must_use]` type would produce. **Diagnostic shape.** Each source has its own message + note: slice 1's wording is preserved verbatim; type-level renders `"discarded `<TypeName>` value — `<TypeName>` is annotated `#[must_use]`"` with `note: `<TypeName>` is annotated `#[must_use = "<msg>"]`. <msg>.` (or a no-author-supplied-reason fallback for bare `#[must_use]`); function-level renders `"discarded return value of `<callee>` — the function is annotated `#[must_use]`"` with the parallel note shape. All three share the same `help:` line offering `let _ = ...` as the canonical fix. **Discard-site precision (unchanged from slice 1).** Statement-position expressions (`StmtKind::Expr`) are checked; block tail expressions (`block.final_expr`) flow as the block's value and are NOT checked at that level; let-bindings (`StmtKind::Let { value, .. }`) recurse into the value but don't trigger the discard check (so `let _ = expr;`, `let x = expr;`, and `let _g = mutex.lock();` are all silent). Return-expressions (`ExprKind::Return(Some(e))`) recurse into `e` but the return itself has type `Never` and never matches the must-use type set. **Test surface** in `tests/must_use_lint.rs` (18 new tests, immediately after the slice 2 baked-stdlib pins; 40 total in the file). **Type-level Iterator-pseudo-struct (3):** `test_discarded_iterator_chain_warns_via_type_level_must_use` (`vec.iter().map(|x| x + 1);` fires with the Iterator wording), `test_iterator_chain_with_terminal_collect_does_not_warn` (the `.collect()` consumes the iterator → outermost return is `Vec[i64]` → silent), `test_let_binding_iterator_chain_does_not_warn` (let-binding silences). **Type-level user-authored (3):** `test_discarded_user_struct_with_must_use_attribute_warns` (user struct with attribute fires;
