author's reason in note), `test_discarded_user_enum_with_must_use_attribute_warns` (enum symmetry), `test_bare_must_use_attribute_on_struct_warns_with_default_note` (bare `#[must_use]` renders the no-author-supplied-reason fallback). **Type-level negative-space (1):** `test_user_struct_without_must_use_does_not_warn` (plain struct silent — catches over-broad lookup). **Function-level (3):** `test_discarded_free_function_with_must_use_warns`, `test_function_without_must_use_does_not_warn`, `test_let_bound_must_use_function_call_does_not_warn` (binding silences even for `#[must_use]` callee). **Method-level (2):** `test_discarded_static_method_with_must_use_warns` (`Builder.new()` → `"Builder.new"` registry key via `Path` callee join), `test_discarded_instance_method_with_must_use_warns` (`obj.method()` → resolved via `method_callee_types`). **Precedence (2):** `test_function_returning_must_use_type_prefers_type_level_diag` (no double-fire; type-level wins), `test_result_discard_prefers_implicit_slice_1_diag` (slice 1 wording wins even when function is `#[must_use]`-annotated — pins the spec's "Result / Option discard warns regardless of attribute" requirement). **Env-side pins (4):** `test_iterator_pseudo_struct_carries_must_use_in_typechecker_env` (guards `register_compiler_intrinsic_env`'s Iterator annotation), `test_peekable_baked_struct_carries_must_use_in_typechecker_env` (guards slice 2's `Peekable[T]` annotation flowing through `env_add_struct`), `test_must_use_functions_registry_populates_from_free_function`, `test_must_use_functions_registry_populates_from_impl_method` (key shapes). **Slice 1 tests (17) preserved.** The slice 1 wording paths are unchanged so all 17 of slice 1's tests + the 5 slice-2 baked-stdlib pins continue to pass against the generalised walker. **Closes the mandate.** Slice 4 is the last sub-slice; the parent `#[must_use]` mandate entry flips to `[x]`. Triage of existing stdlib `pub fn`s with `#[must_use]` annotations remains as a follow-up sub-thread (the slice 3 `missing_must_use` lint catches the candidate set mechanically; each triage commit adds a one-line `#[must_use = "<reason>"]` and slice 4's enforcement lights up automatically with no further plumbing). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features).

- [x] **Closure default capture mode — bare `|...|` runs Rule 2 per-capture-name inference shipped 2026-05-16.** Implements the spec in `design.md § Closures: parameter modes, capture, and escape > Rule 2½`. Surface work shipped previously: parser accepts `own |x|` / `ref |x|` / `mut ref |x|` (`CaptureMode::Own` variant, parser arms with lookahead guards on `Pipe | PipePipe`); `move |x|` is rejected with a redirect-to-`own` diagnostic; ownership-checker enforces the K2 conflict diagnostics for explicit `ref` / `mut ref` prefixes (`CaptureModeViolation`) and the unused-mut-capture perf note for `mut ref` declared / read-only used (`UnusedMutCaptureNote`, with machine-applicable `mut ref` → `ref` rewrite when the prefix span is recorded). Sub-slices: slice 1 (bare-form per-capture-name inference + plumbing + test pins) + slice 2 (`karac explain --concept=closures` inspector page) both shipped 2026-05-16. Per-*path* (Rule 2¼ disjoint-capture) is a separate top-level entry below ("Disjoint closure capture") — once that lands, the per-name inference here generalises to per-path uniformly through the same `closure_captures` registry without rewriting the bare-form classification.

  - [x] **Slice 1 — Bare-form per-capture-name inference + plumbing + test pins shipped 2026-05-16.** The ownership pass already runs Rule 2's first-use scan over each captured root binding when `capture_mode = None` (`src/ownership/expr_check.rs` Closure arm, lines ~895–924): `pre_live` snapshots outer Live bindings, `classify_capture_body_uses` records each capture's `referenced` / `mutated` flags, and the post-walk `states[name] == Moved` check yields the consume signal. Classification: `consumed → Own`, else `mutated → MutRef`, else `Ref`. Output flows into `closure_captures: HashMap<SpanKey, Vec<(String, OwnershipMode)>>` and surfaces via `karac query ownership <fn>`'s `closures[].captures[]` JSON array (one entry per closure, each `{name, mode}` pair recording the inferred mode). The earlier `closure_param_modes` Vec uses the same `(String, OwnershipMode)` shape — parameters and captures share the inference machinery and the surface representation. **Why "per-capture-name" not "per-path".** Today's classification keys by the root binding name; field projections under the same root collapse to one capture entry. This matches Rule 2's per-capture-name granularity; the per-path (Rule 2¼) extension lives in the companion "Disjoint closure capture" entry below — slice 1 here ships the inference machine the per-path extension will plug into without re-architecting it. **Outer-scope routing.** When a bare body's captured root is classified `Own`, the outer-scope use after the closure expression is NOT a UseAfterMove — it routes through Part 4 RC trigger 2 (`ClosureCaptureWithOuterUse`), tentatively promoting the captured binding to `Rc` and recording the entry in `rc_values["fn"]["binding"]`. This is the spec's "(ii) Escape with outer use of a capture" case from Rule 2: the closure creation and the outer use compose under the existing RC dataflow pass rather than a closure-specific borrow rule. **Test surface pinned in `tests/ownership.rs`** (6 new tests, immediately after `nested_closures_each_get_their_own_mode_entry`). Bare-form inference pins (3): `capture_mutated_in_body_is_mut_ref` (field-assign mutation of captured root → MutRef; completes the {Ref, MutRef, Own} trio alongside `capture_read_only_is_ref` and `capture_consumed_in_body_is_own`); `bare_closure_read_capture_leaves_outer_binding_usable` (post-closure outer-scope read after Ref capture); `bare_closure_consume_capture_with_outer_use_routes_through_rc_fallback` (post-closure outer-scope consume after Own capture → `RcTrigger::ClosureCaptureWithOuterUse`, NOT UseAfterMove — pins the routing). Explicit-prefix `own` pins (2): `capture_mode_own_prefix_accepts_consume_body` (K2 row "own + consumes"); `capture_mode_own_prefix_accepts_read_only_body` (K2 row "own + reads only" — the capture-for-ownership-extension idiom; no UnusedMutCaptureNote since that note is specific to `mut ref` declared / read-only used). Diagnostic-wording pins (2 — `tests/ownership.rs`): `capture_mode_ref_consume_diagnostic_includes_spec_fix_wording` (pins the spec-mandated `ref` fix string `"drop the `ref` prefix (use `own` or bare) or remove the consume"`); `capture_mode_mut_ref_consume_diagnostic_includes_spec_fix_wording` (pins `"drop the `mut ref` prefix and use `own`"`). Existing K2 tests (`test_capture_mode_ref_consume_is_error` / `test_capture_mode_mut_ref_consume_is_error`) verified kind + key terms; these new pins lock the full guidance string so a future diagnostic rewrite cannot silently drop the redirect shape. **AST doc tightening.** Updated the `capture_mode` field doc comment in `src/ast/exprs.rs` to spell out the bare-form inference rule (Rule 2 first-use scan) and the K2 prefix enforcement, replacing the stale "captures by ownership; default" wording that predated the bare-form inference shipping.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — `karac explain --concept=closures` inspector page shipped 2026-05-16.** Concept-level explainer surface the spec calls out as "the answer to Rule 2½'s fragility concern". New `karac explain` subcommand (`Command::Explain { concept }` in `src/cli.rs` parallel to `Command::Query`) with a `--concept=NAME` flag; the per-concept static text lives in `src/cli/explain.rs` (`ExplainConcept` enum + `render(concept_name)` dispatch + `CLOSURES_PAGE` constant). Page content meets all three spec requirements: (a) Rule 2 first-use inference (read → `ref`, mutate → `mut ref`, consume → `own`), the three explicit prefixes (`own` / `ref` / `mut ref`), and the K2 conflict table rendered with a redirect-id column (`[K2-ref-consume]`, `[K2-mut-ref-consume]`, `[unused-mut-capture]`) whose bodies appear unwrapped on single lines below the table so the diagnostic-redirect strings the ownership checker emits are pinnable verbatim — the wording `"drop the `ref` prefix (use `own` or bare) or remove the consume"` and `"drop the `mut ref` prefix and use `own`"` is locked by the test pins below; (b) cross-references the disjoint-capture (Rule 2¼) extension naming the companion "Disjoint closure capture" entry so a reader knows the per-name granularity is temporary and where the per-path future lives; (c) closing section "Inspecting inferred capture modes" describes `karac query ownership <file>.<function>` with the actual JSON shape (`closures[]` entries carrying `line` / `column` / `parameters` / `captures`, each `{name, mode}` pair using the same `own` / `ref` / `mut_ref` strings the query JSON emits) plus a sample. **Additional sections** beyond the spec floor: (d) outer-scope routing for `own`-captured roots — pins the spec's "(ii) Escape with outer use of a capture" Rule 2 case naming `RcTrigger::ClosureCaptureWithOuterUse`, which is the most common surprise the page exists to demystify; (e) "when to use which form" — short and escape rules of thumb derived from design.md § Closures' "fragility concern" rationale. **Help surface.** `print_help` (`src/cli/help.rs`) lists the new subcommand with the supported concept set; `print_subcommand_help` adds an "explain" arm that documents `--concept=NAME` and `SEE ALSO: karac query ownership`. **Test surface** in `tests/cli.rs` (16 new tests, immediately after `test_subcommand_help_vendor`). Discovery (2): `test_main_help_lists_explain_command`, `test_subcommand_help_explain`. Content pins (7): `test_explain_concept_closures_renders_page` (section headers — "Closures: parameter modes, capture, and escape", "Rule 2 first-use inference", "Explicit prefixes: own | ref | mut ref", "K2 conflict table"); `test_explain_concept_closures_pins_first_use_classification` (the read/mutate/consume rows + the `ref < mut ref < own` ordering); `test_explain_concept_closures_pins_k2_ref_consume_redirect` (verbatim K2 ref+consume diagnostic string — pinned at `src/ownership/expr_check.rs:1004`); `test_explain_concept_closures_pins_k2_mut_ref_consume_redirect` (verbatim K2 mut-ref+consume string — `src/ownership/expr_check.rs:1007`); `test_explain_concept_closures_pins_unused_mut_capture_note` (the `perf[unused-mut-capture]` code name); `test_explain_concept_closures_cross_references_disjoint_capture` (Rule 2¼ + "Disjoint closure capture" cross-reference per spec requirement b); `test_explain_concept_closures_links_to_query_ownership` (`karac query ownership <file>.<function>` link per spec requirement c); `test_explain_concept_closures_describes_outer_scope_rc_routing` (the `RcTrigger::ClosureCaptureWithOuterUse` outer-scope routing section). Negative-space arg-parsing (7): `test_explain_requires_concept_flag` (bare `karac explain` rejected naming the flag and a supported concept), `test_explain_rejects_unknown_concept_with_supported_set` (rejected concept name surfaces the supported set in the error message — so a typo redirect always lists the live options), `test_explain_rejects_empty_concept_value` (`--concept=` empty value), `test_explain_rejects_duplicate_concept_flags`, `test_explain_rejects_positional_argument` (a bare positional name is rejected with a redirect to `--concept=NAME`), `test_explain_rejects_unknown_flag`. **Why a static-text dispatcher rather than a doc-page renderer.** The spec called out either option; the static `&'static str` shape is the right cut today — one concept, content stable, no plumbing through compiler analysis. When more concepts land (ownership, effects, RC fallback, …), each appends a `ExplainConcept` variant and a page constant; the dispatch stays one match arm. If we later want richer rendering (Markdown → terminal, hyperlinks, search), the surface swaps under the same CLI shape without re-architecting the subcommand. Phase target: 5.2 (CLI surface).

  Phase target: 5.2 (analyser-side inference — shipped; CLI explain surface — shipped). Spec-level decision: ✅ shipped 2026-05-02 (option c with `own` keyword, per v60 item 16 and § Closure Behavior, Rule 2½ rewrite).

- [x] **Disjoint closure capture — place-expression-granular capture, not whole bindings — shipped 2026-05-16.** All six slices landed: (1) closure-analyser path enumeration; (2) per-path mode inference; (3) borrow-checker integration; (4) codegen per-path env layout; (5) Rule 2½ prefix forces per-path modes; (6) whole-root capture reason tracking + N0503 enrichment. See per-slice entries below for ship details. Implement the spec in `design.md § Closures: parameter modes, capture, and escape > Rule 2¼ — Disjoint capture`. Slices: (1) Closure-analyser pass — when scanning a closure body for captures, record the *capture path set* per root binding rather than just the set of captured names. A capture path is `(root: Ident, projection: Vec<FieldName>)`. The walk extends an in-progress path through chained `.field` accesses on a directly-captured local, and stops (committing the current path with the root captured whole) when it reaches an index expression, a method call, a deref of a captured borrow, or a function call passing the binding by value. (2) Per-path mode inference — run the existing use-predicate scan from Rule 2 against each capture path independently, so two paths under the same root may take different modes (one `ref`, the other `mut ref`). The disjointness check uses the existing place-expression algebra from the borrow checker — no new logic. (3) Borrow-checker integration — pass the precise capture-path set to the borrow checker at the closure expression site so outer-scope use of a sibling unmentioned path is permitted; outer-scope use of an ancestor of a captured path is restricted by the existing place-disjointness rule. (4) Closure environment representation — at the IR / interpreter / codegen level, the closure's captured environment carries one slot per captured path (not one slot per captured name). For interpretation, the existing whole-environment snapshot is over-approximating but not unsound (typechecker/ownership pass enforces precision before the interpreter runs); a tighter per-path snapshot is polish, not correctness. For codegen, the synthesized closure struct must lay out one field per captured path so the call site reads the right offset. (5) Rule 2½ prefix interaction — the explicit `ref` / `mut ref` per-closure prefix is applied *after* the disjoint-path enumeration: the prefix forces every enumerated path to take the prefix's mode. (6) Diagnostics — when a closure expression's outer-scope sibling-path access is denied because the borrow checker conservatively captured the whole root (e.g., the body called a method on the root), the diagnostic must explain *why* the whole root was captured ("call to method `User.foo` on `user` captures `user` whole — disjoint capture only sees through field projections") and offer a fix-it hoisting the field access outside the method call. Test coverage (Phase 4 / Phase 5.2): two closures over different fields of the same struct compile and run; a closure that reads `u.name` and writes `u.age` typechecks; outer-scope access to `u.history` after a closure captured `u.name` is permitted; outer-scope move of `u` while `u.name` is ref-captured is rejected; `vec[i].field` capture in a closure captures `vec` whole; method call inside a closure captures the receiver whole, with mode driven by the method's receiver mode; per-iteration loop capture (already shipped) composes with disjoint-path capture (each iteration's `it.field` is a fresh capture, not a shared root). Phase target: Phase 4 (interpreter — environment representation polish) + Phase 5.2 (typechecker — capture-path analysis + borrow-checker integration). The interpreter polish is optional; the analyser work is required.

  - [x] **Slice 6 — whole-root capture reason + N0503 enrichment shipped 2026-05-16.** Spec sentence honoured (partial — the diagnostic-enrichment half): *"the diagnostic must explain *why* the whole root was captured (`call to method `User.foo` on `user` captures `user` whole — disjoint capture only sees through field projections`) and offer a fix-it hoisting the field access outside the method call"*. The full spec's "outer-scope sibling-path access is denied" framing is implemented today as the existing N0503 RC-fallback note (sibling-path access compiles but routes through RC because the whole-root capture forces it); slice 6 enriches that note with the *why* and the fix-it, rather than widening slice 3 to convert the RC-fallback into a hard rejection. **Why the lighter implementation.** The slice-3 narrow comment explicitly punted whole-root captures to the RC-fallback pass with "Pushing a borrow for whole-root captures would either double-emit (slice 3 error + RC note) or require a coordination layer between the two passes — both worse than letting RC own the whole-root case and slice 3 own the path-precise case." Slice 6 honours that partition: leaves slice 3's narrow intact (the existing `slice3_whole_root_capture_does_not_push_borrow_routes_through_rc_fallback` test continues to pass), keeps the RC-fallback pass as the "denial" surface for whole-root cases, and lands the spec-mandated diagnostic enrichment on that surface. Promoting RC-fallback to hard rejection (with the required cross-pass coordination) remains available as a future widening if real usage shows the perf note is too soft. **New `WholeRootCaptureReason` enum in `src/ownership.rs`**: five variants — `MethodCall { method_name, call_span }`, `Index { call_span }`, `Deref { call_span }`, `ByValuePass { call_span }`, `BareIdentifier`. The first four are the slice-1 stopping constructs that commit a root to whole-root capture; `BareIdentifier` is the natural-shape case (the body directly names the binding without going through any stopping construct). `WholeRootCaptureReason::describe(root)` renders the spec-mandated *"the closure body called method `…` on `…` (disjoint capture only sees through field projections)"* prose for each variant; `span()` exposes the construct's source span (None for `BareIdentifier`); `is_bare_identifier()` drives the merge priority. **New `whole_root_capture_reasons: HashMap<SpanKey, HashMap<String, WholeRootCaptureReason>>`** field on `OwnershipChecker` and `OwnershipCheckResult`. Keyed by `(closure SpanKey, captured root name)` — only roots actually committed to whole-root capture appear; path-precise captures (non-empty projection) record no reason because the path itself is the explanation. **Slice-1 walker extension** (`src/ownership/capture_body.rs`): `classify_capture_body_paths` now returns `(Vec<CapturePath>, HashMap<String, WholeRootCaptureReason>)` — same path-set output as before, plus the parallel per-root reason map. `walk_capture_paths_expr` gained a `reasons: &mut HashMap<...>` argument threaded through every recursive call site (Field/Index/Method/Deref/Call/Binary/If/Match/While/For/Loop/Closure/Block/Tuple/StructLit/Pipe/Range/Return/Providers/Cast/Question — every site that touched the original walker is updated, no missing branches). Each stopping-construct arm calls `record_whole_root_reason(reasons, &root, …)` immediately after the path insertion. **Priority merge in `record_whole_root_reason`**: first stopping construct encountered wins; `BareIdentifier` is the lowest-priority reason — vacant entry gets whatever is offered, but an existing `BareIdentifier` is replaced by any non-bare reason while a stopping-construct entry is never replaced. This means a body that both calls `u.show()` (early) and references `u` bare later (e.g., `take(u)` as a separate statement) ends up with `MethodCall` as the reason — the construct most likely to be rewritable wins, not the last one observed. **`ByValuePass` detection** lives in `register_bare_root_arg_as_byvalue` (new private helper in `capture_body.rs`). The Call and MethodCall arms both call it for each arg before recursing — if the arg is *syntactically* a bare identifier (`f(cfg)` shape, not `f(cfg.x)` or `f(1 + cfg)`), `(cfg, [])` is inserted with a `ByValuePass { call_span = enclosing call expr span }` reason. The generic walker's later recursion into the same arg will hit `extract_pure_path` and try to register `BareIdentifier`, but the priority rule keeps `ByValuePass`. Sub-expression bare references (`f(1 + cfg)` → `cfg` deep inside a Binary) get `BareIdentifier` because the by-value detection is shape-gated to the immediate-arg position. **Wiring point** in `src/ownership/expr_check.rs`'s `ExprKind::Closure` arm: the slice-1 call destructures into `(capture_paths, whole_root_reasons)` and inserts the reason map under the closure span key when non-empty (skips empty inserts so consumers can use `whole_root_capture_reasons.is_empty()` as "no whole-root captures fired" sentinel). **N0503 enrichment** in `src/ownership/rc_promote.rs`'s `emit_rc_fallback_notes`: for each RC entry `(fn_key, binding, entry)`, a new `find_whole_root_closure_reason(fn_key, binding)` lookup walks `whole_root_capture_reasons` for any closure whose `closure_function` matches `fn_key` and whose reasons map contains `binding`. When a reason is found, the note's message is extended with `— closure at line N:M captured `X` whole because <reason.describe(X)>` and the suggestion is replaced with the slice-6 fix-it per variant: `MethodCall` → *"hoist the call outside the closure (assign `<method>`'s result to a local before the closure) so the closure body captures only the fields it actually reads"*; `Index` → *"hoist the indexed element into a local before the closure so the closure body captures only the element, not the whole collection"*; `Deref` → *"hoist the dereferenced value into a local before the closure so the closure body captures the pointee directly"*; `ByValuePass` → *"if only specific fields are needed, project them into locals before the closure and pass those locals instead of the whole binding"*; `BareIdentifier` → falls back to the generic *"accept the RC and silence with #[allow(rc_fallback)]"* (the closure body intentionally names the whole binding — no rewrite to suggest). When no closure-capture reason is found, the note keeps the legacy message and the generic suggestion (negative-pin test `slice6_n0503_note_falls_back_to_generic_for_non_closure_rc`). **Test surface** in `tests/ownership.rs` (11 new tests, immediately before the "Step 7 sentinels: ref-captured value escape" section): `slice6_method_call_records_method_call_reason` (basic reason capture — method-call receiver records `MethodCall { method_name = "show", … }`); `slice6_index_records_index_reason` (Index stopping construct); `slice6_by_value_pass_records_byvaluepass_reason` (bare-rooted call arg records `ByValuePass`, not `BareIdentifier`); `slice6_bare_identifier_records_bareidentifier_reason` (body with no stopping construct gets `BareIdentifier`); `slice6_method_call_beats_bare_identifier_priority` (priority rule: stopping construct wins over later bare-identifier reference); `slice6_first_stopping_construct_wins_over_later_one` (priority rule: first stopping construct wins over later stopping construct under the same root); `slice6_path_precise_capture_records_no_reason` (path-precise captures record no reason — the reasons map is empty); `slice6_n0503_note_includes_method_call_reason` (**slice-6 headline test** — full E2E from `|| u.show(); take(u.history);` to the enriched N0503 note containing *"captured `u` whole"*, *"method `show`"*, and the spec phrase *"disjoint capture only sees through field projections"*); `slice6_n0503_note_includes_method_call_fix_it_suggestion` (companion to the headline — verifies the suggestion field carries the slice-6 fix-it text naming the method to hoist); `slice6_n0503_note_falls_back_to_generic_for_non_closure_rc` (negative pin — a non-closure RC promotion `read(o); take(o);` doesn't get any slice-6 closure-attribution in its note, falls back to the generic suggestion); `slice6_describe_helper_renders_method_call_reason` (direct API pin for `WholeRootCaptureReason::describe` so the spec-mandated message shape is regression-guarded even if the helper moves or is rewritten). **Why the priority rule.** The slice-1 walker is recursive top-down through the body AST. For a body like `|| { u.show(); take(u) }`, the walker first visits the MethodCall (Block stmt[0]), then the Call(take, [u]) — `take(u)` registers `ByValuePass { call_span }` for u. Without the priority rule, ByValuePass would either overwrite MethodCall or be overwritten by it, and the choice would depend on AST visit order. With the rule, the first stopping construct wins — MethodCall stays, ByValuePass is dropped. Pinning the rule means future changes to the walker's traversal order don't silently flip which construct the user sees in the note. **Spec sub-points NOT shipped this slice:** the full spec sentence includes "outer-scope sibling-path access is **denied**" — slice 6 leaves that as RC-promotion (perf note) rather than hard error per the slice-3 narrowing rationale. The fix-it is rendered as suggestion text, not as a machine-applicable `TextEdit` — the rewrites are structural (hoist the call out, project fields into locals before the closure) and a one-shot edit can't generically synthesize them without knowing the method's read set or the binding's intended scope. **Closes slice 6.** All six slices of the parent entry at line 353 are now shipped — the parent `[~]` flips to `[x]` once a closing pass confirms no follow-up surface remains.

  - [x] **Slice 5 — Rule 2½ prefix interaction shipped 2026-05-16.** Spec sentence honoured: *"the explicit `ref` / `mut ref` per-closure prefix is applied after the disjoint-path enumeration: the prefix forces every enumerated path to take the prefix's mode"* — and per design.md § Rule 2¼ Interaction with Rule 2½, the `own` prefix participates in the same rule. **Single insertion point.** In `src/ownership/expr_check.rs`'s `ExprKind::Closure` arm, immediately after slice 2's per-path mode inference loop populates `path_modes` and before slice 3's `push_closure_capture_borrows` consumes it (and before the per-closure modes map is recorded via `closure_capture_path_modes.insert`), a small block consults `capture_mode: Option<CaptureMode>` (the AST field the parser already populates for `own |…|` / `ref |…|` / `mut ref |…|`) and, when `Some`, overwrites every entry's mode with the prefix-mapped `OwnershipMode` (`Own → Own`, `Ref → Ref`, `MutRef → MutRef`). The bare form leaves `path_modes` untouched, so slice 2's per-path inference is preserved verbatim. **Ordering.** The prefix overwrite happens *after* path enumeration (slice 1) and per-path mode inference (slice 2) but *before* the borrow push (slice 3) and the map insert. Slice 3's `push_closure_capture_borrows` therefore sees the pinned modes — a `mut ref` prefix yields `MutRef` borrows even for body-read-only paths, an `own` prefix yields all-`Own` paths which slice 3 skips entirely (Own routes through the consume machinery), and a `ref` prefix yields all-`Ref` borrows (downgrades inferred-`MutRef` paths). **Downstream visibility.** The user-visible consequence is the borrow-conflict diagnostic's `by `<mode>`` tail at `src/ownership/borrow.rs:598-602` — the same outer consume that would name `by `ref`` under a bare-form closure now names `by `mut ref`` under a `mut ref` prefix. **What slice 5 does *not* do.** The existing K2 enforcement (lines 1058-1156 of `expr_check.rs`) is untouched: `ref` / `mut ref` + body consume still fires `CaptureModeViolation` at the closure expression, and `mut ref` + read-only body still emits the `UnusedMutCaptureNote` perf note. Per-name `closure_captures` modes are *not* prefix-forced — that map feeds RC promotion, closure-escape detection, and `karac query ownership`, which all have their own semantics for the prefix-vs-inference interaction; touching it would expand slice 5's blast radius beyond the per-path map. Codegen (slice 4) is unaffected: the per-path layout selector at `src/codegen/closures.rs` reads the path set, not the mode, so the slot shape is invariant under the prefix. **Test surface** in `tests/ownership.rs` (9 new tests, immediately before the slice-3 section): `slice5_ref_prefix_pins_read_only_path_to_ref` (sanity — bare-Ref + ref-prefix = Ref, regression guard for accidental re-classification); `slice5_mut_ref_prefix_pins_read_only_paths_to_mut_ref` (**slice-5 headline** — `mut ref || o.x + o.y` lifts both inferred-`Ref` paths to `MutRef`); `slice5_own_prefix_pins_read_only_path_to_own` (pin that `own` also participates, not just `ref` / `mut ref`); `slice5_mut_ref_prefix_pins_multiple_paths_under_one_root` (`mut ref || { u.age = 99; u.name + 1 }` — slice 2 would record `MutRef` + `Ref` per the disjoint-modes test; prefix forces both to `MutRef`); `slice5_mut_ref_prefix_pins_paths_across_multiple_roots` (cross-root pin — `mut ref || { a.v = 10; b.v + 1 }` pins both roots' paths, matching the per-closure scope of the prefix); `slice5_prefix_does_not_alter_path_set` (regression guard — bare and prefixed forms of the same body have identical `closure_capture_paths`; the prefix changes mode, not enumeration); `slice5_mut_ref_prefix_surfaces_mut_ref_flavor_in_slice3_diagnostic` (the user-visible downstream effect — outer consume under a `mut ref` prefix produces `captures `u.x` by `mut ref`` in the conflict message); `slice5_own_prefix_skips_slice3_borrow_push` (interaction with slice 3 — `own` prefix forces every path to Own, slice 3 skips Own paths, so an outer consume that would otherwise fire `ClosureCaptureBorrowConflict` runs clean); `slice5_bare_form_preserves_slice2_inferred_modes` (negative pin — no prefix means slice 5 is a no-op and the recorded modes match slice 2's per-path inference, catching any future refactor that defaults `capture_mode` to a non-`None` value). **Why per-path-only, not per-name.** The per-path map is freshly added in slice 2 and consumed only by slices 3 and 4 — both of which were designed knowing slice 5 would land. The per-name `closure_captures` map predates the disjoint-capture work and is consumed by RC promotion, closure-escape, and parallel-block analyses, each with prefix-vs-inference semantics already wired (the K2 error path and the unused-mut note). Forcing per-name modes here would either duplicate those semantics or override them in surprising ways; the spec scope is explicitly per-*path*, so this slice stays in that lane. **Closes slice 5.** Slice 6 (diagnostics — explaining *why* the whole root was captured when sibling-path access is denied) remains in scope of the parent entry.

  - [x] **Slice 4 — codegen per-path env layout shipped 2026-05-16.** Slice 1/2 produced per-closure `closure_capture_path_modes: HashMap<SpanKey, Vec<(CapturePath, OwnershipMode)>>`; slice 4 wires that map into the codegen pass so the synthesized closure env struct carries one LLVM field per captured `CapturePath` instead of one field per captured root name. Spec sentence honoured: *"For codegen, the synthesized closure struct must lay out one field per captured path so the call site reads the right offset."* **Plumbing.** New `Codegen::closure_capture_paths: HashMap<SpanKey, Vec<(CapturePath, OwnershipMode)>>` field (`src/codegen.rs`) populated by an extension to `load_rc_fallback` — that function already runs at every `compile_to_ir` / `compile_to_object` entry that threads ownership through, so slice 4 doesn't add a new entry-point seam. `compile_closure` now takes a third arg, the closure expression's `Span`, which the dispatcher at `src/codegen/exprs.rs:198` passes via `&expr.span` (the same `SpanKey::from_span(&expr.span)` shape slices 1/2/3 use as the map key). **Two new private types in `src/codegen/closures.rs`:** `RootUnpackPlan { root_ty, type_name, whole_root_slot, sub_slots }` records how each captured root is rebuilt inside the closure body — `Some(idx)` whole-root slot means load the slot and store into a root-named alloca (matches the legacy per-name layout); `None` plus a `sub_slots: Vec<(env_slot_idx, gep_chain, leaf_ty)>` means allocate a root-typed alloca and stitch each captured leaf into its GEP chain. `CapturePathLayout { slot_tys, slot_sources, root_plans }` is the full per-closure plan: env-struct field types in slot order, per-slot `(root_name, gep_chain)` for the capture-site loader, and per-root unpack plans for the body prelude. **Layout builder** `build_capture_path_layout` (`src/codegen/closures.rs`) returns `None` when the ownership pass didn't supply path-mode data for the closure's `SpanKey` (falls through to per-name layout — preserves `compile_to_ir`-without-ownership paths and codegen-only tests). When data is present, per root: (a) if the root is RC-fallback-promoted (`is_rc_fallback_binding`), is a `ref`-param (`ref_params.contains_key`), or has any projection step that can't resolve through `struct_field_names` → emit one whole-root slot and drop sub-paths; (b) else if any path under this root has empty projection → emit one whole-root slot (the slice-2 ancestor-marking rule means a whole-root entry coexists with sub-path entries, and the whole-root slot subsumes the sub-paths); (c) else → emit one slot per non-empty-projection path, sized to the leaf type at the chain end. Mixed layouts are supported: one closure's env may carry a whole-root slot for one root AND per-path slots for another. A consistency check refuses path-set/free-var disagreement (returns `None` → per-name fallback) so we never emit a partial env. **Projection resolver** `resolve_gep_chain` walks a `Vec<String>` projection into a `Vec<u32>` LLVM GEP-index chain by combining a `struct_field_names[type_name].position()` lookup with a numeric-tuple-index fallback (`step.parse::<u32>()`); each step advances both the LLVM `StructType` pointer (`get_field_type_at_index`) and the source-type-name pointer (`struct_field_type_names[type_name][idx]`). `None` at any step → fall back to whole-root for that root. **Capture site** (step 9 in `compile_closure`): for each env slot, walk the source root via `gep_root_chain` and load the leaf with the slot-typed `leaf_type_for_chain` typed load, then `build_insert_value` into the env aggregate. Whole-root slots load via the existing `build_load(slot.ty, slot.ptr, root)` path. **Body unpack** (step 7a): for each root with a whole-root slot, extract from env and store into a root-named alloca (legacy shape, registered as `VarSlot { ptr, ty: root_ty }`); for stitched roots, allocate a root-typed alloca and for each `(slot_idx, gep_chain, leaf_ty)` extract the leaf and `build_store` into the GEP'd position. The body's `compile_field_access` / `compile_method_call` walks the alloca normally — the ownership pass guarantees the body only reads captured paths, so undef neighbouring fields in the stitched root are never touched. `var_type_names` propagation preserved per root so method dispatch inside the body resolves through the user impl-block. **Test surface** in `tests/codegen.rs` (9 new tests, immediately before the "Shared struct (RC) tests" section): `test_e2e_disjoint_field_capture_returns_leaf_value` (**slice-4 headline**: `let f = || p.x; println(f())` → env carries one i64 leaf slot, body stitches it back, returns the captured field's value); `test_e2e_disjoint_two_closures_over_sibling_fields` (spec test "two closures over different fields of the same struct compile and run" — `|| p.x` + `|| p.y` coexist, each with its own per-path env); `test_e2e_disjoint_field_capture_with_outer_sibling_access` (spec test "outer-scope access to u.history after a closure captured u.name is permitted" — closure over `p.x`, outer code reads `p.y` after construction, full pipeline composes); `test_e2e_disjoint_capture_two_fields_under_one_root` (`|| p.x + p.y` — single closure, two sub-paths under one root, env has two i64 leaf slots and body stitches both); `test_e2e_disjoint_capture_nested_field_path` (multi-segment chain — `Outer { a: Inner { v: i64 }, b: Inner }`, two closures over `o.a.v` and `o.b.v`, exercises 2-deep `resolve_gep_chain` walks); `test_e2e_method_call_on_captured_root_uses_whole_root_layout` (spec test "method call inside a closure captures the receiver whole, with mode driven by the method's receiver mode" — slice 1's path scanner commits whole-root at the method-call stopping construct, slice 4 honours that and emits a one-slot whole-root env); `test_ir_disjoint_field_capture_env_slot_is_leaf_type` (IR pin — the env load in the synthesized closure body is typed `{ i64 }`, not `{ i64, i64 }`; the body also contains a `cap.gep.<n>` GEP for the stitching write); `test_ir_method_call_on_captured_root_forces_whole_root_env` (companion IR pin — the env load for the method-call case is typed `{ { i64, i64 } }`, confirming whole-root capture); `test_e2e_disjoint_capture_preserves_uncaptured_fields_after_call` (stress test — closure captures only `p.x`, leaves `p.y` undef in the stitched alloca; after the call, the outer `p.y` is still its original value, pinning that the per-path stitching doesn't perturb outer-scope state). All 9 tests use `run_program_with_ownership` / `ir_for_with_ownership` — the plain `run_program` / `ir_for` helpers pass `None` for ownership and fall through to the per-name layout, which would leave slice 4 untested. **Backward-compat preserved.** Every existing closure test (`test_e2e_closure_*`, 8 cases) continues to pass through the per-name fallback path: ownership data isn't threaded through `run_program`, the `closure_capture_paths` map is empty for those closures, `build_capture_path_layout` returns `None`, and codegen falls through to the legacy `collect_closure_free_vars` env-layout path unchanged. **Why the wrapper-with-fallback rather than a full per-path rewrite.** The per-name layout is a safe, working baseline that the absence of ownership data already proves correct (the `compile_to_ir` path doesn't run the ownership pass at all). Keeping it as the fallback partitions slice 4's risk to the per-path code paths, and lets the codegen's existing test surface continue to validate the per-name shape even after the wire-format change for the per-path shape lands. **Why stitch into a fresh root alloca rather than rewrite the body's field accesses.** The body's `compile_field_access` and friends already walk root allocas correctly — intercepting them to consult a side-table of `(root, projection) → env_slot` would touch dozens of call sites across `expr_ops.rs` / `method_call.rs` / `pattern_binding.rs`. Stitching scoped the per-path delta to one place (the closure body prelude); the body code is unchanged. The stitched root's undef neighbour fields are sound because the ownership pass guarantees the body only reads captured paths. **Interpreter polish deferred.** The spec line *"For interpretation, the existing whole-environment snapshot is over-approximating but not unsound (typechecker/ownership pass enforces precision before the interpreter runs); a tighter per-path snapshot is polish, not correctness."* is honoured by *not* changing the interpreter — `Function { closure_env: Option<HashMap<String, Value>> }` keyed by root name continues to over-approximate, the ownership pass enforces precision before the interpreter runs, and no slice-4 work lands on the interpreter side. **Closes slice 4.** The interpreter polish is optional; the codegen wire-format change required by the spec is shipped. Slices 5 (Rule 2½ prefix interaction) and 6 (diagnostics) remain in scope of the parent entry.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — borrow-checker integration shipped 2026-05-16.** Closure-induced borrows now track per captured path rather than per root: each `Ref` / `MutRef` entry of the slice-2 path-mode set pushes an `ActiveClosureCapture` into a new per-checker `closure_capture_borrows: HashMap<String, Vec<ActiveClosureCapture>>` map (keyed by root, scope-stamped with `current_scope_depth`). The new struct lives next to `ActiveBorrow` in `src/ownership.rs` and carries the captured path, mode, closure span, and scope depth. A new `push_closure_capture_borrows` helper in `src/ownership/borrow.rs` runs at the `ExprKind::Closure` arm in `src/ownership/expr_check.rs` immediately after slice-2's `closure_capture_path_modes` populate. **Narrowing — whole-root + `Own` paths skip the push.** The slice-3 push explicitly skips empty-projection captures *and* `Own`-mode captures: those are the existing RC-trigger-2 / consume-machinery surface (a bare-identifier or stopping-construct capture composed with an outer use routes through `RcTrigger::ClosureCaptureWithOuterUse`, and `Own` paths transition the legacy `Moved` state for the standard UAM / RC dataflow). Slice 3's rejection rule applies only to *path-precise* captures (non-empty projection) — that is the value-add over per-name capture, and pinning the narrowing keeps the existing `tests/rc_fallback.rs::trigger2_read_only_capture_keeps_consume_site_flavor` test (which expects no error + RC promotion for whole-root capture + outer consume) passing unchanged. **Conflict checker.** New `check_consume_vs_closure_captures(place, span)` method in `borrow.rs` translates the consume's `PlaceExpr.projections` into a field-chain `Vec<String>` via `place_projection_as_field_chain` (returns `None` for any `Index` / `Range` segment so index-bearing consumes fall back to whole-root overlap), then walks `closure_capture_borrows[place.root]` and fires `OwnershipErrorKind::ClosureCaptureBorrowConflict` for every entry whose `path.projection` *bidirectionally prefix-overlaps* the consume chain — the shorter of the two projections must be a prefix of the longer. Disjoint sibling-path access (first differing segment exists within both) skips cleanly; whole-root consume against any captured sub-path overlaps trivially (empty consume chain is a prefix of every captured projection). The diagnostic names the consume site, the closure-creation span (in the `consume_span` secondary-label slot the borrow family uses), and the capture mode (`ref` / `mut ref`). New error code `E_CLOSURE_CAPTURE_BORROW_CONFLICT` plumbed through `src/cli.rs:858` alongside the existing `E_SLICE_BORROW_CONFLICT` / `E_CROSS_BORROW_CONFLICT` mappings. **Drain.** `drain_borrows_at_depth` (in `src/ownership/borrow.rs`) extended to also retire closure-capture borrows whose `scope_depth >= exit_depth`, mirroring the slice-borrow scope model — the borrow lives only as long as the scope holding the closure value. **Wiring point + chain-root discipline.** `check_expr_consuming` split into a public wrapper (fires the conflict check via `place_expr_root(expr)` after a Copy gate) and a private `check_expr_consuming_inner` that does the existing dispatch; the FieldAccess/TupleIndex arm's partial-move recursion into `object` now calls `check_expr_consuming_inner` directly so the conflict check fires *exactly once per chain* at the chain root. Without the discipline a chain like `let _x = u.history` would recurse through `Identifier("u")` with an empty-projection consume — bidirectional prefix overlap against any captured `u`-rooted path — false-firing even for disjoint sibling-path closures. The Copy gate at the wrapper site (`consume_expr_is_copy` helper, mirrors the per-variant Copy gate the Identifier / FieldAccess arms use) suppresses the conflict for Copy field/leaf consumes that don't actually move. `consume_named_binding` (used by the MethodCall `bare self` receiver-consume path) also fires the conflict against a synthesized whole-root `PlaceExpr` so a method-call consume through a captured root is caught. **Test surface** in `tests/ownership.rs` (12 new tests, immediately before "Step 7 sentinels: ref-captured value escape (E0508)" and right after the slice-2 block): `slice3_closure_ref_capture_permits_outer_sibling_field_consume` (**the slice-3 headline permissive case** — `let _f = || u.profile.name + 1; let _h = u.history;` accepts; path-aware check matches `["profile"]` vs `["history"]` at segment 0 → disjoint → no error); `slice3_closure_ref_capture_rejects_outer_whole_root_consume` (**the slice-3 headline rejection case**, spec test "outer-scope move of `u` while `u.name` is ref-captured is rejected" — empty consume chain prefix-overlaps the captured `["profile"]` → fires); `slice3_closure_mut_ref_capture_rejects_outer_whole_root_consume` (mut-ref leg of the same rule); `slice3_closure_ref_capture_rejects_equal_path_outer_consume` (`let _f = || u.profile.name + 1; let _p = u.profile;` — `["profile"]` is a prefix of `["profile", "name"]` → overlap → fires); `slice3_closure_ref_capture_permits_disjoint_nested_field_consume` (multi-segment disjointness — pins that the per-segment compare walks all the way through); `slice3_two_closures_over_disjoint_fields_compile_cleanly` (spec test "two closures over different fields of the same struct compile and run" — two precise per-path borrows on disjoint siblings coexist); `slice3_closure_borrow_drains_at_block_exit` + `slice3_borrow_drains_at_scope_holding_closure_value` (drain pins — inner-block-scoped closure exits and the outer consume of the previously-captured root accepts); `slice3_whole_root_capture_does_not_push_borrow_routes_through_rc_fallback` (narrowing pin — `let h = || cfg.id();` then `log(cfg);` accepts and `cfg` ends up in `rc_values` with `DirectReuseAfterConsume`); `slice3_own_capture_does_not_push_borrow_routes_through_rc_fallback` (Own-skip pin — `let _f = || take(o); let _u = o;` produces no slice-3 error and `o` ends up RC-promoted with `ClosureCaptureWithOuterUse`); `slice3_copy_field_outer_consume_does_not_fire_conflict_when_path_overlaps` (Copy-gate pin — `let _f = || o.x + 1; let _u = o.x;` accepts even though the consume's place exactly equals the captured path, because `o.x: i64` is Copy and the wrapper's Copy check suppresses); `slice3_diagnostic_carries_closure_span_as_secondary` (diagnostic shape pin — the closure-creation span lives in the `consume_span` secondary-label slot and the message names both `closure at line` and the capture mode `by `ref``). **Why a wrapper rather than a flag parameter on `check_expr_consuming`.** A flag would force every external caller (~20 sites across `expr_check.rs` + `block_stmt.rs`) to pass `true` explicitly and the FieldAccess recursion to pass `false`. The wrapper / inner split inverts the default — external callers keep the existing signature, only the single FieldAccess→object recursion needs the explicit `_inner` call. The chain-root discipline is enforced at one spot rather than maintained across many. **Why narrow to non-empty-projection captures.** The whole-root case is already covered by the RC-fallback dataflow, which RC-promotes the captured root and lets the outer consume coexist via Rc clones. Pushing a borrow for whole-root captures would either double-emit (slice 3 error + RC note) or require a coordination layer between the two passes — both worse than letting RC own the whole-root case and slice 3 own the path-precise case. The two surfaces partition cleanly: empty projection → RC; non-empty projection → slice 3.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — per-path mode inference shipped 2026-05-16.** New per-closure `closure_capture_path_modes: HashMap<SpanKey, Vec<(CapturePath, OwnershipMode)>>` field on `OwnershipChecker` and surfaced via `OwnershipCheckResult`. Entry list parallel to slice 1's `closure_capture_paths` (same span key, same order — pinned by `capture_path_mode_path_order_matches_capture_paths`) so slice 3's borrow checker can zip-iterate without re-sorting. New analyser `classify_capture_path_mutations` in `src/ownership/capture_body.rs` walks the closure body a second time and returns the subset of slice-1 paths whose places overlap any mutation event. Mutation events: assignment / compound-assign target (`StmtKind::Assign` / `CompoundAssign`); `mut`-marker call/method arg (`arg.mut_marker == true`); `mut ref self` method-call receiver (`method_call_receiver_is_mut_ref(expr)`). For each event the walker extracts the target's `(root, projection)` via `extract_target_place` (chain of `FieldAccess` / `TupleIndex` from a captured `Identifier`) and marks every recorded path whose `(root, projection)` *overlaps* the target as mutated. **Overlap is bidirectional** — `path.projection` is a prefix of `target.projection` (write to descendant mutates ancestors) OR `target.projection` is a prefix of `path.projection` (write to ancestor invalidates descendants); both cases require `MutRef` access at the closure boundary. Wired immediately after slice 1 in `src/ownership/expr_check.rs`'s `ExprKind::Closure` arm: for each path in the slice-1 set, mode = `Own` if the path has empty projection AND `states.get(&path.root)` is `ValueState::Moved` (only whole-root consume promotes to `Own` — sub-place consumes either re-route through the typechecker or surface as assign-target events); else `MutRef` if the path is in `path_mutations`; else `Ref`. **Purely additive — no existing checker path reads the new map yet.** Slice 3 (borrow-checker integration that lets outer-scope sibling-path access remain permitted while ancestor access is restricted) and slice 4 (codegen environment representation with one slot per captured path) consume this map. **Test surface** in `tests/ownership.rs` (12 new tests, immediately before "Step 7 sentinels: ref-captured value escape (E0508)" and right after the slice-1 block): `capture_path_mode_bare_identifier_read_is_ref` (ref-self method on captured root → whole-root path is `Ref`); `capture_path_mode_field_read_is_ref`; `capture_path_mode_field_assign_is_mut_ref` (mirrors per-name `capture_mutated_in_body_is_mut_ref` for the per-path surface); `capture_path_mode_disjoint_fields_independent_modes` (**the slice-2 headline** — `|| { u.age = 99; u.name + 1 }` yields `(u, ["age"])` `MutRef` AND `(u, ["name"])` `Ref` while per-name `u` collapses to `MutRef`; pins the disjointness the per-name view cannot express); `capture_path_mode_compound_assign_is_mut_ref` (`o.x += 1`); `capture_path_mode_method_mut_ref_self_commits_root_mut_ref` (mut-ref-self method call lifts whole-root path to `MutRef`); `capture_path_mode_method_ref_self_commits_root_ref` (paired with the mut-ref-self test to pin both legs of method-receiver mode discrimination); `capture_path_mode_consumed_whole_root_is_own` (by-value pass → `Own` — pins per-path matches per-name for the consume leg); `capture_path_mode_independent_roots_independent_modes` (`a.v = 10; b.v + 1` → `(a, ["v"])` `MutRef`, `(b, ["v"])` `Ref`); `capture_path_mode_ancestor_write_marks_whole_root` (`u.show(); u.age = 99` → both `(u, [])` AND `(u, ["age"])` are `MutRef`; pins the bidirectional-overlap rule — without ancestor-marking the whole-root capture would be falsely `Ref` while a sibling field assign is `MutRef`, and the closure's env-slot for the whole root would lack the mut access the body needs); `capture_path_mode_path_order_matches_capture_paths` (zip-order invariant); `capture_path_mode_modes_keyed_by_closure_expression_span` (per-closure not per-function — mirrors `closure_param_modes_keyed_by_closure_expression_span`). **Why a second walk rather than folding into slice 1's path walker.** Slice 1 enumerates *places touched*; slice 2 detects *mutation events* and matches them against the enumerated places. The two passes have different shapes — slice 1 commits roots-whole at stopping constructs (`Index`, `MethodCall`, `Deref`) regardless of mode; slice 2 only fires on actual mutation events. Folding them would tangle the place-enumeration recursion (which has to descend into sub-expressions normally to find nested captures) with the mutation-event detection (which is per-node, not per-recursion). Keeping slice 2 as a second walk makes both passes auditable independently and lets slice 3 add borrow-checker integration without re-touching either.

  - [x] **Slice 1 — capture-path enumeration shipped 2026-05-16.** New `CapturePath { root, projection }` data type in `src/ownership.rs` (empty `projection` = "captured whole"; non-empty = field-chain projection root-to-leaf, stored as `Vec<String>` so struct-field and tuple-position chains share one representation). New per-closure `closure_capture_paths: HashMap<SpanKey, Vec<CapturePath>>` field on `OwnershipChecker` and surfaced via `OwnershipCheckResult`. New analyser `classify_capture_body_paths` in `src/ownership/capture_body.rs` walks the closure body once and produces the path set: pure `FieldAccess` / `TupleIndex` chains rooted at a pre-live `Identifier` register their full projection (`u.profile.name` → `(u, ["profile", "name"])`, `t.0` → `(t, ["0"])`); stopping constructs (`Index`, `MethodCall` receiver, `Unary{Deref}` of a captured-rooted place) commit the root as captured whole and the walk descends into sub-expressions normally for nested captures. Wired into the existing closure-capture collection point in `src/ownership/expr_check.rs`'s `ExprKind::Closure` arm — runs alongside the per-name `closure_captures` populate, using the same `pre_live` set and closure-param-shadow filter so the two views stay in lockstep. Output is sorted lexicographically by `(root, projection)` for deterministic test pins. **Purely additive — no existing path through the checker reads the new map yet.** Per-path mode inference (slice 2), borrow-checker integration that lets outer-scope sibling-path access remain permitted (slice 3), and codegen environment representation with one slot per captured path (slice 4) consume this map without changing existing per-name semantics. **Test surface** in `tests/ownership.rs` (12 new tests, immediately before "Step 7 sentinels: ref-captured value escape (E0508)"): `capture_path_bare_identifier_is_whole_root`; `capture_path_single_field_chain_records_projection` (pins that `cfg.value` registers only `(cfg, ["value"])` — no whole-root extra entry); `capture_path_nested_field_chain_records_full_projection`; `capture_path_disjoint_fields_under_same_root_record_distinct_paths` (`u.name + u.age` → `{(u, ["age"]), (u, ["name"])}` — the foundation slice 3 will use to accept outer-scope sibling access of `u.history`); `capture_path_index_commits_root_whole`; `capture_path_method_call_receiver_commits_root_whole` (pins that method call on a captured root is a stopping construct — the analyser cannot tell which fields a method touches without inter-procedural inspection); `capture_path_index_into_field_chain_commits_root_whole` (`items[0].field` — the `Index` arm commits `(items, [])` and the surrounding `FieldAccess` does not extend the path); `capture_path_method_call_on_field_chain_commits_root_whole` (intermediate `profile` projection NOT recorded as a separate path since it was an in-progress chain when the stopping construct fired); `capture_path_multiple_roots_each_recorded_independently`; `capture_path_excludes_shadowed_outer_name` (closure-param `x` shadows outer `x` → empty path-set, parity with `closure_captures`'s exclusion); `capture_path_unreferenced_outer_name_produces_no_path`; `capture_path_tuple_index_extends_projection` (`t.0` extends projection with stringified index `"0"`). **Why a separate walker rather than extending `classify_capture_body_uses`.** The per-name walker tracks read/mutated/consumed signals per *binding*; the path walker tracks distinct *places* (root + projection chain) with different stopping rules (index/method/deref commit-to-whole has no analogue in the per-name pass). Conflating two analyses with different inputs and stopping rules would make slice 2's per-path mode inference (which runs the use-predicate scan independently per path) harder to layer cleanly — the current shape lets slice 2 keep using the existing `CaptureBodyUsage` per name AND consume the path set, deciding per-path modes by intersecting the two views.

- [~] **Generic associated types (GATs) — `type Assoc[T]` declarations + `T.Assoc[X]` projections.** Parser surface (slice 1) shipped 2026-05-16; resolver wiring (slice 3) shipped 2026-05-17; typechecker / coherence / bound-enforcement slices (4–9) remain. Implement the spec in `design.md § Associated Types in Traits > Generic associated types (GATs)`. Builds on the already-shipped non-generic associated-types implementation (line ~793).

  - [x] **Slice 1 — parser surface shipped 2026-05-16.** Spec sentence honoured: *"extend the trait-body `type` declaration grammar to accept an optional generic parameter list `[P1, P2, ...]` after the associated-type name, with optional bounds (`type Mapped[U]: Trait`) and an optional `where` clause; extend the impl-block `type` binding grammar identically (`type Mapped[U] = Vec[U]`); reject effect-polymorphism on the GAT itself (`type Mapped[U, with E]`) with a focused diagnostic suggesting the carrying-method form."* **AST extension** in `src/ast/items.rs`: `AssocTypeDecl` and `AssocTypeBinding` both gain `generic_params: Option<GenericParams>` and `where_clause: Option<WhereClause>`. The legacy non-generic shape (`type Item;` / `type Item = i64;`) parses unchanged with both new fields set to `None` — so every existing consumer that ignores the GAT shape works without touching pattern bindings. The two enum carriers `TraitItem::AssocType(...)` and `ImplItem::AssocType(...)` are now `Box<AssocTypeDecl>` / `Box<AssocTypeBinding>` to keep clippy's `large_enum_variant` lint quiet against the `TraitItem::Method(Box<TraitMethod>)` / `ImplItem::Method(Box<Function>)` siblings — auto-deref absorbs the change at every existing read site (formatter, resolver, typechecker, effectchecker, codegen, span_visitor) so the box is invisible to consumers. **Parser wiring** in `src/parser/items_trait.rs`: both `parse_assoc_type_decl` and `parse_assoc_type_binding` now call `parse_optional_generic_params()` immediately after the name and `parse_optional_where_clause()` immediately before the closing semicolon, reusing the same `[T, const N: i64]` / `where T: Trait` machinery that function and struct signatures already consume — single source of truth for generic-param grammar, bound parsing, and where-constraint shapes. **Effect-polymorphism rejection** lives in a new `reject_gat_effect_params(gp, role)` helper in the same impl block. It consults the parsed `GenericParams.effect_params` and, when non-empty, emits one focused `E_GAT_EFFECT_PARAM` diagnostic naming the full effect-param list (so `[U, with E, F]` produces `with E, F`, unambiguously steering the rewrite) and the offending site role (`"declaration"` for trait-side, `"binding"` for impl-side, threaded as the `role` parameter so the user can tell which side fired without inspecting the span). The suggestion text says "move the `with <list>` clause to the carrying method's generic-parameter list instead" — the spec's verbatim guidance. Diagnostic anchored at `gp.span` (the bracketed generic-param-list span); the parser does not retain per-effect-param spans so this is the precise-as-available position. The rejection runs *after* `parse_optional_generic_params()` succeeds, not in the middle of the parameter-list loop — preserving recovery: the GAT's generic-param list is fully consumed even when invalid, so the rest of the trait/impl body continues to parse. **Test surface** in `tests/parser.rs` (12 new tests immediately before `test_trait_method_with_generic_params`): `gat_slice1_trait_assoc_type_with_single_generic_param` (basic — `type Mapped[U];` records `generic_params = Some({U})`); `gat_slice1_trait_assoc_type_with_multiple_generic_params` (`type Mapped[L, R];` — multi-param shape); `gat_slice1_trait_assoc_type_with_bound_on_param` (`type Mapped[U: Clone];` — bound on the GAT's own parameter); `gat_slice1_trait_assoc_type_with_outer_bound` (`type Mapped[U]: Display + Clone;` — bound on the GAT declaration itself, distinct from per-parameter bound, will be slice-7 enforcement target); `gat_slice1_trait_assoc_type_with_where_clause` (`type Mapped[U] where U: Clone;` — `where` clause attaches to the declaration); `gat_slice1_trait_non_generic_assoc_type_unchanged` (regression pin — the legacy `type Item;` form still parses with `generic_params = None`, `where_clause = None`); `gat_slice1_impl_assoc_type_binding_with_generic_param` (**slice-1 headline for the impl side** — `impl Functor for Vec[T] { type Mapped[U] = Vec[U]; }` matches the design.md example verbatim); `gat_slice1_impl_assoc_type_binding_with_where_clause` (impl-side `where` clause on the binding); `gat_slice1_impl_non_generic_assoc_type_binding_unchanged` (regression pin — legacy `type Item = i64;` form unchanged); `gat_slice1_trait_assoc_type_rejects_effect_param` (negative pin — `type Mapped[U, with E];` produces `E_GAT_EFFECT_PARAM` mentioning `with E`, naming the `declaration` role, and steering at the carrying-method form); `gat_slice1_impl_assoc_type_binding_rejects_effect_param` (negative pin, impl-side — same shape but `binding` role); `gat_slice1_multiple_effect_params_all_named_in_diagnostic` (pin that the diagnostic names the *full* effect-param list — `with E, F`, not just `with E` — so the suggested rewrite is unambiguous). **Why an `Option<GenericParams>` rather than `GenericParams` with empty params.** The `None` discriminant is the user-visible "no `[…]` written" signal that downstream slices need: slice 2's resolver must treat the bare and generic forms differently (only the GAT form opens a new generic-parameter scope on the RHS), slice 4's `Type::AssocProjection` extension distinguishes `T.Item` (no args) from `T.Mapped[X]` (with args) by the presence of args, and slice 5's parameter substitution short-circuits to a direct lookup when the binding has no generic params. Encoding "no GAT" as `Some(GenericParams { params: vec![], effect_params: vec![], span })` would force every downstream consumer to distinguish between `vec![]` and `None` at every read site — `Option` is the right shape and matches every other generic-params field across the AST (`StructDef`, `Function`, `TraitDef`, `TraitMethod`, `MarkerTraitDef`, `TraitAliasDef`, `EffectResourceDecl`, `ImplBlock`). **What slice 1 does *not* do.** No resolver wiring (slice 3), no typechecker projection-with-args type (slice 4), no impl-site bound enforcement (slice 7) — the new fields are purely structural at this slice. Existing typechecker / resolver passes ignore the new fields because the legacy shape (no `[…]`, no `where`) still parses to `None` and those passes never read `Option<GenericParams>` / `Option<WhereClause>` on assoc-type nodes. Slice 2 (AST extension confirmation; the spec listed it separately but the AST work landed inside slice 1 — the parser couldn't add the fields without them existing) is therefore subsumed. (2) AST — extend the existing `AssociatedType { name, bound, .. }` node with `generic_params: Vec<GenericParam>` and `where_clause: Option<WhereClause>`. (3) Resolver — bind the GAT's own generic parameters in the right-hand side scope of the impl binding and in the bound expression of the trait declaration; the bound and `where` clauses see those parameters. (4) Type system — extend the existing `Type::AssocProjection { param, assoc }` to `Type::AssocProjection { param, assoc, args: Vec<Type> }` (or add a parallel `AssocProjectionGeneric` variant) so projections like `F.Mapped[i64]` carry their type arguments. (5) Typechecker resolution — when resolving `T.Assoc[X1, X2, ...]` at a call site, locate the trait that provides `Assoc` (via the bounds on `T`), look up the impl's binding for that `(type_name, assoc_name)`, and substitute the GAT's parameters with the supplied arguments before yielding the concrete type. The existing `impl_assoc_types` map needs to key by `(type_name, assoc_name)` and store a `Type` template referencing the GAT's parameters; resolution applies a parameter substitution. (6) Coherence — the existing "one impl per trait per type" rule covers GATs unchanged, since the GAT binding is part of the impl. (7) Bound enforcement — at every impl site, for every legal instantiation of the GAT's parameters, the binding's right-hand side must satisfy the GAT's declared bound (`type Mapped[U]: Trait` requires the impl's `Mapped[U]` choice to satisfy `Trait` for arbitrary `U` — usually proven by structural means: if `Mapped[U] = Vec[U]` and `Vec[U]: Trait` is provable from `T`'s bounds, accepted). (8) Where-clause integration — `where F.Mapped[i64]: FromIterator[i64]` desugars into the standard bound-set checking once GAT projection is wired through the constraint solver. (9) Negative-space coverage — the typechecker rejects two impls of the same trait for the same type with different `Mapped` definitions (existing coherence error path); rejects `for<X> T.Mapped[X]: Send` syntax (parser doesn't accept `for<...>` in v1, which is the right shape). Test coverage (typechecker, Phase 5.2): `trait Functor { type Mapped[U]; fn map[U](self, f: Fn(...) -> U) -> Self.Mapped[U] }` parses and checks; impl on `Vec[T]` with `type Mapped[U] = Vec[U]` checks; call `vec.map(|x| x * 2)` returns `Vec[i64]` with the expected type when `T = i64`; `where F.Mapped[i64]: FromIterator[i64]` constraint resolves; bound `type Mapped[U]: Trait` enforced at impl site (an impl whose `Mapped[U]` does not satisfy the bound is rejected with the typed diagnostic); two impls of the same trait for the same type with different `Mapped` definitions rejected at coherence; `type Mapped[U, with E]` parser-rejected with the focused diagnostic; `for<X>` higher-ranked syntax remains a parser error. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features).

  - [x] **Slice 2 — AST extension.** Subsumed into slice 1: the parser could not add `generic_params` / `where_clause` fields to `AssocTypeDecl` / `AssocTypeBinding` without them existing on the AST, so the AST extension landed alongside the parser surface. No separate work item.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — Resolver wiring shipped 2026-05-17.** Trait-side (`TraitItem::AssocType(assoc)`) and impl-side (`ImplItem::AssocType(binding)`) handlers in `src/resolver/resolve_items.rs` now push a `ScopeKind::Block` scope when `generic_params.is_some()`, define the GAT's parameters via `define_generic_params`, resolve the bound list / `where` clause / RHS type inside that scope, then pop. Non-generic shapes (`type Item;` / `type Item = i64;`) skip the scope push, preserving existing behavior. Bounds and where-clauses on non-generic forms are now also resolved (was no-op before slice 3) — `type Item: Display;` records `Display` in the resolution map when it's in scope, with the silent-on-unknown-trait behavior of `resolve_trait_bound` preserved. **Test surface** in `tests/resolver.rs` (8 new tests at end-of-file): `gat_slice3_trait_assoc_type_generic_param_registered_as_typeparam` (pins that `U` exists as `SymbolKind::TypeParam` in `all_symbols()`); `gat_slice3_trait_assoc_type_non_generic_form_registers_no_param` (regression: `type Item;` adds no new symbol); `gat_slice3_trait_assoc_type_param_not_visible_in_sibling_method` (negative: `U` from `type Mapped[U]` is unresolved in a sibling `fn other() -> U;`); `gat_slice3_impl_assoc_type_binding_rhs_resolves_param` (headline: `type Mapped[U] = Wrapper[U]` resolves clean); `gat_slice3_impl_assoc_type_binding_rhs_errors_on_undefined_param` (negative: `type Mapped[U] = Wrapper[Q]` errors on `Q`, confirming the new scope doesn't swallow all names); `gat_slice3_impl_assoc_type_binding_param_not_visible_in_sibling_method` (impl-side scope-pop pin); `gat_slice3_trait_assoc_type_with_where_clause_resolves` (where-clause sees GAT param); `gat_slice3_impl_assoc_type_binding_with_where_clause_resolves` (impl-side where-clause sees binding's GAT param). **What slice 3 does *not* do.** Type-system projection-with-args (slice 4), typechecker resolution + parameter substitution (slice 5), impl-site bound enforcement (slice 7), constraint-solver integration of GAT-projection where-clauses (slice 8) — all downstream. The GAT param is now a resolver-visible symbol; the typechecker still treats projections as their non-generic form pending slice 4.

  - [x] **Slice 4 — Type system `AssocProjection` extension shipped 2026-05-17.** Extended `Type::AssocProjection` with `args: Vec<Type>` (chose the field-extension shape over the parallel `AssocProjectionGeneric` variant — the non-generic form is just `args: vec![]`, so every consumer handles one arm not two; the `args` field walks alongside the existing `Named.args` shape consumers already understand). **Type-side changes** in `src/typechecker/types.rs`: `Type::AssocProjection` carries the new `args` field with a doc-comment spelling out the slice 4 → slice 5 boundary (slice 4 carries args through substitution / free-var search / display; slice 5 does the actual binding-RHS lookup + parameter substitution). `type_display` renders `F.Item` unchanged (empty args = no brackets) and `F.Mapped[i64]` with the args inside `[...]` matching the surface syntax.   - [x] **Slice 5 — Typechecker resolution + parameter substitution shipped 2026-05-17.** Wires the actual GAT-projection resolution path: when `<concrete>.Mapped[X1, X2, ...]` reaches `resolve_assoc_projections`, the resolver builds a substitution map from both impl-side params (struct's `generic_params` zipped with the projection's `receiver_args`) AND GAT-side params (entry's `gat_params` zipped with the projection's own `args`), then applies the substitution in one pass against the stored template — yielding the concrete type (`Wrapper[i64]` for `Doubler.Mapped[i64]` with binding `type Mapped[U] = Wrapper[U]`; `Pair[String, i64]` for `Wrapper.Mapped[i64]` with `receiver_args = [String]` and binding `type Mapped[U] = Pair[T, U]`). **Env storage extension** in `src/typechecker/env.rs`: new `ImplAssocTypeEntry { ty: Type, gat_params: Vec<String> }` wraps the previous bare `Type` value; `impl_assoc_types` is keyed `(type_name, assoc_name)` as before. `gat_params` is empty for non-generic bindings (`type Item = i64`, the existing prelude intrinsics) and lists the GAT's own parameter names for generic bindings (`type Mapped[U] = ...` → `["U"]`). **Binding-RHS lowering** in `src/typechecker/items.rs::check_impl_block`: the AssocType binding handler now extends the generic scope passed to `lower_type_expr` with the binding's own `generic_params` so RHS references like the `U` in `Wrapper[U]` lower as `Type::TypeParam("U")` instead of falling through as `Named { name: "U", args: [] }`. Both impl-side and GAT-side TypeParams are uniformly substitutable in the stored template; the resolver distinguishes them via the `gat_params` list. **Type structural change** in `src/typechecker/types.rs`: new `Type::AssocProjection.receiver_args: Vec<Type>` carries the resolved receiver's args (e.g., `[String]` for a `Wrapper[String]` receiver) once `substitute_type_params` has solved the receiver TypeParam. Empty pre-substitution and for non-generic receivers. The split between `param` (bare type name) and `receiver_args` (the receiver's args) is what lets the resolver look up the impl entry by bare name AND substitute the impl-block's generic params, while the projection's own `args` substitute the GAT params. `type_display` renders `param<receiver_args>.assoc[args]` when receiver_args is non-empty (e.g., `Wrapper<String>.Mapped[i64]`), keeping the non-generic surface (`F.Item`) and the bare-projection-with-args (`F.Mapped[i64]`) unchanged. **Receiver capture** in `substitute_type_params` (`src/typechecker/inference.rs`): when the projection's outer TypeParam is solved to a concrete type, the resolver now extracts the bare name into `param` and the args into `receiver_args` — rather than the pre-slice-5 `type_display(concrete)` shape which produced `"Wrapper<String>"` and failed the bare-name lookup. Handles `Type::Named` / `Shared` / `Rc` / `Arc` shapes with appropriate base-name + arg-list extraction; non-Named fallbacks keep the pre-existing `type_display` behaviour and empty receiver_args. **Two-sided substitution** in `resolve_assoc_projections` (`src/typechecker/lowering.rs`): the lookup-hit branch now constructs a `HashMap<String, SubstValue>` from BOTH (a) the struct's `generic_params` paired with the projection's `receiver_args` — substituting impl-side TypeParams like the `T` in `Pair[T, U]` against the receiver's args — AND (b) the entry's own `gat_params` paired with the projection's `args` — substituting GAT-side TypeParams like the `U` against the projection's instantiation. The combined map is applied to `entry.ty` via `substitute_type_params`; the result is recursively re-resolved so a substituted template that itself contains an unresolved projection gets resolved in the same pass. **Walker backfill** for the new `receiver_args` field: `find_unbound_type_param` walks into `receiver_args` after the outer-param-in-scope check; the `collect` and `substitute` helpers inside `instantiate_signature_with_fresh_vars` walk `receiver_args` symmetrically with `args` (a no-op for parser-produced signatures where `receiver_args` is always empty, but it keeps the structure stable for synthesised types that may carry pre-resolved receivers). **`element_type_of` migration**: switched from `item_ty` direct read to `entry.ty` access — transparent change, the existing `Vec[T].iter()` element-typing path is unchanged. **Test surface (10 unit tests in `src/typechecker/tests.rs::gat_slice5_assoc_projection_resolution_tests` + 3 integration tests in `tests/typechecker.rs`).** Unit tests: `impl_assoc_types_entry_records_gat_params_for_generic_binding` (THE KEY STORAGE PIN — registers an impl with `type Mapped[U] = Wrapper[U]`, asserts entry's `gat_params == ["U"]`, asserts template is `Wrapper[TypeParam(U)]` not `Wrapper[Named(U,[])]` — pins both the gat_params recording AND the binding-RHS lowering fix together), `impl_assoc_types_entry_has_empty_gat_params_for_non_generic_binding` (regression — `type Output = i64;` keeps `gat_params: []`), `resolve_substitutes_gat_param_from_projection_args` (headline — `Doubler.Mapped[i64]` with template `Wrapper[U]` resolves to `Wrapper[i64]`), `resolve_substitutes_both_impl_and_gat_params` (THE KEY RESOLUTION PIN — `Wrapper.Mapped[i64]` with `receiver_args =   - [x] **Slice 6 — Coherence regression pin shipped 2026-05-17.** Three regression tests in `tests/typechecker.rs` pinning that the existing impl-overlap diagnostic (`TypeErrorKind::ConflictingImpl`, emitted from `env_build.rs::impl_overlap_exists`) covers the GAT case unchanged — the GAT binding is part of the impl block and contributes no extra coherence rule. **No production-code change** per the spec. **Scope nuance discovered during implementation.** The slice 6 spec sentence assumes "two impls of the same trait for the same type" are rejected by the existing diagnostic. That diagnostic actually fires for two of three duplicate-impl shapes today: (a) two specialized impls on the same concrete instantiation (`impl Functor for Wrapper[i32]` × 2), and (b) generic-on-name vs specialized (`impl[T] Functor for Wrapper[T]` + `impl Functor for Wrapper[i32]`). It does NOT fire for two fully-concrete duplicates with empty target args (`impl Functor for Doubler` × 2) — that shape is the documented "pre-existing trait-coherence concerns left unchanged" carve-out in `env_build.rs::impl_overlap_exists`, applying equally to non-GAT impls. Slice 6 pins the GAT case under the surfaces where the diagnostic already fires; the third shape is a pre-existing gap, not GAT-introduced, and remains untouched per the slice's "no production-code change" boundary. **Test surface (3 tests in `tests/typechecker.rs`).** `test_gat_slice6_duplicate_gat_impls_on_concrete_instantiation_rejected` (two `impl Functor for Wrapper[i32]` with different `Mapped[U]` RHS — `Vec[U]` vs `Set[U]` — must trip ConflictingImpl); `test_gat_slice6_duplicate_gat_impls_rejected_even_with_identical_binding` (two `impl Functor for Wrapper[i32]` with IDENTICAL `Mapped[U] = Vec[U]` — still ConflictingImpl, pinning that the rule is at the impl level, not the binding level); `test_gat_slice6_generic_and_specialized_gat_impls_rejected` (`impl[T] Functor for Wrapper[T]` + `impl Functor for Wrapper[i32]` — generic-vs-specialized overlap fires regardless of GAT binding). All three pass against the slice 5 baseline with zero `env_build.rs` / `typechecker.rs` source changes — confirming the slice 5 entry wrapper (`ImplAssocTypeEntry` with `gat_params` and the lowered RHS template) is structurally compatible with the existing coherence path. Slice 4 + slice 5 tests continue to pass.

  - [x] **Slice 7 — Impl-site bound enforcement shipped 2026-05-17.** At every impl site, for every legal instantiation of the GAT's parameters, the binding's right-hand side must satisfy the GAT's declared bound. The check fires at the AssocType binding registration site in `src/typechecker/items.rs::check_impl_block` for every `type Name[...]: Trait` declaration carried on the trait's matching `AssocTypeDecl`. **Implementation** in `src/typechecker/items.rs::check_impl_block`: builds a `HashMap<String, Vec<TraitBound>>` once per impl block by walking `program.items` for the trait declaration matching `imp.trait_name` and collecting each `TraitItem::AssocType` decl's `bounds` keyed by assoc-type name. The binding loop then enforces the bounds per binding: for each bound trait, calls `self.gat_rhs_satisfies_bound(&bound_ty, &bound_trait)` on the lowered RHS template; failures emit `error[E_GAT_BOUND_NOT_SATISFIED]: binding \`type Name = <rhs>\` does not satisfy declared GAT bound \`Name: Trait\`` at the binding span, naming both the GAT and the missing trait so the reader knows exactly which `: Trait` clause the binding broke. **Structural-proof helper** `gat_rhs_satisfies_bound` lives in `src/typechecker/bounds.rs` (the natural home alongside `validate_inline_generic_bounds` / `validate_where_clause`). Three proof paths: (1) **TypeParam RHS** (`type Mapped = T` with impl `[T: Trait]`) — discharges via the impl's `enclosing_bounds[T]`, accepting if any bound matches `Trait` directly OR via the supertrait closure (`env.supertrait_closure_traits` reused from the existing supertrait-walk infrastructure); (2) **concrete-head RHS** (`Foo`, `Vec[U]`, `i64`, etc.) — routes through `type_satisfies_bound` (promoted from `fn` to `pub(super)` in `src/typechecker/exprs.rs` for cross-module reuse) → which consults built-in `type_supports_*` for the derive-recognised traits (Hash/Eq/PartialEq/Ord/PartialOrd/Display) and the impl table (with `impl_args_match`'s "stored-empty matches any" rule) for user-defined traits — so a generic-on-name impl like `impl[T] Trait for Foo[T]` discharges `Foo[U]: Trait` for arbitrary `U`; (3) **anything else** (function types, raw pointers, type variables, the `Type::TypeVar` shape) returns `false` conservatively — the diagnostic at the binding site surfaces the mismatch. **Cross-module visibility change.** `TypeChecker::type_satisfies_bound` (`src/typechecker/exprs.rs:849`) was a private `fn`; slice 7 promotes it to `pub(super)` so the cross-module call from `bounds.rs::gat_rhs_satisfies_bound` resolves.
