The only previous caller was the discharge engine inside `exprs.rs` itself; the new caller is the slice 7 helper. **Test surface (8 integration tests in `tests/typechecker.rs`).** `test_gat_slice7_concrete_rhs_satisfies_bound_accepted` (headline — `type Mapped[U] = Foo` where `Foo` impls `Show`, bound `: Show` accepts), `test_gat_slice7_non_satisfying_rhs_rejected` (THE KEY NEGATIVE PIN — `type Mapped[U] = Bar` where `Bar` does NOT impl `Show`, expects `E_GAT_BOUND_NOT_SATISFIED` naming Mapped + Show), `test_gat_slice7_typeparam_rhs_satisfies_via_impl_bound_accepted` (`type Mapped = T` with impl `[T: Show]` — TypeParam path discharges via enclosing_bounds), `test_gat_slice7_typeparam_rhs_without_impl_bound_rejected` (symmetric negative — impl `[T]` with no Show bound, rejected), `test_gat_slice7_unbounded_gat_accepts_any_rhs` (regression — when the GAT decl has no `: Trait` clause, slice 7 is a no-op and any RHS is accepted), `test_gat_slice7_non_gat_binding_with_bound_satisfied` / `test_gat_slice7_non_gat_binding_with_bound_rejected` (the non-generic associated-type shape `type Item: Show` composes uniformly with the GAT enforcement path — both arms pinned), `test_gat_slice7_supertrait_satisfies_bound` (structural proof via supertrait closure — RHS impls `ShowPlus: Show`, slice 7 accepts because the supertrait walk reaches `Show`). All slices 4-6 tests + the 21 pre-existing assoc-type / projection tests continue to pass. **Bound-trait scope: user-defined + impl-table-registered builtins.** The slice 7 surface is the impl-table-driven path; built-in derive-only traits like `Clone` are recognised by the parser (`is_known_trait`) but are not yet registered as impl-table entries, so a bound `: Clone` on a GAT would conservatively reject every concrete RHS today. Tightening Clone (and the other derive-only-builtin traits in `bounds.rs::DERIVE_ONLY_BUILTINS`) to participate in `type_satisfies_bound` is out-of-scope for slice 7 — it's a broader change to the derive-recognition surface that bundles with the slice 8 constraint-solver work, where `where`-clause-driven proofs (`where F.Mapped[i64]: FromIterator[i64]`) also land. **What slice 7 does *not* do.** No GAT-param-with-inline-bound enforcement (the GAT's own params don't take inline bounds in v1 — `type Mapped[U: Trait]` is parsed but the inline-bound-on-GAT-param surface is post-v1 / P1); no `where`-clause integration on the GAT decl (slice 8 — `type Mapped[U] where U: Trait` parses and resolves but the predicate is not yet discharged at impl-site); no derive-only-builtin enforcement (carry-forward to a follow-up that promotes Clone/Copy/Debug/etc. into impl-table-aware surfaces). The structural-proof rule is the v1 minimum; the constraint-solver work in slice 8 will tighten the proof scope further.

  - [x] **Slice 8a — Where-clause projection bound discharge shipped 2026-05-17.** `where F.Mapped[i64]: FromIterator[i64]` parses as a new where-clause variant, lands in the resolver / typechecker validation surface, and discharges at call sites by substituting the call's type-arg solutions into the projection LHS, resolving via `resolve_assoc_projections`, and proving the resolved RHS implements each declared bound. **AST extension** in `src/ast/types.rs`: new `WhereConstraint::ProjectionBound { projection: TypeExpr, bounds: Vec<TraitBound>, span: Span }` variant alongside the existing `TypeBound` / `AssocTypeEq` / `ConstPredicate`. Distinct from `TypeBound` because the LHS is a full projection type-expression (`F.Mapped[i64]`) rather than a bare type-parameter name. Empty-`generic_args` projections on the LHS (`T.Item: Trait`) compose uniformly through the same variant. **Parser** in `src/parser/generics.rs::parse_optional_where_clause`: after consuming the first identifier and a `.`, the parser reads the assoc-type name + an optional `[args]` bracket list, then dispatches on the next token — `=` keeps the existing `AssocTypeEq` path (rejecting projection-LHS args on equality with a focused diagnostic since `T.Assoc[args] = Type` has no v1 semantics), `:` builds the new `ProjectionBound` by re-assembling the receiver + assoc segments into a 2-segment `TypeExpr::Path` and parsing the bound list with `parse_trait_bound` separated by `+`. Other shapes fall through to the existing diagnostic. **Resolver** in `src/resolver/resolve_refs.rs::resolve_where_clause`: the new arm calls `resolve_type_expr(projection)` so the receiver type-param resolves and any GAT arg types record in the resolution map, then walks `bounds` through `resolve_trait_bound` so the trait reference is recorded. **Typechecker decl-time validation** in `src/typechecker/bounds.rs::validate_where_clause`: the new arm lowers the projection type-expression against the function's generic scope (which both validates the receiver is in scope via the standard lowering diagnostics and surfaces any GAT arity issues), then walks `bounds` for trait-alias rejection + unknown-trait-name diagnostic mirroring the `TypeBound` arm's surface. **Typechecker call-site discharge** in `src/typechecker/exprs.rs::discharge_projection_bounds` (new sibling to `discharge_type_bounds`): builds a `HashMap<String, SubstValue>` from `solutions` and walks each `ProjectionBound`. For each constraint, lowers the projection against `solutions.keys()` as the scope (so the receiver lowers as a `Type::AssocProjection` with the receiver-name as `param`), substitutes the solutions via `substitute_type_params` (which captures the receiver's bare name + args into the projection's `param` + `receiver_args` fields), resolves through `resolve_assoc_projections` against `env.impl_assoc_types`, and checks each bound via `type_satisfies_bound`. Misses emit `error[E_WHERE_CLAUSE_PROJECTION_BOUND_NOT_SATISFIED]: projection bound \`<projection>: <trait>\` is not satisfied; resolved projection type \`<rhs>\` does not implement \`<trait>\``. Post-substitution projections that remain unresolvable (receiver still a `TypeParam`, impl table miss, propagating `TypeVar` / `Error` shapes) are skipped silently — upstream unsolved-T / generic-on-name diagnostics surface those. **`has_generic` override extension** in `check_call_args_with_substitution_full`: the slice 3c override that forces full instantiate+unify+discharge when a where-clause carries any `ConstPredicate` now also fires on `ProjectionBound` — without this, a function with no generic params / non-generic return / sole `where F.Mapped[i64]: Trait` clause would hit the non-generic early-return path and skip discharge entirely. The `discharge_type_bounds` callsite at the bottom of the function now calls `discharge_projection_bounds` after it so the two run as siblings on the same `where_clause` walk. **Module-boundary visibility.** `substitute_type_params` and `SubstValue` are now imported into `src/typechecker/exprs.rs` (previously consumed only inside `inference.rs` / `lowering.rs`); no signatures changed, just the imports widen. **Other crate touch-ups** (mechanical / no semantic change): `src/codegen/mono.rs`, `src/effectchecker/bounds.rs`, `src/typechecker/env.rs::env_build`, `src/typechecker/lowering.rs` (the `collect_param_bounds` walk) — all use `if let WhereConstraint::TypeBound { ... } = c else { continue }` so the new variant naturally falls through. `src/formatter/items.rs` adds an explicit arm that renders the projection LHS + `: Trait + ...` to keep the formatter exhaustive. **Test surface (9 integration tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::gat_slice8a_*`).** `test_gat_slice8a_projection_bound_accepted_when_resolved_rhs_satisfies` (THE HEADLINE — `where F.Mapped[i64]: Collector` accepted at the call site by inferring `F = V` from the argument, resolving `V.Mapped[i64]` to `Vec[i64]` via the binding `type Mapped[U] = Vec[U]`, discharging `Vec[i64]: Collector` via the generic-on-name `impl[T] Collector for Vec[T]`), `test_gat_slice8a_projection_bound_rejected_when_resolved_rhs_misses` (THE KEY NEGATIVE PIN — the binding resolves to `Bar` with no `Collector` impl, expects `E_WHERE_CLAUSE_PROJECTION_BOUND_NOT_SATISFIED` naming Collector), `test_gat_slice8a_projection_bound_unbound_receiver_skipped` (regression — when the caller forwards `G` to `use_it` without binding to a concrete type, the discharge skips silently rather than firing a false positive), `test_gat_slice8a_projection_bound_validates_trait_name_at_decl` (decl-time pin — unknown trait names in the projection bound emit the standard unknown-trait diagnostic from `validate_where_clause`), `test_gat_slice8a_projection_bound_with_generic_args_on_trait` (mirrors the exact spec example `where F.Mapped[i64]: FromIterator[i64]` — the trait carries its own generic args; recognition keys off the trait name today, mirroring `discharge_type_bounds`), `test_gat_slice8a_non_generic_projection_bound_accepted` (the degenerate-GAT shape `T.Item: Collector` composes uniformly with the discharge path), `test_gat_slice8a_multiple_projection_bounds_all_discharge` / `test_gat_slice8a_multiple_projection_bounds_one_misses` (multi-bound surface `: Collector + Show` — both must satisfy; positive accepts, negative fires the focused diagnostic on the missing trait), `test_gat_slice8a_slices_4_through_7_still_pass_regression` (regression pin — slices 4-7 examples continue to typecheck against the new variant). All slices 4-7 tests + the 21 pre-existing assoc-type / projection tests continue to pass. **Single-arg explicit-generic-args call shape note.** The headline test uses argument-position inference (`use_it(V {})`) rather than explicit-generic-args (`use_it[V]()`) because the parser's `lookahead_generic_args_call` requires a top-level comma in the bracket list to disambiguate from `Index { object, index }` — single-arg generic calls on free functions parse as `Index`-shaped and don't route through `infer_explicit_generic_args_call`. This is pre-existing parser behaviour, not a slice 8a issue; arg-position inference exercises the same `discharge_projection_bounds` code path. **What slice 8a does *not* do.** No derive-only-builtin trait participation in `type_satisfies_bound` (slice 8b carry-forward (a)); no GAT-decl `where`-clause discharge at impl-site (slice 8b carry-forward (b)); no inline-bound-on-GAT-param enforcement at projection-resolution time (slice 8b carry-forward (c)); no tightening of `types_compatible` on `AssocProjection` (slice 8b/c carry-forward (d)). The discharge surface is the call-site path against `FunctionSig.where_clause`; non-function declarations (struct / enum / impl-block where-clauses) carry `ProjectionBound` through resolution but slice 8a does not extend the discharge to impl-block instantiations — that lands under slice 8b alongside the GAT-decl where-clause discharge.

  - [x] **Slice 8b — Slice 7 carry-forwards (a) + (b) + (c) shipped 2026-05-17.** Three of the four slice 7 carry-forwards land together; carry-forward (d) (`types_compatible` tightening on `AssocProjection`) is deferred to slice 8c because it requires constraint-solver plumbing beyond the slice 8 surface. **(a) Derive-only-builtin trait participation in `type_satisfies_bound`** (`src/typechecker/exprs.rs:type_satisfies_bound`, `src/typechecker/derives.rs`). The built-in-switch in `type_satisfies_bound` now routes `Clone` / `Copy` / `Debug` through `type_supports_clone` / `is_type_copy` / `type_supports_debug` — Clone and Debug are new helpers added in `derives.rs` mirroring the pattern of `type_supports_hash` / `type_supports_display` (primitive coverage + named-type derived-traits lookup + built-in collection delegation when `args` all satisfy + supertrait closure path via `env.has_impl`); Copy reuses the pre-existing `is_type_copy` helper. With these wired, a `: Clone` / `: Copy` / `: Debug` bound on a GAT now discharges through slice 7's structural-proof path for concrete types that carry the corresponding derive (or that are primitives). Pre-slice-8b a `: Clone` bound conservatively rejected every concrete RHS because Clone has no `env.impls` entry; the v1 surface is now consistent across the seven discharge-recognised traits (Hash / Eq / PartialEq / Ord / PartialOrd / Display / Clone / Copy / Debug). **(b) GAT decl `where`-clause discharge** + **(c) inline-bound-on-GAT-param** are wired together via a single helper `discharge_gat_decl_constraints` in `src/typechecker/exprs.rs` called from `discharge_projection_bounds` after the projection is substituted. **Storage extension** in `src/typechecker/env.rs::ImplAssocTypeEntry`: two new fields — `param_bound_traits: Vec<Vec<String>>` (position-aligned with `gat_params`, listing the inline bound trait names declared at the trait's `AssocTypeDecl.generic_params[i].bounds`) and `where_clause: Option<WhereClause>` (the GAT decl's where-clause cloned at impl-block registration). Populated in `src/typechecker/items.rs::check_impl_block` by looking up the matching trait's `AssocTypeDecl` (cache extended from the slice 7 `trait_assoc_bounds` walk into a `trait_assoc_decls: HashMap<String, &AssocTypeDecl>` mapping); the slice 7 bounds-cache (`trait_assoc_bounds`) is rebuilt off the same decl map to keep its surface unchanged. The new fields default to empty for non-generic bindings and for the prelude-baked entries in `register_stdlib_impls` (`src/typechecker/env_build.rs`) — explicit `param_bound_traits: Vec::new(), where_clause: None` initialisers everywhere `ImplAssocTypeEntry` is constructed. **Discharge in `discharge_gat_decl_constraints`** ([`src/typechecker/exprs.rs`](../../src/typechecker/exprs.rs)). Walks the position-aligned `(gat_param, bound_traits, arg)` triples and discharges each arg against its declared inline bounds via `type_satisfies_bound`, emitting `error[E_GAT_PARAM_BOUND_NOT_SATISFIED]: GAT param \`<name>: <trait>\` on \`<receiver>.<assoc>\` is not satisfied; arg \`<arg>\` does not implement \`<trait>\`` on miss. Then walks the entry's `where_clause`, substitutes `gat_params → projection.args` (a fresh `HashMap<String, Type>` rather than the `SubstValue` form because discharge only consumes concrete types), and for each `TypeBound` constraint, resolves the LHS `type_name` against the substitution and checks each bound via `type_satisfies_bound`, emitting `error[E_GAT_WHERE_CLAUSE_NOT_SATISFIED]: GAT decl \`where <name>: <trait>\` on \`<receiver>.<assoc>\` is not satisfied; arg \`<arg>\` does not implement \`<trait>\`` on miss. Non-`TypeBound` constraints (AssocTypeEq / ConstPredicate / nested ProjectionBound) skip silently — they're uncommon on GAT decls and aren't worth carrying complex resolver-pluming for at this slice. Arg-types that are still `TypeParam` / `TypeVar` / `Error` post-substitution skip silently to avoid noise on upstream unsolved-T diagnostics. **Trigger sites.** Today the helper fires from `discharge_projection_bounds` (i.e., when a where-clause projection bound like `where F.Mapped[i64]: Trait` discharges, the GAT-decl constraints on `F.Mapped[i64]` also discharge). Implicit-usage trigger (`fn f[F: Functor](x: F.Mapped[NoShow])` without a where-clause bound) is not yet exercised — the discharge surface needs a sibling walker over the call's substituted param/return types that scans for `AssocProjection` nodes and discharges them. That walker is straightforward to add but is out of scope for slice 8b (the carry-forward call-out specifically points at projection-resolution time, which is where the explicit-bound trigger already fires); a follow-up under slice 8c can widen the trigger surface alongside the `types_compatible` work. **Defensive pin updated** in `src/typechecker/tests.rs::impl_assoc_type_entry_construct_and_field_access`: the entry-construction test now spells out the new fields explicitly and reads them back, pinning against future field-shape drift. **Test surface (9 integration tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::gat_slice8b_*`).** `test_gat_slice8b_a_clone_bound_on_gat_accepted_via_derive` / `test_gat_slice8b_a_clone_bound_rejected_without_derive` (carry-forward (a) Clone via derive metadata, both arms), `test_gat_slice8b_a_copy_bound_on_primitive_accepted` (primitive coverage for Copy), `test_gat_slice8b_a_debug_bound_accepted_via_derive` (Debug mirror of Clone test), `test_gat_slice8b_c_inline_bound_on_gat_param_rejected_via_where_clause` / `test_gat_slice8b_c_inline_bound_on_gat_param_accepted_when_arg_satisfies` (carry-forward (c) — `type Mapped[U: Show]` checked at projection time via the discharge_projection_bounds → discharge_gat_decl_constraints path; both arms), `test_gat_slice8b_b_where_clause_on_gat_decl_rejected_when_arg_misses` / `test_gat_slice8b_b_where_clause_on_gat_decl_accepted_when_arg_satisfies` (carry-forward (b) — `type Mapped[U] where U: Show` mirror, both arms), `test_gat_slice8b_slices_4_through_8a_still_pass_regression` (regression — the slice 8a headline test continues to pass, confirming the helper is a no-op for non-bounded GAT decls). All slices 4-8a tests + the 21 pre-existing assoc-type / projection tests continue to pass. **What slice 8b does *not* do.** No tightening of `types_compatible` on `AssocProjection` — deferred to slice 8c (see below). No discharge for non-`TypeBound` constraints inside the GAT decl's where-clause (AssocTypeEq / ConstPredicate / nested ProjectionBound) — uncommon on GAT decls; can be added when a real use case appears. No implicit-trigger walker over arbitrary signature positions (`fn f[F: Functor](x: F.Mapped[NoShow])` without a where-clause bound doesn't yet discharge GAT-decl constraints on `NoShow`) — bundles with slice 8c's broader scan. The slice 7 derive-only-builtin call-out is fully consolidated; the slice 8b surface lands the three smaller carry-forwards in one cohesive step.

  - [x] **Slice 8c — `types_compatible` tightening + implicit-trigger walker shipped 2026-05-17.** The fourth slice 7 carry-forward (d) plus the implicit-trigger walker for `discharge_gat_decl_constraints`. **Implementation — `types_compatible` projection arm tightened to structural-only** (`src/typechecker/types.rs`). Pre-slice-8c the arm was wildcard-permissive (`(AssocProjection, _) | (_, AssocProjection) => true`); slice 8c rewrites it as: two `AssocProjection` nodes match iff `param` / `assoc` / `args` / `receiver_args` all structurally match (component-wise `types_compatible`), and a one-sided projection vs anything else returns `false`. **Checker-aware projection-resolving wrappers** (`src/typechecker.rs`). `types_compatible_with_projections(&self, a, b)` and `is_subtype_with_projections(&self, super_ty, sub_ty)` resolve both sides through `resolve_assoc_projections` before delegating to the pure structural check / `is_subtype`. A conservative unresolvable-fallback (via the new `projection_unresolvable_with` helper in `types.rs`) returns `true` when one side resolves to a projection and the other doesn't — preserving the pre-slice-8c semantics for in-body checks inside a generic function where the projection's eventual binding depends on the caller's type-param choice. The strict negative path fires at the call site where the projection's receiver is bound to a concrete type and the impl-table lookup succeeds; the resolved RHS then unifies via the regular structural arm. **Call-site wiring.** `check_assignable` now routes through `is_subtype_with_projections`; the `if`/`if-let` / `match`-arm / range branch-compat checks in `src/typechecker/exprs.rs` + `src/typechecker/patterns.rs` route through `types_compatible_with_projections`. Pure-context callers (`unify_types` in `inference.rs`, `lub_block_type`, the slice/array element-compat sub-calls inside `types_compatible` itself, the `env.unify` debug helper) keep the bare `types_compatible` — those sites don't have `&self` and the pure structural rule is the right semantics. **Call-site return-type substitution gap** (`src/typechecker/exprs.rs::check_call_args_with_substitution_full`). The pre-slice-8c path resolved the return type with `resolve_type_vars` + `resolve_assoc_projections`, which left a return type `F.Mapped[i64]` with `param: "F"` even when F was solved to V via the call's `solutions` map — because `resolve_type_vars` walks `TypeVar` ids but doesn't touch `AssocProjection.param` (a `String`). Slice 8c slots in a `substitute_type_params(&ret, &solutions_as_subs)` pass between the `resolve_type_vars` step and the `resolve_assoc_projections` step so the projection's `param` string rewrites from `"F"` to `"V"` and the subsequent impl-table lookup succeeds. Same treatment for the param-position walker below. **Implicit-trigger walker** (`src/typechecker/exprs.rs::discharge_gat_decl_constraints_in`, called from `check_call_args_with_substitution_full`). Slice 8b shipped `discharge_gat_decl_constraints` but only fired it from the explicit-where-clause path inside `discharge_projection_bounds`; signatures like `fn f[F: Functor](x: F.Mapped[NoShow])` without a where-clause bound never reached the discharge so the GAT decl's `type Mapped[U: Show]` inline bound on `U` was silently skipped. The new walker scans each substituted-but-not-yet-resolved sub_param + return type for `AssocProjection` nodes (recursing into `Tuple` / `Named.args` / `Array.element` / `Slice.element` / `Ref` / `MutRef` / `Weak` / `Rc` / `Arc` / `Pointer.inner` / `Function.params` / `Function.return_type` / `OnceFunction.params` / `OnceFunction.return_type`) and dispatches each to `discharge_gat_decl_constraints`. The walker fires on the **substituted-but-not-resolved** projection because `discharge_gat_decl_constraints` keys off `(param, assoc)` against the impl-table — calling `resolve_assoc_projections` first would erase the projection (replace it with the substituted RHS), losing the discharge opportunity entirely. **Slice 4/5 permissive-arm tests retired in slice-8c framing** (`src/typechecker/tests.rs`). The named pin `types_compatible_remains_permissive_for_projection_with_args` is renamed to `types_compatible_structural_match_on_projection_with_args` and re-stated as a structural-equality assertion: two structurally identical projections match; a one-sided projection vs concrete returns `false`; structurally different projections (different `assoc` name or different `args`) also fail to match. **Test surface (9 integration tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::gat_slice8c_*`).** `test_gat_slice8c_types_compatible_one_sided_projection_vs_concrete_rejected` (THE HEADLINE NEGATIVE — `produce(V {})` returns the impl-resolved `Bar`; assigning to an `i64` slot fires the standard TypeMismatch instead of being silently accepted by the permissive arm), `test_gat_slice8c_types_compatible_projection_resolves_through_impl_table` (THE HEADLINE POSITIVE — `V.Mapped[i64]` resolves to `Vec[i64]` via the impl table; assignment into a `Vec[i64]` slot succeeds via the projection-aware wrapper), `test_gat_slice8c_types_compatible_structurally_identical_projections_match` (two unresolved `F.Mapped[i64]` projections in `if`-branches match via the structural arm), `test_gat_slice8c_implicit_param_position_projection_fires_inline_bound` (THE HEADLINE FOR THE WALKER — `fn use_it[F: Functor](_f: F, _x: F.Mapped[NoShow])` with `type Mapped[U: Show]` fires `E_GAT_PARAM_BOUND_NOT_SATISFIED` at the call site), `test_gat_slice8c_implicit_param_position_projection_accepted_when_arg_satisfies` (positive twin — `F.Mapped[Foo]` with `Foo: Show` passes silently), `test_gat_slice8c_implicit_return_position_projection_fires_where_clause` (return-position walker — `produce(V {})` returning `F.Mapped[NoShow]` with `type Mapped[U] where U: Show` fires `E_GAT_WHERE_CLAUSE_NOT_SATISFIED`), `test_gat_slice8c_implicit_walker_recurses_into_nested_projections` (walker recurses into compound shapes — `Vec[F.Mapped[NoShow]]` at the param position fires the inline-bound miss), `test_gat_slice8c_unresolvable_projection_skips_discharge_silently` (regression — when F stays a generic param at the call site, the discharge short-circuits at the impl-table miss and stays silent, matching slice 8a's "unresolvable projection skipped" rule), `test_gat_slice8c_slices_4_through_8b_still_pass_regression` (regression pin — the slice 8a/8b headline tests continue to pass against the slice 8c tightening + implicit walker). All slices 4-8b tests + the 21 pre-existing assoc-type / projection tests continue to pass. **Single-arg explicit-generic-args call shape note.** The walker tests use argument-position inference (passing `_f: F` alongside the projection-typed param so F is solved from the receiver) rather than explicit-generic-args, mirroring the slice 8a parser-note workaround for the `[V](...)` ambiguity on single-arg generic calls. **What slice 8c does *not* do.** No discharge for non-`TypeBound` constraints inside the GAT decl's where-clause (carries forward from slice 8b — AssocTypeEq / ConstPredicate / nested ProjectionBound on GAT decls remain unhandled). No projection-resolution at `unify_types` (`inference.rs`) — the pure structural rule is sufficient there because the only sites where projections vs concrete cross-shape unification matters (assignment / branch-compat / call-arg unification) route through `check_assignable` / the wrapper. No widening to higher-ranked projections (`for<X> F.Mapped[X]: Trait`) — slice 9 carve-out. The slice 7 carry-forward (d) is fully consolidated; the implicit-trigger walker closes the slice 8b call-out that explicit + implicit projection trigger sites should both fire the GAT-decl constraints discharge.

  - [x] **Slice 9 — Negative-space coverage shipped 2026-05-17.** Three pins documenting v1 GAT non-features so future readers know the rejections are load-bearing, not accidental gaps. No production-code change per the slice spec — diagnostics being re-asserted were planted by slices 1 (effect-param rejection) and 6 (coherence). **Test surface (1 typechecker test in `tests/typechecker.rs` + 2 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs`).** `test_gat_slice9_a_coherence_rejects_duplicate_impls_with_distinct_gat_bindings` (typechecker — slice-9-framed mirror of slice 6's coherence pin: two `impl Functor for Wrapper[i32]` blocks with genuinely-different `Mapped[U]` RHS shapes — `Vec[U]` vs `Set[U]` — still trip `TypeErrorKind::ConflictingImpl`. GAT bindings are part of the impl block; they contribute no coherence rule of their own. Slice 6 already pins this surface; slice 9's contribution is the explicit framing so the negative-space intent is searchable by name); `gat_slice9_b_higher_ranked_for_in_where_clause_rejected` (parser — `where for<X> F.Mapped[X]: Send` fails to parse: `for` is a loop keyword in Kāra v1, not a binder, so the parser rejects on the `for` token in where-clause position. This pin guards against a future parser change adding binder-position `for` (e.g., for existentials) silently accepting HRTBs); `gat_slice9_c_effect_param_on_gat_decl_still_rejected` (parser — re-verification of slice 1's `E_GAT_EFFECT_PARAM` diagnostic + "carrying method" steering-suggestion surface. Intentionally redundant with `gat_slice1_trait_assoc_type_rejects_effect_param` so a regression in the parser's effect-param rejection trips both the slice 1 (slice-as-shipped behaviour) and slice 9 (v1 negative-space contract) framings). All slices 4-8c tests + the 21 pre-existing assoc-type / projection tests continue to pass. **Why redundant pins.** Slice 9 (a) and (c) deliberately retest surfaces that slices 6 and 1 already cover. The redundancy is the feature: when one of these diagnostics is regressed, two framings fail in parallel — the slice-as-shipped pin and the explicit-negative-space pin — making the intent of the rejection unmistakable to whoever is bisecting the regression. **What slice 9 does *not* do.** No new production code (the spec is test-only); no new error codes (re-uses `TypeErrorKind::ConflictingImpl` and `E_GAT_EFFECT_PARAM`); no widening of HRTB rejection beyond the where-clause position (`for<X>` in other parser positions like trait-decl args is not exercised — those positions don't accept generic-quantifier syntax today and the parser rejects them via the standard "expected X" diagnostics).

- [ ] **`impl Trait` in argument, return, and RPITIT positions (TAIT *declaration grammar* lands at v1; TAIT *witness inference* is P1).** Implement the spec in `design.md § \`impl Trait\` (Existential Types)`. Slices: (1) Lexer — no new tokens; the existing `impl` keyword handles the prefix. (2) Parser — extend the type-expression grammar so `impl TRAIT_PATH [GENERIC_ARGS] [\`with\` EFFECT_LIST]` is accepted in: type-position arguments (`fn f(x: impl T)`), function return types (`-> impl T`), trait method return types (`fn f(...) -> impl T;` inside `trait { ... }`), the right-hand side of `type` aliases (`type X = impl T;` — declaration parses at v1; witness-inference machinery is P1), and inside generic-argument positions where a type may appear (e.g., `Vec[impl T]` is rejected at v1 with a diagnostic suggesting an explicit generic parameter — `impl Trait` deep in nested type positions is post-v1). (3) AST — new `TypeKind::ImplTrait { trait_path: Path, args: Vec<GenericArg>, use_effects: Option<EffectList>, span: Span }` variant. (4) Resolver — argument-position `impl Trait` desugars at the resolver into a fresh anonymous generic parameter `[T_impl_N: Trait]` with the same bounds (no existential, no special handling downstream); return-position / RPITIT keep the `ImplTrait` kind through to the typechecker; TAIT references are recorded as `TaitReference { tait: TaitId, generic_args: ... }` placeholders that the v1 stub treats identically to a `dyn Trait` of the same trait bound (the witness-inference pipeline lands at P1, see the `[→ P1]` companion entry below). The desugar of argument-position `impl Trait` runs **before** trait-method position checking so the "no `impl Trait` in trait-method argument position" rule is enforced uniformly: trait method declarations require the explicit generic form. Dual-`impl Trait` argument positions (`fn pair(x: impl T, y: impl T)`) produce two independent generic parameters — verified by the desugar being per-occurrence. (5) Typechecker — return-position `impl Trait` types unify only via their declared trait bound; the concrete return type is computed from the function body and recorded as the existential's witness. The body's return-expression type must implement the declared `Trait`; failure emits `error[E_IMPL_TRAIT_MISSING_BOUND]` with the offending type and the missing trait. The typechecker rejects callers that try to name the existential's concrete type, pattern-match on it past the trait surface, or use it in a position requiring a non-trait type. **TAIT use sites that depend on the witness type** (calling a method that the trait does not declare but the witness type would) emit `error[E_TAIT_NOT_IMPLEMENTED_YET]: TAIT 'NAME' is recognized but the witness-inference pipeline lands in P1; cast through the trait surface for now`. (6) Capture-set checker — for return-position / RPITIT existentials, compute the captured type parameters and borrow regions per the elision rule in design.md (type parameters appearing in the return-type expression; borrow regions of `ref` parameters that flow into a `ref` in the return-type expression). The borrow checker uses the captured set to bound the existential's lifetime at use sites — a use after the captured borrow's source is dropped is the existing borrow-checker error. No explicit `use<>` syntax in v1. The capture-set rule for TAIT references uses only the alias's own type parameters (no implicit capture of the defining function's generics), matching the design.md spec; this rule applies at v1 even though witness inference is P1. (7) RPITIT blocks `dyn Trait` — the compiler rejects `dyn TraitWithRPITIT` with `error[E_RPITIT_INCOMPATIBLE_WITH_DYN]` naming the offending method; the impl Trait method shape has no fixed vtable slot. (8) **TAIT same-concrete-type enforcement, opaque cross-package surface, and generic TAIT instantiation are P1** — see the companion `[→ P1]` entry below. The v1 work for TAIT is parser/AST/resolver-recording/v1-stub-diagnostic only. (9) Effect-checking integration is deferred to Phase 8 alongside `dyn Trait` effect checking — until then, `impl Trait` calls are accepted by the parser/typechecker but the effect checker requires the containing function to declare `with _` (mirrors the existing `dyn Trait` Phase 8 transition rule). When Phase 8 lands, the effect checker will: (a) verify each concrete return type's trait-method impls have effects covered by the existential's declared `with E'` ceiling; (b) propagate function execution effects (`with E`) at the call site; (c) propagate existential method-use effects (`with E'`) at every method invocation on the returned existential; (d) handle unbound-trait existentials identically to unbound-trait `dyn Trait` (caller declares `with _`). Test coverage (typechecker + parser slices, Phase 5.2): argument-position `impl Trait` desugars correctly (call sites accepting different concrete types per call); two `impl T` arguments don't unify; return-position `-> impl Iterator[Item = i64]` accepts a concrete iterator return; same with split `with E` / `-> impl T with E'` syntax; RPITIT method declaration parses inside `trait`; impl of an RPITIT method picks its own concrete return; trying to use `dyn Trait` on a trait with RPITIT is rejected with the typed diagnostic; **TAIT declaration parses and registers**; TAIT use site through trait-surface methods works (treated as `dyn Trait`-like for v1); TAIT use site that depends on the witness produces the `E_TAIT_NOT_IMPLEMENTED_YET` stub diagnostic; capture-set check accepts an iterator outliving an unrelated `ref Logger` parameter; capture-set check rejects an iterator outliving its `ref Vec[T]` source; the explicit `[T: Trait]` form continues to work alongside argument-position `impl Trait`; trait-method-argument-position `impl Trait` rejected with a diagnostic suggesting the explicit form. Effect-checking test coverage lands with Phase 8. Phase target: 5.2 (parser/typechecker/capture-set/RPITIT-blocks-dyn/TAIT-declaration-and-stub). Effect-checking integration: Phase 8. TAIT semantics: P1 (see companion entry).

  - [x] **Slice 1 — Parser surface + AST node shipped 2026-05-17.** Implements parent spec items (2)+(3). **Implementation — AST** (`src/ast/types.rs`): new `TypeKind::ImplTrait { trait_path: PathExpr, args: Vec<GenericArg>, use_effects: Option<EffectList>, span: Span }` variant. The spec called for `trait_path: Path` but the codebase has no top-level `Path` type — `PathExpr` (the same shape used by `TypeKind::Path`) is the right mirror, so the variant uses `PathExpr` directly. The `use_effects` field is `Option<EffectList>` (the same shape `Fn(...) with E` uses for its effect-spec); `None` when the `with` suffix is absent. **Parser surface** (`src/parser/types.rs`): new `Token::Impl` arm on `parse_type` accepts `impl TRAIT_PATH[GENERIC_ARGS] [with EFFECT_LIST]`. The trait path is parsed via `parse_path_type` so multi-segment paths (`std.iter.Iterator`) and positional generic args route through the same machinery as regular path types; any generic args are lifted out of the inner `PathExpr` into the variant's `args` field. The optional `with` clause mirrors `Fn(...) with E`'s peek-only dispatch (`with _` → `EffectItem::Polymorphic`, otherwise hands off to `parse_effect_list` for the verb / variable / group items). **Rejection diagnostics — position tracking** (`src/parser.rs`): new `impl_trait_block_stack: Vec<ImplTraitBlockReason>` field on the `Parser` records "current type-position is illegal for `impl Trait`, reject with diagnostic X." Two reasons today: `NestedGenericArg` (pushed by `parse_generic_type_args` around each type-arg's `parse_type` call) emits `E_IMPL_TRAIT_IN_NESTED_POSITION` with steering text suggesting an explicit generic parameter; `TraitMethodArg` (pushed by `parse_trait_method` around the parameter-list parse) emits `E_IMPL_TRAIT_IN_TRAIT_METHOD_ARG` with steering text suggesting the explicit `[T: Trait]` form. The trait-method-arg block is popped *before* the return-type parse so RPITIT (`fn m() -> impl T`) keeps working uniformly — the rejection is parameter-position-only. Parser-level rejection is the early-exit; slice 2's resolver-side desugar will also enforce the trait-method-arg rule. **Downstream stub arms** (`src/effectchecker.rs`, `src/formatter/types.rs`, `src/parser.rs::render_type_for_diagnostic`, `src/resolver/resolve_refs.rs`, `src/typechecker/items.rs::check_type_expr_visibility`, `src/typechecker/lowering.rs::lower_type_expr_inner`): seven exhaustive-match sites needed a `TypeKind::ImplTrait` arm to keep the build clean. Six of them mirror the `TypeKind::Path` behaviour (resolve the trait path, walk generic args, route through the same private-type-leak / diagnostic-rendering / formatter machinery). The seventh — the typechecker's lowering path — emits a focused `E_IMPL_TRAIT_NOT_YET_IMPLEMENTED` diagnostic naming the trait and steering at the explicit `[T: Trait]` form, then returns `Type::Error`. This keeps reach-through panics out while making the slice-sequencing pause loud and named, per the user-facing diagnostic policy. **Test surface (11 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs::impl_trait_slice1_*`):** `impl_trait_slice1_argument_position_parses` (`fn f(x: impl Iterator) {}`), `impl_trait_slice1_return_position_parses` (`fn f() -> impl Iterator { ... }`), `impl_trait_slice1_trait_method_return_position_parses` (RPITIT — `trait Source { fn iter(self) -> impl Iterator; }`), `impl_trait_slice1_type_alias_rhs_parses` (TAIT — `type Iter = impl Iterator;`), `impl_trait_slice1_with_effect_clause_parses` (`-> impl Iterator with reads(World)` — pins the `use_effects` field carrying a `reads(World)` `EffectItem::Verb`), `impl_trait_slice1_with_generic_args_parses` (`-> impl Iterator[i64]` — pins positional generic args on the trait path), `impl_trait_slice1_nested_position_rejected` (`fn f(x: Vec[impl T]) {}` rejected with `E_IMPL_TRAIT_IN_NESTED_POSITION` + explicit-generic-parameter steering), `impl_trait_slice1_trait_method_argument_position_rejected` (`trait Sink { fn write(self, x: impl Display); }` rejected with `E_IMPL_TRAIT_IN_TRAIT_METHOD_ARG` + explicit-generic steering), `impl_trait_slice1_regular_fn_argument_position_accepted` (positive pin — free function argument-position `impl Display` accepted), `impl_trait_slice1_impl_method_argument_position_accepted` (positive pin — impl-block method argument-position `impl Display` accepted; only trait-decl methods reject), `impl_trait_slice1_multi_segment_trait_path_parses` (`-> impl std.iter.Iterator` — pins multi-segment trait path routing). All pre-existing parser / typechecker / formatter tests pass against the new variant. **Deviations from the spec.** (a) `trait_path: PathExpr` instead of the spec's `trait_path: Path` (no `Path` type exists in this codebase; `PathExpr` is the right mirror for the variant). (b) `Iterator[Item = i64]` (assoc-type binding in generic-args position) is *not* a parseable surface at v1 — the generic-args grammar accepts type-expressions or const-expressions but no `Item = type` shape — so the tests use `Iterator` (bare) and `Iterator[i64]` (positional) variants. The slice-1 `TypeKind::ImplTrait` arm exercised is identical; the missing `[Item = ...]` surface is a separate carry-forward for later slices to wire up if needed. **What slice 1 does *not* do.** No semantic handling — the typechecker emits `E_IMPL_TRAIT_NOT_YET_IMPLEMENTED` on `Type::Error` lowering so any user code touching `impl Trait` post-parse gets a focused "slice 2-4 will land this" diagnostic rather than a panic. No resolver desugar of argument-position occurrences (slice 2). No typechecker semantics for return-position / RPITIT (slice 3). No capture-set checker (slice 4). No `dyn Trait` rejection on RPITIT traits (slice 5). No TAIT v1 stub diagnostics (slice 6). No effect-checking integration (Phase 8). **Blocks slices 2-6** are now unblocked. Phase target: 5.2.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — Resolver desugar (argument-position) shipped 2026-05-17.** Implements parent spec item (4) argument-position half. **Implementation — pipeline placement** (`src/desugar.rs` new module, `src/lib.rs` `desugar_program` re-export, wired into `src/cli.rs` `Pipeline::resolve` and `src/lib.rs` `run_program_with_drops` / `run_program_with_dbg` / `run_program_full` between `parse` and `resolve`): the desugar runs as a pre-resolve AST-rewriting pass on `&mut Program`. Placing it inside `Parser::parse` was rejected because the `fmt` CLI calls `crate::parse` directly and needs to round-trip `impl Trait` verbatim through `formatter::format_program`; instead each compilation driver invokes `desugar_program` explicitly. **Algorithm** (`src/desugar.rs::desugar_impl_trait_args_in_function`): for each `Item::Function` and each `ImplItem::Method` inside `Item::ImplBlock`, walk params; when `param.ty.kind` is a top-level `TypeKind::ImplTrait`, allocate the next `T_impl_arg_N` name (per-function counter), build a `TraitBound { path: trait_path.segments, generic_args: Some(args) or None, span }` from the impl-trait node, append a `GenericParam { name, bounds: vec![bound], is_const: false, const_type: None, span }` to `f.generic_params` (creating the `GenericParams` if absent), and replace `param.ty` with `TypeExpr { kind: TypeKind::Path(PathExpr { segments: vec![synthetic_name], generic_args: None, span: original_span }), span: original_span }`. Per-occurrence so `fn pair(x: impl T, y: impl T)` produces `T_impl_arg_0` and `T_impl_arg_1` — the typechecker never unifies them. **Downstream phase changes — zero.** Because the desugar mutates the AST into a shape the resolver and typechecker already know how to walk (an explicit generic param + a path-typed parameter), no resolver / typechecker / lowering changes were required; `define_generic_params` registers the synthetic name with bounds, `generic_param_names` includes it in the function's generic scope, `lower_path_type` resolves it via the existing `generic_scope.contains(name) → Type::TypeParam(name)` branch, and the typechecker's `enclosing_bounds` discharge dispatches trait methods on the synthetic param via the same machinery as user-declared generics. **Trait-method-arg rule** stays parser-level (slice 1's `TraitMethodArg` block via `ImplTraitBlockReason`); the spec calls for the desugar to run "before trait-method-position checking" — since the parser rejects `impl Trait` in trait-method-arg position before the AST reaches the desugar, the spec's ordering constraint is satisfied by virtue of the position never existing post-parse. **Return-position + TAIT-RHS + RPITIT-return** intentionally NOT desugared — those keep their `TypeKind::ImplTrait` kind and continue to hit the slice-1 `E_IMPL_TRAIT_NOT_YET_IMPLEMENTED` stub diagnostic until slices 3 / 6 land their typechecker semantics. **`use_effects` on argument-position** (`impl T with E`) is dropped during desugar per the parent spec's "same bounds (no existential, no special handling downstream)" rule — the `with E` clause is meaningful only on return-position existentials where slice 3 + Phase 8 pick it up. **Test surface (6 resolver tests in `tests/resolver.rs::impl_trait_slice2_*`, 2 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::impl_trait_slice2_*`):** `argument_position_desugars_to_synthetic_generic_param` (pins the AST shape — `f.generic_params.params[0].name == "T_impl_arg_0"`, bound is `Display`, param ty is `TypeKind::Path(["T_impl_arg_0"])`), `pair_args_produce_two_distinct_synthetic_params` (per-occurrence — `T_impl_arg_0` + `T_impl_arg_1`), `explicit_generic_form_continues_to_work_alongside_impl_trait` (`fn mixed[T: Display](x: T, y: impl Display)` — user's `T` plus synthetic `T_impl_arg_0`), `return_position_kept_as_impl_trait` (`fn iter() -> impl Iterator` — return type stays `TypeKind::ImplTrait`, no synthetic generic params added), `impl_method_argument_position_desugars` (inherent-impl method's `impl Display` param desugars per-method), `synthetic_param_bounds_recorded_in_symbol_table` (post-desugar resolver registers the synthetic name as `SymbolKind::TypeParam` with bound `Display` via `record_generic_bounds`); typechecker: `argument_position_typechecks_with_distinct_call_site_types` (two call sites of `show(impl Tagged)` infer independent `Alpha` / `Beta` concrete types), `pair_arguments_dont_unify` (`pair(Alpha, Beta)` is accepted by `fn pair(x: impl Tagged, y: impl Tagged)`). **What slice 2 does *not* do.** No typechecker semantics for return-position / RPITIT (slice 3). No capture-set checker (slice 4). No `dyn Trait` rejection on RPITIT traits (slice 5). No TAIT v1 stub semantics (slice 6). No effect-checking integration (Phase 8). No support for `ref impl T` or other non-top-level argument positions — the desugar handles top-level argument-position `impl Trait` only, matching the spec's `fn f(x: impl T)` shape. **Blocks slice 3** unblocked. Phase target: 5.2.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — Typechecker (return-position + RPITIT) shipped 2026-05-17.** Implements parent spec item (5). **Type representation** (`src/typechecker/types.rs`): new `Type::Existential { trait_name: String, trait_args: Vec<Type>, origin: SpanKey }` variant. `origin` is the `SpanKey` of the `TypeKind::ImplTrait` AST node — two distinct `-> impl Iterator` declarations on different functions yield distinct origins so the typechecker keeps their witnesses separate even when their bounds match structurally. **Lowering** (`src/typechecker/lowering.rs`, replaces the slice-1 `E_IMPL_TRAIT_NOT_YET_IMPLEMENTED` stub at line 142): any `TypeKind::ImplTrait` reaching the typechecker (return-position / RPITIT-return / TAIT-RHS — argument-position was eliminated by the slice-2 desugar) lowers to `Type::Existential` carrying the trait name (`trait_path.segments.join(".")`), positional trait args (`Vec<Type>`, const-args dropped pending design), and the origin SpanKey. **Body return-check** (`src/typechecker.rs::check_assignable`): when the expected slot is `Type::Existential { trait_name, .. }` and the found is a concrete witness, route through `is_subtype_with_projections` → existential branch → `type_satisfies_bound(found, trait_name)`; a body whose tail-expr type does not implement the declared trait emits `error[E_IMPL_TRAIT_MISSING_BOUND]: function returns 'impl X' but body type 'W' does not implement 'X'` naming both the trait and the offending witness. **Caller-side opacity**: `types_compatible` rejects existential↔concrete cross-direction (both orderings) — `(Existential, Existential) => same-origin only`; `(Existential, _) | (_, Existential) => false` for the mixed case so `let x: Concrete = call_returning_existential()` and any pattern-match-past-trait-surface attempt surfaces as a normal type-mismatch with the diagnostic naming `impl TraitName` for the opaque side. Same-origin existentials unify; distinct-origin existentials (different declaration sites) do not — this is the witness-identity guarantee that lets each `fn` body pick its own concrete return type. **`type_satisfies_bound`** (`src/typechecker/exprs.rs`): existential whose `trait_name` exactly matches the queried trait satisfies the bound by construction (slice 3 does not yet walk supertrait closures here — slice 5 / Phase 8 may extend). **Display** (`src/typechecker/types.rs::type_display`): `Type::Existential` renders as `impl TraitName` (or `impl TraitName[Arg1, Arg2]` with trait args). **Other consumers**: `type_is_fully_concrete` returns false for existentials (an impl block target can never name an existential, so they stay out of the specialized lane); `type_supports_eq` / `type_supports_hash` / `type_supports_display` / `type_supports_clone` / `type_supports_debug` / `type_supports_ord` / `type_supports_partial_eq` / `type_supports_partial_ord` return false for existentials (the derive-matches-bound surface goes through `type_satisfies_bound`'s existential-trait-name comparison, not through these helpers). **RPITIT**: trait-method declarations like `trait Source { fn iter(self) -> impl Iter; }` lower the return type to `Type::Existential` at typecheck time; per-impl picking of concrete return types is automatic because the codebase does not yet enforce trait-method/impl-method signature compatibility — each impl's `fn iter(self) -> ConcreteType { ... }` is checked on its own merits, which IS the RPITIT semantics. **Effects** (`with E'`): the parser carries `use_effects` on the `TypeKind::ImplTrait` node; slice 3's lowering drops it. Phase 8's effect-check integration consumes it later. **Test surface (7 tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::impl_trait_slice3_*`):** `return_position_accepts_witness_implementing_trait` (`-> impl Tagged` returning a `Beta` that `impl Tagged`); `return_position_rejects_witness_not_implementing_trait` (`-> impl Tagged` returning `i64` — pins the `E_IMPL_TRAIT_MISSING_BOUND` diagnostic naming both the witness and the trait); `caller_naming_witness_concrete_type_rejected` (`let x: Beta = make()` where `make() -> impl Tagged` — opacity diagnostic names `Beta` expected vs `impl Tagged` found); `return_position_with_effect_clause_typechecks` (`-> impl Tagged with reads(World)` parses, lowers, accepts witness — `with E'` drops at slice 3, Phase 8 integration); `rpitit_method_declaration_typechecks` (trait method declaration with `-> impl Iter` typechecks at trait-decl time); `rpitit_impl_picks_concrete_return_type` (impl method picks its own `-> i64` return for an RPITIT trait method); `two_distinct_impl_trait_decls_have_distinct_witnesses` (witness-identity pin — `fn make_a() -> impl Tagged` and `fn make_b() -> impl Tagged` have distinct origins). **What slice 3 does *not* do.** No capture-set checker (slice 4). No `dyn Trait` rejection on RPITIT traits (slice 5). No TAIT v1-stub semantics — TAIT-RHS lowering produces `Type::Existential` today but TAIT use-site semantics await slice 6 (slice 6's stub will route TAIT use-sites through the dyn-Trait shape; for now they pass through the existential type unchanged). No codegen support — programs that USE the existential at call sites work end-to-end through the typechecker only; codegen lowering for existentials is the slice 4+ continuation. No effect-checking integration (Phase 8). No supertrait closure in `type_satisfies_bound`'s existential arm. **Blocks slice 4** unblocked; slice 5 / slice 6 also unblocked. Phase target: 5.2.

  - [x] **Slice 4 — Capture-set checker shipped 2026-05-17.** Implements parent spec item (6). **Capture-set computation** (`src/typechecker/items.rs::record_impl_trait_captures`, called from `check_function` after the return type is lowered): walks the AST return-type expression for every nested `TypeKind::ImplTrait` node and computes, per occurrence, (a) the set of type-parameter names that textually appear in the existential's trait args (e.g., `impl Iter[T]` captures `T`; `impl Iter[i64]` does not capture any) and (b) the set of `ref`/`mut ref` input parameter names whose borrow regions are captured. Per design.md § "Capture set" and Kāra's conservative multi-input ref-return elision (see safety_design.rs § multi-source), a `ref` anywhere in the existential's trait args triggers the capture of EVERY `ref`/`mut ref` input on the fn (and `self` when the receiver is `ref self`/`mut ref self`); a `ref`-less existential captures no inputs. **Storage**: new `pub struct ImplTraitCaptures { type_params: Vec<String>, input_borrows: Vec<String> }` in `src/typechecker.rs`, exposed via `TypeCheckResult::impl_trait_captures: HashMap<SpanKey, ImplTraitCaptures>` keyed by the `TypeKind::ImplTrait` AST node's `SpanKey` (the same key shape used by `Type::Existential::origin`). **Borrow-checker integration** (`src/ownership.rs::collect_callee_existential_capture_indices` + `src/ownership/borrow.rs::record_existential_capture_borrows`, called from both Call arms in `src/ownership/expr_check.rs`): at OwnershipChecker construction time, each callee whose return type has captured input borrows is registered with the positional indices of its captured params; at every `Call` site to such a callee, the captured argument's place-expression root is recorded into `slice_borrow_sources[call_span]` and an `ImmSlice` active borrow is pushed against the source root (after the call's snapshot restore so the borrow persists past the call). The existing slice-borrow propagation pipeline (`StmtKind::Let` → `slice_binding_sources[name]` + `slice_binding_scope_depth[source_root]`, and the source-scope-exit drain in `drain_borrows_at_depth`) and the conflict matrix in `push_active_borrow` carry the existential's borrow through downstream detection without further integration. **Reusing `ImmSlice`** as the existential's borrow kind keeps the existing slice-shape drain path applicable; a dedicated `Existential` borrow kind can be added later if diagnostic messaging needs to distinguish. **Method-call dispatch**: `MethodCall` borrow-tracking is left for a future sub-slice — today's collector covers free functions and static impl methods (`Type.name(...)`); RPITIT through `MethodCall` is the natural extension. **Test surface (5 typechecker tests + 2 ownership tests):** `tests/typechecker.rs::impl_trait_slice4_*` — `captures_type_param_appearing_in_return` (`fn make[T](xs: Vec[T]) -> impl Iter[T]` captures `T`); `does_not_capture_type_param_absent_from_return` (`fn count[T](xs: Vec[T]) -> impl Iter[i64]` captures no type param); `captures_input_borrow_when_ref_appears_in_return` (`fn first(v: ref Vec[i64]) -> impl Iter[ref i64]` captures `v`); `does_not_capture_unrelated_ref_input_when_no_ref_in_return` (`-> impl Iter[i64]` with a `log: ref Logger` input captures no input borrow); `captures_all_ref_inputs_on_ambiguous_elision` (two `ref Vec` inputs + `ref` in return → both captured per the conservative over-approximation); `tests/ownership.rs::impl_trait_slice4_*` — `iterator_unrelated_log_drop_accepted` (positive: `log` not in capture set, no spurious diagnostic when its scope ends), `iterator_outliving_its_vec_source_rejected` (negative: existential's capture borrow on `v` conflicts with a later `v.as_slice_mut()` via the existing slice-vs-slice conflict matrix — the conflict is the proof that the existential's borrow is actively tracked against `v`). **What slice 4 does *not* do.** No `use<>` syntax (per spec, no v1 surface). No supertrait-closure analysis on the captured set. No `MethodCall` capture-borrow registration (free fns + static impl methods only at v1). No block-expression-tail / typed-LetUninit propagation for existentials — the borrow IS pushed; the source-scope-exit drain fires its drop-of-borrowed diagnostic when the user surfaces the existential through a scope-shape the existing pipeline can name (e.g., conflict matrix as exercised in the rejection test). A typed `let it: impl Iter[ref i64];` would require an `impl Trait` name-side surface that Kāra deliberately does not have. No codegen lowering for existentials. No effect-checking integration (Phase 8). **Blocks slice 5** unblocked (RPITIT-blocks-dyn is structurally independent and can land next). Phase target: 5.2.

  - [x] **Slice 5 — RPITIT blocks `dyn Trait` shipped 2026-05-17.** Implements parent spec item (7). **Parser surface** (`src/parser/types.rs`): new `Token::Dyn` arm at `parse_type` mirroring the `Token::Impl` shape — reads `dyn TRAIT_PATH[GENERIC_ARGS]` and emits a `TypeKind::Dyn { trait_path, args, span }` AST node. The general `dyn Trait` feature (vtable construction, dynamic dispatch, effect-opacity story) is P1-deferred per design.md § Polymorphism; the parser surface lands today only so the slice-5 check has a syntactic target. **AST** (`src/ast/types.rs`): new `TypeKind::Dyn` variant; doc comment cross-references both the RPITIT check (`E_RPITIT_INCOMPATIBLE_WITH_DYN`) and the P1-deferred general stub (`E_DYN_TRAIT_NOT_IMPLEMENTED_YET`). **Typechecker check** (`src/typechecker/lowering.rs`): `TypeKind::Dyn` lowering walks generic args first (surfaces nested errors), then queries `trait_first_rpitit_method(program, trait_name)` which scans the trait declaration's methods for any `return_type` whose `TypeKind` is `ImplTrait` (RPITIT). When the helper returns `Some(method_name)`, emit `E_RPITIT_INCOMPATIBLE_WITH_DYN` naming both the trait and the offending method ("no fixed vtable slot can be synthesized") with the steering hint to route through a generic parameter `[T: TraitName]`. Otherwise emit the generic `E_DYN_TRAIT_NOT_IMPLEMENTED_YET` stub (general `dyn Trait` semantics ship at P1). Either way the lowered type is `Type::Error` so downstream phases recover cleanly. **Downstream stub arms** (formatter, resolver `resolve_type_expr`, effectchecker `collect_effect_var_names_in_type` + `format_type_expr_with_subs`, ownership `collect_impl_trait_spans`, typechecker `check_type_expr_visibility` + `walk_for_impl_trait` + `collect_capture_signals` + parser `render_type_for_diagnostic`): each gets a one-arm passthrough that walks the trait path / generic args for nested error surfacing. The visibility-leak rule applies uniformly — a private trait name surfacing through a `pub` signature via `dyn` is just as much a leak as via `impl` or bare path. **Test surface (3 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::impl_trait_slice5_*`):** `dyn_trait_with_rpitit_method_rejected` (the headline negative — a trait with an `-> impl Iter` method consumed via `dyn Source` fires `E_RPITIT_INCOMPATIBLE_WITH_DYN` naming the offending `iter` method); `dyn_trait_without_rpitit_hits_p1_stub` (a non-RPITIT trait hits the generic `E_DYN_TRAIT_NOT_IMPLEMENTED_YET` instead, and the RPITIT diagnostic does NOT misfire); `dyn_trait_parses_as_type_kind_dyn` (parser surface pin — `dyn Trait` builds `TypeKind::Dyn`, not a bare `Path`, so future parser refactors can't silently bypass the slice-5 check). **What slice 5 does *not* do.** No vtable construction, no dynamic dispatch, no `dyn Trait` value/type semantics — the lowered type is `Type::Error` regardless of the diagnostic chosen, since the general `dyn Trait` machinery is P1. No `dyn TraitAlias` expansion (slice depends on the P1 trait-alias work). No supertrait-closure RPITIT walk (today's check only inspects the trait's own methods; a trait that inherits an RPITIT method via a supertrait would need a closure walk to reject — additive). No effect-checker integration (Phase 8). **Blocks slice 6** independent — slice 6 (TAIT declaration + v1 stub) can land in parallel. Phase target: 5.2.

  - [x] **Slice 6 — TAIT declaration + v1 stub shipped 2026-05-17.** Implements parent spec item (4) TAIT half + item (8) v1 portion. **Parser surface** unchanged — slice 1's TAIT-RHS position already produces `TypeKind::ImplTrait` on the type-alias RHS, and slice 3's lowering already maps that to `Type::Existential`. **TAIT marker** (`src/typechecker/types.rs`): new `tait_alias: Option<String>` field on `Type::Existential` — `Some(alias_name)` when the existential was minted from a `type X = impl Trait;` declaration, `None` for return-position / RPITIT-return existentials (slice 3). **Marker propagation** (`src/typechecker/env_build.rs::env_add_type_alias`): when the alias's `t.ty.kind` is `TypeKind::ImplTrait`, mutate the lowered `Type::Existential` to carry `tait_alias = Some(t.name)`. The marker is the load-bearing signal for slice 6's TAIT-specific diagnostic — slice 3's caller-side opacity / body-return-check paths use the existential's `trait_name` + `origin` and stay unaware of the alias context. **TAIT use-site dispatch** (`src/typechecker/expr_method_call.rs::dispatch_existential_receiver_method`): new method-call receiver arm for `Type::Existential` that looks up `method` on the existential's declared trait via [`find_trait_method`]. On hit, dispatches through [`dispatch_trait_assoc_fn`] with `Self → Type::TypeParam(trait_name)` — the same trait-surface lowering used by `Type::TypeParam` receivers, which keeps slice 6 uniform with slice 3's `type_satisfies_bound` story. On miss, the diagnostic depends on `tait_alias`: when `Some(alias)`, emit `error[E_TAIT_NOT_IMPLEMENTED_YET]: TAIT 'NAME' is recognized but the witness-inference pipeline lands in P1; method 'M' is not declared on trait 'T', and dispatching against the alias's concrete witness requires the deferred TAIT machinery — cast through the trait surface for now`; when `None`, emit the generic `no method 'M' on 'impl T' value` for return-position existentials (slice 3 already covers the rest of opacity). **Trait-surface success path identical to slice 3** — `s.show()` on a `let s: Shown = make()` where `Shown = impl Tagged` resolves `show` through the `Tagged` trait declaration. **Witness-required miss path** — `s.extra()` (a method on `Concrete` but NOT on `Tagged`) fires the focused `E_TAIT_NOT_IMPLEMENTED_YET`. **Capture-set rule for TAIT references**: TAIT-sourced existentials inherit slice 4's capture-set machinery via the same `origin: SpanKey` plumbing; the alias's own type parameters are the only captured params (per design.md § Capture set), and the slice-4 walk already enforces this by sourcing captures from the impl-trait AST node's span. **Test surface (3 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::impl_trait_slice6_*`):** `tait_declaration_typechecks_cleanly` (pure plumbing — `type Shown = impl Tagged;` parses, desugars, resolves, typechecks without firing any slice-1/3 stub); `tait_use_through_trait_surface_method_works` (`let s: Shown = make(); s.tag()` where `tag` is on the trait — dispatcher routes through `dispatch_trait_assoc_fn` and the call type-checks); `tait_use_with_non_trait_method_emits_stub_diagnostic` (`s.extra()` where `extra` is on the witness's inherent impl but NOT on the trait — fires `E_TAIT_NOT_IMPLEMENTED_YET` naming the alias `Shown`, the missing method `extra`, and the trait `Tagged`). **What slice 6 does *not* do.** No witness inference (P1) — defining-use inference from function bodies returning the alias is the central P1 deliverable; today's slice 6 carries the alias name as a marker but never resolves it to a concrete type. No same-concrete-type enforcement at the package boundary (`E_TAIT_CONCRETE_MISMATCH` is P1). No opaque cross-package surface (consumers see the existential through whatever lowering the alias produces — there's no cross-package boundary check for TAITs at v1). No generic TAIT instantiations (`type Iter[T] = impl Iterator[Item = T]` — the lowering routes through `lower_type_expr` with `gp` as the alias's own params, but the per-instantiation witness-inference plumbing awaits P1). No inherent-method resolution against the witness inside the defining package (the trait-surface-only routing is the v1 stub). No `MethodCall` capture-borrow registration for TAIT references — slice 4's free-fn / static-impl-method coverage is the same here; method-call wiring is the natural extension. **Replaces** the spec's prior "v1 stub treats TAIT use sites identically to a `dyn Trait`" framing with the simpler "existential with TAIT marker" framing that reuses slice 3's existential machinery without introducing a new lowering target. **Companion**: replaced by the [`→ P1`] entry below once witness inference lands. Phase target: 5.2.

  - [→ Phase 8] **Effect-checking integration.** Parent spec item (9). Deferred to Phase 8 alongside `dyn Trait` effect checking. Until then, `impl Trait` calls are accepted but the containing function must declare `with _` (mirrors the existing `dyn Trait` Phase 8 transition rule). When Phase 8 lands: (a) verify each concrete return type's trait-method impls have effects covered by the existential's declared `with E'` ceiling; (b) propagate function execution effects (`with E`) at the call site; (c) propagate existential method-use effects (`with E'`) at every method invocation on the returned existential; (d) handle unbound-trait existentials identically to unbound-trait `dyn Trait` (caller declares `with _`). Tests land with Phase 8.

- [→ P1] **TAIT — witness inference and opaque cross-package surface.** Full design in [`docs/deferred.md` § P1 § Type Alias `impl Trait` (TAIT) — Witness Inference and Opaque Surface](deferred.md#type-alias-impl-trait-tait--witness-inference-and-opaque-surface). The v1 entry above lands TAIT *declaration* parsing, AST, resolver-side `TaitReference` recording, and the v1 stub that treats TAIT use sites identically to `dyn Trait` of the same trait bound for typechecking. This P1 entry covers: defining-use inference (witness type computed from function bodies returning the alias), same-concrete-type enforcement at the package boundary (`E_TAIT_CONCRETE_MISMATCH`), opaque cross-package surface (consumers see the trait bound, never the witness), generic TAIT instantiations (`type Iter[T] = impl Iterator[Item = T]` with per-instantiation witnesses), inherent-method resolution against the witness inside the defining package, and the diagnostic shape that surfaces the alias name + inferred witness in errors. Replaces the v1 `E_TAIT_NOT_IMPLEMENTED_YET` stub with the real witness-inference pipeline.

- [ ] **`MaybeUninit[T]` + `Pod`-bounded `mem.zeroed`.** **v2 unsafe-track epic** — bundled with the `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` rule entry above and `unsafe extern { }` (further above) as three v2 features sharing the same `unsafe`-keyword infrastructure investment; downstream consumer of the bundle is `get_unchecked` at [`phase-7-codegen.md`](phase-7-codegen.md) line 438 (P2 v2, downgraded 2026-05-10). Implement the spec in `design.md § Unsafe Escape Hatch > Uninitialised Memory: \`MaybeUninit[T]\` only`. Slices: (1) Stdlib type — `MaybeUninit[T]` opaque wrapper sized + aligned like `T` (compiler-known layout intrinsic, since the size/alignment-from-`T` rule cannot be expressed in user Kāra); methods `uninit()`, `zeroed() where T: Pod`, `unsafe assume_init(self) -> T`, `unsafe assume_init_ref(ref self) -> ref T`, `unsafe assume_init_mut(mut ref self) -> mut ref T`, `write(mut ref self, val: T) -> mut ref T`, `as_ptr(ref self) -> *const T`, `as_mut_ptr(mut ref self) -> *mut T`. (2) Stdlib type — `MaybeUninit::uninit_array[T, const N: usize]() -> Array[MaybeUninit[T], N]` (depends on const generics from item 1). (3) `Pod` marker trait in `std.mem` — auto-implemented for `i8`..`u128`, `f32`/`f64`, `bool`, fixed-size arrays of `Pod`, tuples of `Pod`, structs all of whose fields are `Pod` (must be opt-in via `#[derive(Pod)]` to avoid silent extension); explicitly **not** implemented for references, function pointers, `NonZero*`, `char`, enums (no auto-impl on enum types — they must implement manually after the author confirms zero is a valid discriminant). (4) Stdlib function — `mem.zeroed[T]() -> T where T: Pod` returns a fresh zero-filled `T` directly (no `MaybeUninit` wrapper); implemented as a compiler intrinsic that emits a memset to zero. (5) **Negative space** — there is no `mem.uninitialized[T]() -> T`. The stdlib must not export it under any name; the resolver explicitly recognises `std.mem.uninitialized` as an unresolved name with a focused diagnostic pointing at `MaybeUninit[T]::uninit()` instead. (6) Codegen — `MaybeUninit[T]` lowers to a typed-but-uninitialised stack/heap slot of `T`'s size and alignment; `assume_init` is a no-op cast at the LLVM level; `write` is a typed store; `as_ptr` / `as_mut_ptr` are address-of operations. The compiler must mark the underlying storage with the LLVM `freeze` semantics where appropriate to prevent UB-via-undef-bits propagation in optimisation. (7) Test coverage: `MaybeUninit::uninit()` produces a value usable via `write` then `assume_init` round-trip; `MaybeUninit::zeroed() where T: Pod` accepted; `MaybeUninit::zeroed() where T: NonZero[u32]` rejected with a `Pod` bound diagnostic; `mem.zeroed[u8]()` accepted; `mem.zeroed[NonZero[u32]]()` rejected; `mem.zeroed[Option[ref i32]]()` rejected; `import std.mem.uninitialized` rejected with the `MaybeUninit::uninit()` redirect; `unsafe assume_init` requires an `unsafe { }` block per `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` rule; `MaybeUninit::uninit_array` returns the const-generic-sized array form once const generics ship. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features), with the `Pod` derive and `mem.zeroed` intrinsic landing alongside the const-generics work for `MaybeUninit::uninit_array`.

- [x] **`#[non_exhaustive]` on public structs and enums shipped 2026-05-17.** Parser + AST flag + resolver-side placement validation (slices 1+2) shipped 2026-05-16; typechecker cross-package struct-literal enforcement (slice 4 literal half) + enum-exhaustiveness wildcard rule (slice 5) + struct-pattern enforcement (slice 4 pattern half, with `..` rest-pattern enabling change) shipped 2026-05-17; stdlib hygiene lint `missing_non_exhaustive` on the slice-4b cascade (slice 6) shipped 2026-05-17; diagnostic polish — machine-applicable fix-it `replacement` text for the pattern + match diagnostics, introducing the `FixIt` infrastructure on `TypeError` (slice 7) — shipped 2026-05-17. Literal-half fix-it deferred (AST lacks per-brace spans and rewriting requires either source-text access or a multi-edit shape beyond slice 7's surface); the descriptive message at the literal site still steers to `<Name>.new(...)`. Implement the spec in `design.md § \`#[non_exhaustive]\` for Evolvable Public Types`.

  - [x] **Slices 1+2 — parser flag + resolver placement validation shipped 2026-05-16.** Spec sentences honoured: *"Attribute parser — recognize `#[non_exhaustive]` as a type-level attribute on `pub struct` / `pub enum` declarations; reject on private types (the attribute is meaningless when there is no cross-package boundary), on traits, on functions, and on enum variants"* and *"AST — capture as `is_non_exhaustive: bool` on the existing struct/enum item nodes."* The two slices are bundled because the AST field is the parser's storage shape — splitting them would land an unused field for one commit. **AST extension** in `src/ast/items.rs`: `StructDef.is_non_exhaustive: bool` and `EnumDef.is_non_exhaustive: bool`, both defaulted to `false` at every construction site (the parser sets the flag from attribute presence; `prelude.rs`'s `stub_struct` defaults `false`). **Parser wiring** in `src/parser/items.rs`: `parse_struct_def` and `parse_enum_def` both scan their parsed `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` for `name == "non_exhaustive"` and set the flag — same parse-time `iter().any()` shape that the sibling `no_rc` flag on `StructDef` already uses. The parser does not validate placement (no rejection on private types, traits, fns, etc.) — that lives in the resolver per the existing `#[compiler_builtin]` parser/resolver split, so downstream tools that re-parse without a resolver still see the captured attribute. **Resolver placement validation** in `src/resolver/collect.rs`: new `reject_non_exhaustive_attr(attrs, target_kind)` helper emits one `E_NON_EXHAUSTIVE_INVALID_TARGET` diagnostic per `#[non_exhaustive]` attribute on a disallowed item, naming the target kind in the message (`"private struct"`, `"private enum"`, `"function"`, `"trait"`, `"marker trait"`, `"trait alias"`, `"impl block"`, `"impl method"`, `"struct field"`). The kind name is the role string the human reads — not generic "this item is not a pub struct or pub enum" boilerplate. Wired into every `collect_*` site that handles an item with attributes: `collect_function`, `collect_trait`, `collect_trait_alias`, `collect_marker_trait`, `collect_impl` (block + each method), and the two `collect_struct` / `collect_enum` paths (which run the helper *only* when `is_non_exhaustive && !is_pub`, so the canonical `pub struct` / `pub enum` case skips the helper entirely). Struct-field-level rejection runs at the start of `collect_struct` because `StructField` has its own `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` field — Rust accepts variant-level non-exhaustive but the spec ships type-level only at v1, and field-level rejection prevents the silent-ignore failure mode. **Enum-variant-level rejection is structurally impossible** because `Variant` has no `attributes` field at the AST level — attributes between a variant comma and the variant name would fail to attach and produce a parser error elsewhere; explicit rejection isn't needed. **New `ResolveErrorKind::NonExhaustiveInvalidTarget`** in `src/resolver.rs`; mapped to `E0239` in both `src/cli.rs` error-code tables (the diagnostic-emit path at line 705 and the legacy `resolve_error_code` map at line 2708 — both must stay in sync so JSON and text output agree). **Test surface (6 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs`)**: `non_exhaustive_slice1_struct_sets_flag` (basic — `pub struct` with the attribute sets `is_non_exhaustive = true`); `non_exhaustive_slice1_enum_sets_flag` (enum mirror); `non_exhaustive_slice1_struct_without_attribute_has_flag_false` (regression pin — bare `pub struct` keeps `false`); `non_exhaustive_slice1_enum_without_attribute_has_flag_false` (enum mirror); `non_exhaustive_slice1_flag_set_on_private_struct_parser_does_not_reject` (negative pin — parser captures the flag even on private types; the rejection layer is the resolver, not the parser); `non_exhaustive_slice1_coexists_with_other_attributes_on_struct` (the flag is set when `#[non_exhaustive]` appears alongside other attributes like `#[must_use = "..."]`). **Test surface (12 resolver tests in `tests/resolver.rs`)**: `non_exhaustive_slice1_accepted_on_pub_struct` / `..._pub_enum` (positive pins — no diagnostic on legal placement); `non_exhaustive_slice1_rejected_on_private_struct` / `..._private_enum` / `..._non_pub_struct` (rejection on `private struct` / `private enum` / bare module-private `struct`); `non_exhaustive_slice1_rejected_on_function` / `..._trait` / `..._marker_trait` / `..._trait_alias` / `..._impl_block` / `..._struct_field` (rejection on each disallowed item kind, asserting the kind name appears in the diagnostic so the role is unambiguous); `non_exhaustive_slice1_rejection_uses_dedicated_error_kind` (pin that the `ResolveErrorKind::NonExhaustiveInvalidTarget` discriminant is used rather than overloading existing kinds, AND that the message carries the symbolic `E_NON_EXHAUSTIVE_INVALID_TARGET` prefix for CLI/IDE consumers). **What slices 1+2 do *not* do.** No cross-package literal-or-pattern checks (slice 4 — typechecker enforces wildcard / `..` requirement); no exhaustiveness-checker wildcard rule for cross-package non-exhaustive enums (slice 5); no stdlib hygiene lint (slice 6, blocked on the lint registry at line 379); no fix-it `replacement` text (slice 7 polish — the resolver's `replacement` shape doesn't support multi-edit fix-its that the spec's `Struct.new(...)` constructor rewrite would need). The parser-captured flag is structurally complete for any downstream pass that wants to consult it — slices 4 and 5 just have to read `is_non_exhaustive` and the defining-package id (already available via existing resolver metadata). (3) Resolver — record the flag on each defining package's exported type metadata so cross-package consumers can read it. (4) Typechecker — for struct literal expressions and exhaustive struct patterns (no `..`) where the struct's defining package differs from the current package and the struct is `#[non_exhaustive]`, emit a focused error with a fix-it: literal → `Struct.new(...)` (named-arg call) when a `pub fn new` exists; pattern → insert `..` before the closing brace. (5) Exhaustiveness checker — when matching on a value whose enum type is `#[non_exhaustive]` and defined in a different package, the wildcard requirement is unconditional regardless of which variants are covered; emit the existing non-exhaustive-match diagnostic with a fix-it inserting `_ => todo!("handle new variant")`. The check is package-relative: same-package matches are checked normally so local code catches "you added a variant and forgot to handle it". (6) Stdlib hygiene lint (new) — `missing_non_exhaustive` warning that fires on a stdlib `pub enum` whose name ends in `Error` or whose declared role is "stdlib error enum" and which lacks `#[non_exhaustive]`; the lint is `deny`-by-default for stdlib crates and `allow` for user code. The list of "must-have" types is enforced by reviewer judgement plus the lint heuristic — not a hard rule baked into the compiler. (7) Diagnostics — every error from this feature must distinguish "this type is `#[non_exhaustive]`, you must use a wildcard / `..` / constructor" from the unrelated "you forgot a variant" or "you forgot a field" cases; the wording must explicitly tell the reader the type is `#[non_exhaustive]` and link to the design.md section. Test coverage: external `match` on `#[non_exhaustive]` enum without wildcard rejected with the typed diagnostic; same with wildcard accepted; same-package `match` on the same enum without wildcard rejected via the normal exhaustiveness rule (not the `#[non_exhaustive]` rule); external struct literal on `#[non_exhaustive]` struct rejected with the constructor-fix-it; external struct pattern without `..` rejected; external struct pattern with `..` accepted; same-package literal and exhaustive pattern accepted; attribute on a private type rejected; attribute on a trait rejected; attribute on a function rejected; new error-variant additions on a stdlib `#[non_exhaustive]` enum compile cleanly across a cross-package consumer that uses a wildcard arm; `missing_non_exhaustive` lint fires on a stdlib `pub enum FooError` lacking the attribute and is silent on a user-package `pub enum BarError` lacking it. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features).

  - [x] **Slice 4 — literal half (2026-05-17) + pattern half with `..` rest-pattern enabling change (2026-05-17) both shipped.** Spec sentence honoured for the literal half: *"Typechecker — for struct literal expressions ... where the struct's defining package differs from the current package and the struct is `#[non_exhaustive]`, emit a focused error with a fix-it: literal → `Struct.new(...)` (named-arg call) when a `pub fn new` exists."* **`StructInfo` extension** in `src/typechecker/env.rs`: two new fields — `is_non_exhaustive: bool` (mirrors `StructDef.is_non_exhaustive`) and `defining_stdlib_origin: bool` (mirrors `StructDef.stdlib_origin`). Populated in every `StructInfo` construction site in `src/typechecker/env_build.rs`: the regular `env_add_struct` reads both flags from the `StructDef`, the slice-1 prelude-bake pre-pass in `register_builtin_types` and the type-method scaffolding site default `is_non_exhaustive: false, defining_stdlib_origin: true` (built-in / range types are stdlib-internal scaffolding and never reach the cross-package check). **`current_fn_stdlib_origin: bool`** on `TypeChecker` (`src/typechecker.rs`): defaults `false` at construction; saved/restored across every `check_function` call (`src/typechecker/items.rs`) based on `f.stdlib_origin`. Save/restore is symmetric with the existing `current_return_type` / `current_self_type` / `enclosing_bounds` patterns — nested item walks (impl methods inside a stdlib impl block, trait default-body synthesized functions) propagate the inner function's origin during body checking and unwind to the outer on return. **Cross-package check** in `infer_struct_literal` (`src/typechecker/fields.rs`): after the existing field-validation pass, if `info.is_non_exhaustive && info.defining_stdlib_origin && !self.current_fn_stdlib_origin`, emit `error[E_NON_EXHAUSTIVE_CROSS_PACKAGE_LITERAL]` naming the struct and suggesting the `<Name>.new(...)` constructor fix-it.
