Both functions call `scan_deprecated_attr` and store the payload on the AST node. **Resolver placement validation** in `src/resolver/collect.rs`: `collect_const` and `collect_type_alias` both call `reject_non_exhaustive_attr(attrs, "module const" / "type alias")` and `reject_track_caller_attr(attrs, ...)` — neither attribute is legal on these item kinds (`#[non_exhaustive]` is type-level only on `pub struct` / `pub enum`; `#[track_caller]` is fn-only). `#[deprecated]` is accepted on both (spec-listed targets); no rejection helper is called for it. **Test surface (5 parser tests + 6 resolver tests)** covering positive payload capture, regression pins (no attribute → empty field), the long-form deprecation shape, and the four cross-product rejection sites. **What this entry does *not* do.** No use-site `#[deprecated]` warning emission on consts / type aliases (still blocked on lint emission infrastructure — slice 4 of the lint-level-attributes entry at line 385). No `lint_overrides` field on `ConstDecl`/`TypeAliasDef` (slice 4 of lint-level entry will add it across all attribute-bearing nodes alongside the cascade). The parser-captured `deprecation` field is structurally complete; the warning emission will read it once the cascade infrastructure lands.

- [x] **Identifier case-class enforcement.** Enforce the case-class rule specified in `design.md § Identifiers and Naming`. Lexer classifies each `Ident` token as Type / Const / Value by its character pattern (see `syntax.md §1.5`). Parser checks the class at every declaration site — `struct` / `enum` / `trait` / `type` / `distinct` / generic param / const generic param / associated type / `effect resource` require Type-class; `fn` / function-body `let` / param / field / `mod` / `layout` / effect group / effect verb require Value-class; `const` requires Const-class. Mismatch emits a structured diagnostic with position-aware wording and a suggested rename. `#[kara_name = "..."]` attribute on `extern` items provides the FFI escape hatch (CN-7). Non-ASCII identifiers remain a parse error (Unicode deferred). No-op for existing codebase — all current Kāra source already follows the convention. Test coverage for every site in `tests/parser.rs` (snake_case struct/enum/variant/trait/type-alias rejected, PascalCase fn/param/field/extern-fn rejected, snake_case const-generic/assoc-type/generic-param rejected, PascalCase layout name rejected, single-upper Type-class accepted, leading-underscore Value-class accepted, `#[kara_name]` skip-check accepted, let-binding deferred to resolver).

- [~] **`#[profile(P1, P2, ...)]` attribute.** Function/module attribute asserting compatibility with a specific set of project profiles. Compile error if the function's transitive effect set isn't compatible with the *intersection* of the listed profiles' constraints (function must satisfy the strictest constraint from any listed profile). Slices 1+2 (parser + AST + resolver validation) shipped 2026-05-18 — see sub-bullet below. Slice 3 (effect-checker integration) shipped 2026-05-18 — see sub-bullet below. The spec also references `kara.toml`'s `profiles = [...]` vocabulary; the current manifest carries a singular `[package].profile = "..."` field — see the `[->]` sub-bullet below for the deferral. Stdlib `core` layer is the first major user; portability marking becomes structural rather than convention-based. The attribute name `profile` is chosen over `profile_compatible` for consistency with `kara.toml`'s `profiles = [...]` vocabulary.

  - [x] **Slices 1+2 — parser + AST + resolver validation shipped 2026-05-18.** Spec sentences honoured: *"Parser: recognize `#[profile(...)]` with comma-separated profile name list."* and *"Resolver: validate names against profiles defined in `kara.toml`; unknown names are a parse-level diagnostic."* **AST extension** in `src/ast/items.rs`: `Function.profile_compat: Vec<String>`, defaulted to `Vec::new()` at every construction site (parser sets the list from attribute presence; the synthesized stubs in `prelude.rs::stub_function`, `typechecker/items.rs`, `effectchecker.rs`, `effectchecker/bounds.rs` all default empty — none represent user-authored functions). **Parser wiring** in `src/parser/items.rs`: new `pub(crate) fn scan_profile_attr(attrs) -> Vec<String>` reads bare positional identifiers across all `#[profile(...)]` occurrences on the function and accumulates into a single list (slice 3 dedupes at intersection-compute time). Reject everything else with focused parse diagnostics: `E_PROFILE_NO_PROFILES` (empty arg list / bare `#[profile]`), `E_PROFILE_STRING_VALUE` (`#[profile = "..."]` shorthand or `#[profile("embedded")]` string positional), `E_PROFILE_NAMED_ARG` (`#[profile(name: embedded)]` / `#[profile(name = embedded)]`), `E_PROFILE_NON_IDENT_ARG` (any other expression — integer, bool, struct literal, …). Duplicates within one attribute (`#[profile(a, a)]`) tolerated at parse — slice 3 dedupes. **Resolver placement validation** in `src/resolver/collect.rs`: new `reject_profile_attr(attrs, target_kind)` mirrors `reject_track_caller_attr` and is wired into every non-fn `collect_*` site (`collect_struct` block + field, `collect_enum` block + variant, `collect_trait`, `collect_trait_alias`, `collect_marker_trait`, `collect_impl`, `collect_const`, `collect_type_alias`); produces `error[E_PROFILE_INVALID_TARGET]` naming the target kind. New `validate_profile_names(f)` walks `f.profile_compat` against the closed v1 set (`default` / `embedded` / `kernel`, mirroring `CompileProfile` from `src/manifest.rs`) and emits `error[E_UNKNOWN_PROFILE]` on each unknown name; the diagnostic lists the valid set and anchors at the function's span (per-arg span tracking is a future refinement once the scan helper threads it through). **New `ResolveErrorKind::ProfileInvalidTarget` + `UnknownProfile`** in `src/resolver.rs`; mapped to `E0244` / `E0245` in both `src/cli.rs` error-code tables (the diagnostic-emit path and the legacy `resolve_error_code` map — both stay in sync per the established pattern). **Test surface (10 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs::profile_slice1_*`)**: `single_profile_captured` (basic — one profile in the list); `multi_profile_captured` (`#[profile(embedded, kernel)]` → both names); `absent_attribute_leaves_empty` (regression pin); `multiple_attributes_accumulate` (two `#[profile]` attributes append into one list); `rejects_empty_arg_list` / `rejects_string_shorthand` / `rejects_string_positional` / `rejects_named_arg` / `rejects_integer_arg` (one per malformed shape, each pinning the specific symbolic-code emission); `set_on_non_fn_item_parser_does_not_reject` (parser captures uniformly; placement rejection is the resolver's job). **Test surface (13 resolver tests in `tests/resolver.rs::profile_slice12_*`)**: `accepted_on_function_with_known_profile` / `accepted_on_function_with_all_three_known` (positive pins for each known profile and all-three combination); `rejects_unknown_profile_name` (basic unknown — names the offending profile and emits the symbolic code); `unknown_diagnostic_lists_valid_profiles` (the diagnostic enumerates `default` / `embedded` / `kernel` so the user can self-correct); `rejects_one_unknown_among_known` (per-name checking; one bad name doesn't suppress good ones); `rejected_on_struct` / `..._enum` / `..._trait` / `..._impl_block` / `..._module_const` / `..._type_alias` / `..._struct_field` (rejection at each disallowed site, asserting the kind name appears in the message); `rejection_uses_dedicated_error_kinds` (pin that both new discriminants round-trip). **What slices 1+2 do *not* do.** No effect-checker integration — the `profile_compat` list is structurally captured but no per-call constraint check fires (slice 3). No module-level placement — `#[profile]` on a module is part of the spec but blocked on the module-attribute AST surface (separate enabling change). No `kara.toml`-driven validation — the resolver validates against the closed `CompileProfile` enum since the manifest carries a singular `profile` field today (see `[->]` below). Phase target: 5.2.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — effect-checker integration shipped 2026-05-18.** Spec sentence honoured: *"Effect checker: for each function with `#[profile(...)]`, intersect the listed profiles' constraint sets and check the function's transitive effect set against the intersection; emit a focused diagnostic on any forbidden effect."* **New module** `src/effectchecker/profile_compat.rs` houses `check_profile_compat(&mut self)` plus the free helper `profile_forbids_effect(CompileProfile, &Effect) -> bool`. The helper duplicates the per-profile forbidden-effect table from `extern_ffi::profile_forbids` but is keyed on an explicit `CompileProfile` argument rather than `self.profile` — the attribute names target profiles independent of the active build profile, and the two checks now have distinct surfaces (`ProfileViolation` for extern declarations under the build profile, `ProfileIncompatibleEffect` for `#[profile(...)]`-annotated functions under any listed profile). The forbidden tables agree by construction: `default` forbids nothing, `embedded` forbids `allocates(Heap)`, `kernel` forbids `allocates(*)` / `panics` / `blocks` / `suspends`. **Walker shape** mirrors the `missing_track_caller` lint: walk every `Item::Function` and every `Item::ImplBlock` inherent-or-trait-method (both are kept — the attribute is structurally valid on both, and the resolver does not distinguish). Inherent methods key as `Type.method` to match the `inferred_effects` lookup convention; free fns key as `name`. Functions with empty `profile_compat` skip; functions whose declared profile list contains an unknown name skip entirely (the resolver already emitted `E_UNKNOWN_PROFILE`, so we don't pile a stale-data effect error on top). **Dedup** is done at check time — `#[profile(embedded, embedded)]` or two `#[profile]` attrs naming the same profile collapse to one constraint contributor, so one diagnostic per offending effect is emitted regardless of duplication. **Effect-source selection.** The check reads `self.inferred_effects[key]` — by Phase A's `collect_function_info` seeding, this map contains the declared set for `Explicit` declarations *and* the inferred propagation result, so a function declaring `with allocates(Heap)` and a function inferring `allocates(Heap)` from a `Vec.new()` call both surface the same way. The check runs in Phase B after `check_with_e_unification` so the inferred set is fully settled. **New `EffectErrorKind::ProfileIncompatibleEffect`** in `src/effectchecker.rs`; mapped to `E0407` in `src/cli.rs` (the per-effect-error mapping table — the legacy duplicate path inherited the same variant via the exhaustive match, so no second site needs touching). **Diagnostic shape.** One error per offending effect, naming the function, the declared profile list, the effect (with resource in parens for resource verbs), and the profile(s) that forbid it. When only one listed profile forbids the effect the diagnostic reads `forbidden by the \`<P>\` profile`; when two or more forbid it the phrasing shifts to `forbidden by the strictest of \`P1, P2, …\` (forbidden by \`P_a\`, \`P_b\`, …)` so the user sees the tightening came from the intersection rather than a single profile. **Test surface (17 effect-checker tests in `tests/effectchecker.rs::profile_slice3_*`)**: `default_allows_all_effects_via_attribute` (default-profile baseline — `allocates(Heap)` accepted); `embedded_accepts_pure_function` (no effects, no violation); `embedded_rejects_heap_allocates` (the canonical case — message asserts symbolic code, fn name, profile name, effect rendering); `embedded_allows_non_heap_allocates` (user-defined resource `Arena` passes `embedded` since only `Heap` is forbidden); `kernel_rejects_panics` / `kernel_rejects_blocks` / `kernel_rejects_suspends` / `kernel_rejects_allocates_any_resource` (one per kernel-forbidden verb — `blocks` is triggered via an `extern "C"` call to inherit the ABI default, `suspends` via `Receiver.recv()`, `panics` via `todo()`, `allocates(Arena)` via a declared effect); `intersection_tightens_one_profile_forbids` (`#[profile(embedded, kernel)]` + `panics` — only `kernel` forbids, diagnostic names `the \`kernel\` profile` and echoes the full declared list); `intersection_tightens_multiple_profiles_forbid` (`#[profile(embedded, kernel)]` + `allocates(Heap)` — both forbid, "strictest of" phrasing kicks in); `two_offending_effects_yield_two_errors` (per-effect granularity — two diagnostics for `allocates(Heap)` + `panics` under `kernel`); `inherent_method_checked` (`Type.method` key shape — method-level violation surfaces with the type-qualified name); `inferred_effect_drives_check` (the declared list is empty but inferred carries `allocates(Heap)` from a `Vec.new()` call — confirms the post-inference map is the source of truth); `unknown_profile_skips_check` (`#[profile(yolo)]` produces no profile-compat diagnostic since the resolver already errored); `dedupe_within_attr` (duplicate profile names emit one diagnostic, not two); `diagnostic_uses_dedicated_error_kind` (kind discriminant round-trip); `absent_attribute_silent` (functions without `#[profile]` never produce profile-compat diagnostics regardless of their effect set). **What slice 3 does *not* do.** No module-level enforcement — the attribute is still function-only at the AST level, so a module-level `#[profile(...)]` is still parser-blocked. No `kara.toml`-driven validation — see the `[->]` sub-bullet below. Phase target: 5.2.

  - [ ] **Sub-open — `kara.toml` `profiles = [...]` array.** The spec entry references `kara.toml`'s `profiles = [...]` vocabulary, but the current manifest carries a singular `[package].profile = "..."` field (single profile per package, not an array). Adding a manifest-level `profiles` array is a separate enabling change; until it lands, the resolver validates against the closed `CompileProfile` enum's known set. Reopen condition: user request for multi-profile package declarations or a custom-profile mechanism beyond the three built-ins.

- [x] **C-string literals `c"..."` — lex acceptance.** Spec lives at design.md § C-String Literals (v60 item 18). Today the lexer rejects `c"..."` with a focused diagnostic that points at the spec ("specced for v1 but lex acceptance lands in Phase 5.2"); the work here is to graduate the prefix from rejected to recognized. Sub-steps: (1) `Token::CStringLiteral { bytes: Vec<u8>, source_len: i64 }` variant in `src/token.rs` — `bytes` excludes the trailing NUL (the codegen layer appends it); `source_len` records the textual length for `len()` / `as_bytes()` introspection without re-walking. (2) Lexer dispatch arm — add `b'c' if self.peek() == b'"' => self.c_string()` between the existing `f"`-arm and the reserved-prefix catch-all. (3) `c_string()` method — body parsing identical to `string()` plus the `\xHH` hex-byte escape (already implemented for byte-literals, lift the helper); `\u{...}` Unicode escapes encode to UTF-8 bytes. (4) Interior-NUL guard — any escape that produces a `0x00` byte (`\0`, `\x00`, `\u{0}`) is a lex error `error[E_INTERIOR_NUL_IN_C_STRING]` with the message from design.md, pointing at the offending escape. (5) Update the existing `test_v60_reserved_string_prefix_diagnostic` in `tests/lexer.rs` to drop the Phase-5.2-gating diagnostic and add positive lex tests for the new token shape (empty, ASCII, escape sequences, Unicode escapes producing multi-byte UTF-8). Parser handling and the stdlib `CStr` / `CString` types ship in Phase 8 (see follow-up entry below); this Phase 5.2 entry is lex-level only. (Phase 5.2 — items 3, 18, 22 land together as the FFI-tightening cluster.)

- [~] **Field offsets `offset_of[T](field)` + `ptr.container_of` / `ptr.container_of_mut`.** Spec lives at design.md § Field Offsets (v60 item 25). The `offset_of` intrinsic shipped earlier (parser + typechecker + codegen + tests) — see the `[x]` sub-bullet below. The `ptr.container_of` / `ptr.container_of_mut` stdlib helpers remain open and are soft-blocked on the strict-provenance APIs at line 511 — see the `[ ]` sub-bullet below.

  - [x] **`offset_of[T](field.path)` intrinsic shipped.** Parser special-form in `src/parser/stmts.rs::parse_offset_of_special_form`, dispatched from `src/parser/exprs.rs:1130` when an identifier `offset_of` is followed by `[`. Argument grammar is `FIELD_PATH = IDENT ("." IDENT)*` parsed as a dotted identifier sequence, *not* as an expression — indexing / method calls / dereferences inside the parens are rejected at parse with `error[E_OFFSET_OF_INVALID_PATH]`. **AST** `ExprKind::OffsetOf { ty: TypeExpr, field_path: Vec<String> }` in `src/ast/exprs.rs:229`. **Typechecker** `infer_offset_of` in `src/typechecker/expr_ops.rs:42` walks each path segment against `env.structs`, descending into nested struct field types; result type is `usize`. **Diagnostic family**: `E_OFFSET_OF_GENERIC_PARAM` (type-parameter target), `E_OFFSET_OF_OPAQUE_TYPE` (opaque foreign type — consulted via `env.opaque_foreign_types`), `E_OFFSET_OF_NON_STRUCT_TARGET` (primitives, enums, walk-into-non-struct on a nested segment), `E_OFFSET_OF_INVALID_PATH` (empty path or non-identifier segment forms — parser-side), `E_OFFSET_OF_UNKNOWN_FIELD` (segment doesn't name a field on the current struct; diagnostic enumerates the available field names). Private-field access from outside the defining module routes through the standard `check_cross_module_field_access` rather than a dedicated `E_OFFSET_OF_PRIVATE_FIELD` (the standard cross-module field-access diagnostic is what fires — same load-bearing surface, different symbolic code). **Const-evaluator** path: `compile_offset_of` in `src/codegen/exprs.rs:324` lowers to a literal `usize` constant via inkwell's `TargetData::offset_of_element` (chained across nested segments); no runtime arithmetic is emitted. Because the LLVM struct type the codegen consults is the post-layout-transformation type, layout-block SoA-transformed structs return the runtime (physical) offset automatically — no special-casing needed. **Test surface** (`tests/typechecker.rs::test_offset_of_*`): returns usize, first field, nested path, unknown field rejected, opaque type rejected, non-struct rejected, walk-into-non-struct rejected, indexing-form parser-rejected, call-form parser-rejected. E2E codegen tests in `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_offset_of_*`: first field == 0 with `#[repr(C)]`, second field, nested path. **Sub-opens** still attached to this half: (a) no `W_OFFSET_OF_UNION_FIELD` warning — depends on union support landing at line 515; (b) no explicit regression test for the SoA layout-block case — the behaviour is correct by construction (TargetData walks the lowered type) but a pinned test would catch a future layout-pipeline regression; (c) no dedicated `E_OFFSET_OF_ENUM_VARIANT` / `E_OFFSET_OF_PRIVATE_FIELD` symbolic codes — the funneling through `E_OFFSET_OF_NON_STRUCT_TARGET` / `check_cross_module_field_access` is intentional today, but if the diagnostic catalogue is curated for stable symbolic codes per kind, splitting these out is a cosmetic follow-up.

  - [ ] **`ptr.container_of` / `ptr.container_of_mut` stdlib helpers — soft-blocked on line 511 (strict-provenance APIs).** Generic functions in the prelude `ptr` module: `unsafe fn container_of[T, F](field_ptr: *const F, field: <field-path>) -> *const T` and the `_mut` variant. The `field` argument uses the same special-form field-path syntax as `offset_of`. Spec-mandated lowering is `field_ptr.with_addr(field_ptr.addr() - offset_of[T](field))`, leveraging the strict-provenance APIs from line 511 to keep the address arithmetic provenance-preserving. The `unsafe` marker carries the precondition "field_ptr actually points at the named field of an enclosing T". **Why blocked rather than ship-now-refactor-later:** the spec's lowering is the provenance-correct one, and writing an interim lowering with bare `ptrtoint` / `inttoptr` would either bake in a soundness gap or require a rewrite once line 511 lands — both worse than carrying the deferral. **Reopen condition:** line 511 (strict-provenance APIs) ships. Once `with_addr` / `addr` are stdlib functions, this slice is a thin layer: parser special-form sharing the `offset_of` field-path machinery, typechecker dispatch into the `ptr` module, lowering to the `with_addr` call chain. Test plan from the original entry stays applicable: container_of round-trip recovers the enclosing struct pointer; transparent carrier returns 0; rejection at non-place / non-struct / opaque-type / generic-param sites. (Phase 5.2 — typechecker work.)

- [~] **Strict-provenance pointer APIs `ptr.addr` / `ptr.with_addr` / `ptr.expose` / `ptr.from_exposed`.** Spec lives at design.md § Pointer Provenance (v60 item 20). Slices 1 (cast rejection) and 2 (stdlib `ptr` API surface) shipped 2026-05-18 — see sub-bullets below. Slice 3 (codegen lowering) remains open and blocks end-to-end execution of round-trip patterns; typechecker-side acceptance is complete.

  - [x] **Slice 1 — `ptr ↔ int` cast rejection shipped 2026-05-18.** Spec sentences honoured: *"Cast-rejection — extend the existing `as`-cast typechecker to reject all four `ptr ↔ usize` casts."* The rule is widened to **any integer width**, not just `usize` — otherwise users could circumvent strict-provenance via an intermediate `as u32` / `as i64` cast. **Implementation** in `src/typechecker.rs::check_cast_pair`: two new arms placed immediately before the generic-fallthrough. `Type::Pointer { .. } as integer` emits `error[E_PTR_TO_INT_CAST_FORBIDDEN]` naming both `ptr.addr(p)` (the safer default) and `ptr.expose(p)` (the round-trip case) so the user can pick the right primitive without reading the spec. `integer as Type::Pointer { .. }` emits `error[E_INT_TO_PTR_CAST_FORBIDDEN]` naming both `ptr.with_addr(base, addr)` (reseat-existing-pointer form) and `ptr.from_exposed[T](addr)` (round-trip form) — the spec deliberately leaves the choice to the user since the compiler can't reliably guess which is in scope. Both diagnostics use `TypeErrorKind::InvalidCast` (mapped to `E0210` in `src/cli.rs`) — the symbolic code lives in the message body per the existing convention used by `E_CHAR_AS_NARROW_INT` / `E_INT_AS_CHAR` / `E_INT_AS_BOOL` / `E_FLOAT_AS_BOOL`. **Test surface (8 tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::provenance_slice1_*`)**: `ptr_const_as_usize_rejected` / `ptr_mut_as_usize_rejected` (the canonical `usize` cases); `ptr_as_i64_also_rejected` (confirms the rule covers non-`usize` integer widths — the design intent that a user can't circumvent via intermediate cast); `usize_as_ptr_const_rejected` / `usize_as_ptr_mut_rejected` (reverse direction); `int_as_int_still_accepted` (regression pin — usize widening / narrowing still works); `diagnostic_names_ptr_addr_suggestion` (E_PTR_TO_INT diagnostic surfaces both `ptr.addr` and `ptr.expose`); `diagnostic_names_with_addr_and_from_exposed` (E_INT_TO_PTR diagnostic surfaces both `ptr.with_addr` and `ptr.from_exposed`). **What slice 1 does *not* do.** No stdlib `ptr` API — the diagnostic messages name `ptr.addr` / `ptr.expose` / `ptr.with_addr` / `ptr.from_exposed` but those functions are not yet callable; that surface lands in slice 2. No `&T → *_ T` reference-to-raw cast rejection — tracked under line 517 (the raw-pointer-construction entry); the spec calls that `E_REF_TO_RAW_PTR_CAST_FORBIDDEN` and the ergonomic story is `ptr.const(...)` / `ptr.mut(...)` which is also part of line 517. Raw-to-raw casts (`*const T as *mut T` etc.) currently funnel through the generic-fallthrough "cannot cast" diagnostic — out of scope for slice 1 (they're not in the strict-provenance forbidden set).

  - [x] **Slice 2 — stdlib `ptr` API surface shipped 2026-05-18.** Spec sentence honoured: *"Stdlib `ptr` module — generic functions `addr` / `with_addr` / `with_addr_mut` / `expose` / `expose_mut` / `from_exposed` (unsafe) / `from_exposed_mut` (unsafe)."* **`ptr` module registration**: `src/resolver.rs` adds `push(self, "ptr", SymbolKind::Module)` alongside the existing `env` / `process` magic modules — local bindings named `ptr` shadow the module per the standard scope rules. **Seven function signatures** in `src/typechecker/env_build.rs` (sibling to `env.var` / `process.exit`): `ptr.addr` / `ptr.expose` (`[T](p: *const T) -> usize`), `ptr.expose_mut` (`[T](p: *mut T) -> usize`), `ptr.with_addr` / `ptr.with_addr_mut` (`[T](p, addr: usize) -> *const T` / `*mut T`), `ptr.from_exposed` / `ptr.from_exposed_mut` (`[T](addr: usize) -> *const T` / `*mut T`). Function names cannot syntactically contain `.`, so the entries are registered programmatically rather than as baked `.kara` source — the same pattern `env.var` / `process.exit` use. **Method-call dispatch** in `src/typechecker/expr_method_call.rs::infer_method_call`: the parser produces `MethodCall { object: Ident("ptr"), method: "addr" }` for `ptr.addr(p)`, so a new `ptr` arm routes through `check_call_args_with_substitution_full` — the full generic-aware path. The simpler `env` arm uses `check_assignable` directly, which would silently accept any argument against a `*const T` slot because `(Type::TypeParam(_), _) => true` in `types_compatible`; the full-substitution path instantiates `T` to a fresh metavar so the outer `*const ?T` shape unifies properly. **Type-system substrate** in `src/typechecker/inference.rs::unify_types` and `src/typechecker/types.rs::types_compatible`: missing `Type::Pointer` arms added (mutability must match — `*const T` does not unify with `*mut T`; the strict-provenance APIs `with_addr` / `with_addr_mut` provide the explicit constness-conversion path). Without these arms `unify_types(*const ?T0, *const i64)` fell through to the wildcard-false branch, so `?T0` never bound — generic-aware ptr dispatch surfaced this gap. **Unsafe enforcement** in `src/unsafe_lint.rs`: `top_level_unsafe` seeded with `"ptr.from_exposed"` and `"ptr.from_exposed_mut"`; the `OpWalker::MethodCall` arm extended to match the dotted name (`format!("{mod}.{method}")`) against the registry when the object is a bare `Identifier`, treating the leading identifier as a magic module rather than a value. The path-form callee arm (`OpWalker::Call` with `ExprKind::Path` callee) also joins segments with `.` — covers the explicit-generic-args form `ptr.from_exposed[T](addr)` if it ever lands. The diagnostic shape matches the existing `Vec.get_unchecked` precedent: lint name `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn`, help text directs the user to wrap in `unsafe { ... }` with a `// Safety:` comment. **Test surface (9 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::provenance_slice2_*` + 7 unsafe-lint tests in `tests/unsafe_lint.rs::test_ptr_*`)**: typechecker — each of the seven functions accepts the correct argument shape and returns the correct type; round-trip pattern `with_addr(p, addr(p) | 1)` typechecks; wrong-argument-type rejected (regression pin against the `(TypeParam, _) => true` permissiveness bug). Unsafe-lint — `ptr.from_exposed` / `ptr.from_exposed_mut` outside `unsafe { }` produce the expected diagnostic; both inside `unsafe { }` are silent; `ptr.addr` / `ptr.with_addr` / `ptr.expose` are safe and produce no diagnostic regardless of context. **What slice 2 does *not* do.** No codegen lowering — calls typecheck but `cargo run` won't actually execute them (slice 3 ships the LLVM `ptrtoint` / `inttoptr` lowering with provenance metadata). No explicit-generic-args path-form (`ptr.from_exposed[i64](addr)` doesn't bind T via the `[T]` syntax — T is inferred from the return-type context, which works for every realistic use site). No effect-system declaration — the seven functions have no declared effects; if a future spec entry assigns them an effect (e.g. `expose` could be argued to belong in a `reads(Provenance)` category), the seeding lives next to the env.functions registration and is a one-line change. (Phase 5.2 — typechecker work.)

  - [ ] **Slice 3 — codegen lowering.** `addr` and `with_addr` lower to LLVM `ptrtoint` / `inttoptr` with provenance-preserving metadata (`!provenance.preserve` markers when supported; otherwise plain `inttoptr` with the existing alias-analysis annotations). `expose` and `from_exposed` lower to the same instructions but mark the source pointer as having escaped via `noalias` invalidation. The unsafe marker on `from_exposed` is a typecheck-only check (slice 2); codegen treats both equally. Test plan: positive — read-back via `addr` matches the original pointer's address bits; `with_addr(p, addr(p) | 1)` round-trips through `with_addr(_, _ & !1)`; `expose` followed by `from_exposed` round-trips a stored address. (Phase 7-adjacent — codegen substrate.)

- [ ] **Opaque foreign types — `extern "C" { type Foo; }`.** Spec lives at design.md § Opaque Foreign Types (v60 item 24). Sub-steps: (1) Parser — extend the `unsafe extern "ABI" { ... }` block grammar so each item may be either a foreign-function declaration (existing) or an opaque-type declaration `type IDENT ;` (new). Reject generic forms `type Foo[T];` at parse with `error[E_OPAQUE_TYPE_GENERIC_FORBIDDEN]`. AST: new `ExternItem::OpaqueType { name, attrs, vis, span }`. (2) Resolver — register the opaque type name in the type namespace at the enclosing module's level (visibility from the declaration). Multiple declarations of the same opaque-type name across blocks/files emit `warning[W_OPAQUE_TYPE_REDECLARED]` rather than an error — the C side has the final word; duplicate declarations are noisy but not unsound. (3) Typechecker — model opaque types as a new `Type::OpaqueExtern { name, ... }` variant with sizing flag `Sized = false`. The pointer-only constraint is enforced at every use site: a place or value of opaque-extern type that is *not* behind `*const T` / `*mut T` / `ref T` / `mut ref T` is rejected with `error[E_OPAQUE_TYPE_REQUIRES_INDIRECTION]` (covers by-value lets, by-value parameters, by-value returns, struct fields, array element types, and any other non-indirect occurrence). Field access and method calls on a value of opaque-extern type are rejected with `error[E_OPAQUE_TYPE_NO_FIELDS]` / `error[E_OPAQUE_TYPE_NO_METHODS]`. `size_of[Foo]()` and `align_of[Foo]()` are rejected with `error[E_OPAQUE_TYPE_NO_KNOWN_SIZE]`. `impl ... for Foo` (inherent or trait) blocks are rejected with `error[E_OPAQUE_TYPE_NO_INHERENT_OR_TRAIT_IMPLS]` — the wrapper-type pattern (`distinct type SafeFile = *mut FILE; impl Drop for SafeFile { ... }`) is the supported alternative. `#[derive(...)]` is rejected with the same diagnostic family. `ptr.const(...)` / `ptr.mut(...)` on an opaque-type place fails the place-validator with the standard E_PTR_CONST_REQUIRES_PLACE diagnostic — a place of opaque type cannot exist in the first place because by-value bindings are forbidden. (4) Codegen — opaque-extern types lower to LLVM's incomplete struct type (`%struct.Foo = type opaque`), used only as the pointee in `*const T` / `*mut T` types; no allocation or memory operation is ever emitted on an opaque type directly. (5) Effect integration — opaque type declarations contribute no effects; functions in the same `unsafe extern { }` block that take or return pointers to the opaque type follow the standard FFI effect-declaration rules. (6) Linker integration — opaque-type declarations emit no linker symbols (the type is the C side's; only function bindings produce import symbols). Test plan: positive — `extern "C" { type FILE; }` plus `fopen`/`fclose` signatures parse, type-check, and round-trip a `*mut FILE` through Kāra code; the `SafeFile` wrapper-type pattern compiles; the same opaque type declared twice (different files) emits the redeclare warning and resolves to one type. Negative — by-value `let f: FILE = ...` rejected; by-value parameter `fn f(x: FILE)` rejected; field-of-struct `struct S { f: FILE }` rejected; field access `(*ptr).x` where ptr: *mut FILE is rejected (no fields known); `size_of[FILE]()` rejected; `impl Display for FILE` rejected; `extern "C" { type Foo[T]; }` parser-rejected; `#[derive(Debug)] type FILE` rejected. (Phase 5.2 — typechecker work; lexer/parser change lands together. Items 3, 18, 22, 24 cluster together as the FFI-tightening cluster.)

- [ ] **FFI unions — `union Foo { ... }`.** Spec lives at design.md § FFI Unions (v60 item 22). Sub-steps: (1) Lexer — add `union` to the keyword arm in `src/lexer.rs` (currently a free identifier). The keyword token kind is unconditional; there is no contextual-keyword treatment because every legitimate use is at item position. (2) Parser — accept `UNION_DEF` per syntax.md § 3.3a alongside `STRUCT_DEF` and `ENUM_DEF`. AST: new `Item::Union { name, attrs, vis, fields, span }` variant carrying a `Vec<UnionField { name, ty, vis, span }>`. Reject empty fields-list at parse with `error[E_EMPTY_UNION]`. Reject tuple-style (`union Foo(T, U)`) and generic (`union Foo[T] { ... }`) forms at parse — neither has a v1 use case. (3) Resolver — register `Foo` in the type namespace; resolve field types in the enclosing scope. (4) Typechecker — required-`#[repr(C)]` check at union-decl time produces `error[E_UNION_REQUIRES_REPR]` if absent (also accepts `#[repr(C, packed)]`). Per-field `Copy`/`Pod` bound check produces `error[E_UNION_FIELD_NOT_COPY]` naming the offending field's type. Reject `impl Drop for Foo` on a union type (`error[E_UNION_DROP_FORBIDDEN]`). Reject `#[derive(...)]` on a union (`error[E_UNION_DERIVE_FORBIDDEN]` — the diagnostic enumerates the rejected derives). Reject `#[non_exhaustive]` (`error[E_UNION_NON_EXHAUSTIVE_FORBIDDEN]`). Construction-literal check: exactly one field name in the literal (`error[E_UNION_LITERAL_REQUIRES_ONE_FIELD]` for zero or multiple). Field-access check: a union field read or pattern-bind requires `unsafe { }` (`error[E_UNION_READ_REQUIRES_UNSAFE]`); a `&u.field` / `&mut u.field` borrow likewise (`error[E_UNION_BORROW_REQUIRES_UNSAFE]`); a field assignment is unconditionally safe; `ptr.const(u.field)` / `ptr.mut(u.field)` are safe (they don't read the bytes — the place-expression validator already permits union field paths). (5) Layout — codegen lowers a `#[repr(C)] union Foo { ... }` to LLVM's storage with `size = max(field_sizes)`, `align = max(field_aligns)`, size rounded up to a multiple of `align`. The field-`Copy` constraint means no destructors are emitted for unions; layout-block syntax is rejected on union types (no SoA transformation makes sense). (6) Effect integration — union field reads contribute no effects to the enclosing function's inferred set; the surrounding `unsafe { }` block carries the language-level safety load. If a hardware effect is in play (volatile MMIO read interpreted as a union field), the effect is captured by the existing `volatile_read` / `reads(Hardware)` machinery, not by union semantics. (7) Cross-`extern` use — no special handling beyond what `#[repr(C) struct]` already does; `extern "C"` signatures may name union types as parameters, returns, or struct fields. Test plan: positive — `#[repr(C)] union FloatBits { f: f32, bits: u32 }` parses, type-checks, and round-trips bit-pattern reads/writes; `epoll_data` example from design.md compiles in a stub `unsafe extern "C" { }` block; `size_of[FloatBits]()` reports the larger field's size; `align_of[FloatBits]()` reports the larger field's alignment. Negative — bare `union Foo { ... }` without `#[repr]` is rejected; `union Foo { v: Vec[i32] }` (Vec is not Copy) is rejected; `impl Drop for FloatBits` is rejected; `#[derive(Eq)] union Foo { ... }` is rejected; safe-context `let v = u.bits;` is rejected; `let FloatBits { bits } = u;` outside `unsafe { }` is rejected; literal `FloatBits { f: 1.0, bits: 1 }` is rejected; literal `FloatBits {}` is rejected. (Phase 5.2 — typechecker work; depends on `#[repr]` and Pod/Copy bound infrastructure being stable. Lexer change lands together. Items 3, 18, 22 cluster together as the FFI-tightening cluster.)

- [ ] **Raw pointer construction `ptr.const` / `ptr.mut`.** Spec lives at design.md § Raw Pointer Construction (v60 item 19). Sub-steps: (1) Parser/typechecker — recognise `ptr` `.const` `(...)` and `ptr` `.mut` `(...)` as a special call form during expression-call lowering; the argument is parsed as an ordinary expression but routed through a *place-expression* validator at typecheck time rather than the value-expression typecheck. Place-expression validity matches the existing borrow-rooting rules (binding, field access, index, deref, projection chains over those); a non-place argument produces `error[E_PTR_CONST_REQUIRES_PLACE]` / `error[E_PTR_MUT_REQUIRES_PLACE]`. The `mut` form additionally checks that the place is mutably reachable using the same logic as `mut ref` borrow checking; failure produces `error[E_PTR_MUT_REQUIRES_MUTABLE_PLACE]`. The result type is `*const T` / `*mut T` where `T` is the place's type. (2) Cast-rejection — extend the existing `as`-cast typechecker to reject `&T as *const U` and `&mut T as *mut U` with `error[E_REF_TO_RAW_PTR_CAST_FORBIDDEN]`; the diagnostic includes a suggested-fix span replacing the cast with `ptr.const(...)` / `ptr.mut(...)` and points at the `as` operator. Casts between raw-pointer types (`*const T as *mut T`, etc.) remain unaffected — only the `&T → *_ T` origin cast is forbidden. (3) Stdlib `ptr` module — generic functions `null[T]() -> *const T`, `null_mut[T]() -> *mut T`, `dangling[T]() -> *const T`, `dangling_mut[T]() -> *mut T`, `is_null[T](p: *const T) -> bool`. These are ordinary stdlib items with no special parsing — only `ptr.const` / `ptr.mut` are place-form special cases. (4) Local-binding shadowing — a local binding named `ptr` shadows the prelude module within its scope; in that case `ptr.const(...)` parses as a method call on the local, and the special-form recognition does *not* fire. The standard prelude-shadow lint (warn-by-default) flags the shadow. Test plan: positive `ptr.const(local_binding)`, `ptr.const(struct_field)`, `ptr.mut(arr[i])`, `ptr.const(*ref_binding)`; rejection on value expressions (`ptr.const(x + 1)` — not a place); rejection on immutable place under `ptr.mut`; rejection of `&v as *const T`; passthrough of `*const T as *mut T`. Construction is *safe* — no `unsafe { }` block required for `ptr.const(...)` itself; only dereference, arithmetic, unaligned/volatile, and pointee-changing casts trip the unsafe rule. (Phase 5.2 — typechecker work; depends on the existing borrow-rooting / mutable-place infrastructure being stable.)

- [ ] **C-string literals — parser + stdlib `CStr` / `CString` types.** Follow-up to the Phase 5.2 lex-acceptance entry above. Sub-steps: (1) Parser — accept `Token::CStringLiteral` in expression position, lower to a literal AST node carrying the bytes and source length. (2) Typechecker — assign type `ref CStr` with `'static` lifetime to the literal expression; `CStr` resolves to a stdlib type (Phase 8). (3) Stdlib `CStr` — unsized type `[u8]`-shaped with the trailing-NUL invariant; methods `as_ptr(ref self) -> *const u8`, `len(ref self) -> i64`, `is_empty(ref self) -> bool`, `as_bytes(ref self) -> Slice[u8]`, `to_string_slice(ref self) -> Result[StringSlice, Utf8Error]`, `to_string(ref self) -> Result[String, Utf8Error]`. (4) Stdlib `CString` — owning heap-allocated counterpart; constructed via `String.to_cstring(ref self) -> Result[CString, NulError]` and `Slice[u8].to_cstring(ref self) -> Result[CString, NulError]`; `as_ptr` / `len` / `is_empty` / `as_bytes` mirror `CStr`. (5) `unsafe`-only constructor `CStr.from_raw(ptr: *const u8) -> ref CStr` for runtime-borrowed C strings (walks to terminating NUL at `O(N)` per the spec). Test plan: round-trip via FFI through a stub `extern "C" fn strlen(s: *const u8) -> usize`; `to_string_slice` on UTF-8 and non-UTF-8 inputs; `to_cstring` rejection on interior-NUL `String`. Depends on the Phase 7.2 stdlib codegen substrate landing first. (Phase 8.)

### 5.3: Advanced Diagnostics

- [x] **`--output=jsonl` streaming mode.** Newline-delimited JSON, six event types (`build_start`, `phase_start`, `phase_complete`, `phase_skipped`, `diagnostic`, `build_complete`). Strict superset of `--output=json`. See design.md § AI-First Compiler Interface > 1b. Streaming Phase Events.

- [x] **Error return traces.** Ring buffer (depth 64) at each `?` site. `"error_return_trace"` field in JSON output. Pushed on `Err`/`None` propagation, cleared on `Ok`/`Some`. Truncation flag set when buffer is full.

- [x] **Enhanced per-SCC effect diagnostics.** Tarjan's SCC algorithm detects mutual recursion groups. `"mutual_recursion_groups"` JSON field includes full effect resolution trace — which call site resolved which effect through which callee. See [deferred.md § Per-SCC Effect Diagnostics](deferred.md#per-scc-effect-diagnostics).

- [x] **`karac query` subcommands.** `karac query effects` (inferred + declared effects), `karac query ownership` (parameter modes, RC values).

- [x] **`karac query cost-summary` (static counts).** Per-function and per-module table of every silent runtime cost the compiler emitted: RC ops (Rc/Arc), Arc-provider-wraps, borrow-flag fields, partition-guard sites, auto-clone insertions. Each category aggregates into `totals` and breaks down per-function with a `derivation` array of source locations. v1 is static counts only — runtime attribution (sampling-profiler-driven %wall-clock against a real workload) is post-v1. Closed 2026-05-01 — see WIP block above for landed-implementation details. v1 wires `rc_ops` (per-function from the ownership pass), `arc_provider_wraps` (per-function `with_provider[R]` AST sites), and `borrow_flag_fields` (totals-only over `shared struct` `mut` fields); `partition_guard_sites` and `auto_clone_insertions` ship as `0` until parameterized resources and the REPL `--auto-clone` flag respectively land — schema reserves the keys so post-v1 wiring is purely additive. Codegen-time wiring of additional cost sites (e.g. tighter Arc-provider-wrap accounting once Phase 7 lowering tracks per-call closure-boundary crossings) can refine the static counts; the surface stays the same.

- [x] **`ffi_float_eq` lint.** ✓ DONE (2026-04-27) — `src/ffi_lint.rs`: `check_ffi_float_eq(program)` collects all `extern "C"` function names that return `f32`/`f64`, then walks for `BinOp::Eq`/`NotEq` where either operand is a direct call to one of those functions. Wired into `cmd_run` in `cli.rs`. 6 tests in `tests/ffi_lint.rs`. Indirect patterns (via let-binding) not tracked — requires DFA.

- [x] **`undocumented_unsafe` lint.** ✓ DONE (2026-04-27) — `src/unsafe_lint.rs`: `check_undocumented_unsafe(program, source)` walks the AST for `ExprKind::Unsafe` nodes; checks the line immediately before the `unsafe` keyword in the raw source text for `// Safety:` (case-insensitive). `#[allow(undocumented_unsafe)]` on the enclosing function suppresses; `#[deny(undocumented_unsafe)]` escalates to error. Wired into `cmd_run` in `cli.rs` (text output mode). 8 tests in `tests/unsafe_lint.rs`. Note: `unsafe fn` not yet a syntactic form; lint only covers `unsafe { }` blocks. ~~`unsafe fn` doc-comment `# Safety` section check and one-time doc pass deferred.~~

- [x] **Empty prefix-literal diagnostic — `Vec[]` / `Array[]` / `Set[]` / `Map[]` without binding annotation.** Per `design.md § Collection Literals` (line 1462), an empty prefix-literal has no element type to infer and requires a binding annotation. Today the typechecker accepts empty literals in check mode (the binding's expected type drives recovery — see `phase-8-stdlib-floor.md § Set[T] LLVM codegen` subtask 8 for the `Set[]` case; `Vec[]` / `Array[]` / `Map[]` follow the same pattern), but synthesis-mode use (no enclosing annotation) currently surfaces a generic `Type::Error` rather than a focused message. Slices: (1) Typechecker — at the `infer_expr` arm for `ExprKind::PrefixCollectionLiteral { items: [] }`, detect synthesis-mode entry (no expected type threaded from `check`) and emit `error[E_EMPTY_PREFIX_LITERAL_NEEDS_ANNOTATION]` naming the literal kind. (2) Diagnostic body — `cannot infer element type from empty 'Vec[]' literal — add a binding annotation: 'let v: Vec[T] = Vec[]'`, with per-kind annotation skeletons (`Vec[T]`, `Array[T, 0]`, `Set[T]`, `Map[K, V]`); the fix-it offers both the annotated-literal form and the corresponding constructor (`Vec.new()` / `Set.new()` / `Map.new()`) per design.md line 1470. (3) Check-mode unchanged — annotated binding, typed call argument, typed struct-field initializer continue to recover via the expected type with no diagnostic. Test coverage: bare `let x = Vec[];` / `Array[]` / `Set[]` / `Map[]` each rejected with the per-kind diagnostic; annotated forms continue to typecheck (regression — `test_set_prefix_literal_empty_with_annotation` already exists for `Set`; add `Vec` / `Array` / `Map` counterparts); typed call-arg and struct-field positions with empty literals accepted. Phase target: 5.3 (typechecker diagnostic emission only; no parser / resolver / AST changes). Closes `phase-4-interpreter.md` line 10.

- [→ P1] **`karac explain --format=json` — structured diagnostics.** Machine-parseable diagnostic output with a finite error-class enum, typed `expected` / `got` fields, and ranked candidate patches. The MVP `karac explain` ships human-readable prose only; the JSON format adds an opt-in machine-consumable shape for LLM agents and IDE tooling. Class enum freezes once the diagnostic catalogue has matured (~20+ entries). Full design in [`docs/deferred.md` § P1 § Structured Diagnostics and Error Class Enum](deferred.md#structured-diagnostics-and-error-class-enum-karac-explain---formatjson).

- [→ P1] **Signature-from-call-site stub diagnostic.** When the resolver hits an unresolved-identifier *call* inside a `_test.kara` file, enrich the existing `unresolved identifier` diagnostic with a `hints[].diff` entry that proposes a stub function in the sibling production file with parameter types inferred from the call's argument expressions, return type inferred from `assert_eq` / `==` comparison context, and a `todo()` body. Implementation picks the inference layer (resolver-time best-effort vs. post-typecheck refinement) based on quality bar; the diagnostic shape is identical at either layer. Activation gated to `_test.kara` files only — production-file unresolved calls keep the plain diagnostic. Reuses the `karac test --init` compiling-skeleton convention for `todo()` bodies. Full design in [`docs/deferred.md` § P1 § Signature-from-Call-Site Stub Diagnostic](deferred.md#signature-from-call-site-stub-diagnostic).

- [→ P1] **`karac catalog` — public API surface index.** Subcommand that indexes every exported item (fully qualified name, kind, generic parameters with bounds, parameter modes and types, return type, declared effect row, refinement constraints, source span) and emits JSONL for downstream consumers (LLM agents, IDE plugins, doc generators). Public surface only; private items have inferred reported-tier effect rows that are not stable enough to index. Full design in [`docs/deferred.md` § P1 § Signature Catalog](deferred.md#signature-catalog-karac-catalog).

- [→ P1] **`karac query affected-by` — call-graph reach query.** New `karac query` subcommand that exposes the compiler's call graph (already computed for effect inference) as a queryable surface. Given a file:line range or fully-qualified function path, returns the transitive callers, callees, and reaching test functions as JSONL with `--tests-only` and `--direction=callees|callers|all` filters. Structural prerequisite for the test-selection flags (`--related FILE`, `--since REV`) in the `karac tdd` watch driver and the `coverage_delta` event in `karac test --coverage` — without it, both features ship with reduced functionality. Implementation extends the existing query infrastructure (`karac query effects` / `ownership` / `concurrency` already shipped) by surfacing the existing graph traversals as a public JSONL surface; engineering well-understood (no research questions). Full design in [`docs/deferred.md` § P1 § karac query affected-by](deferred.md#karac-query-affected-by--call-graph-reach-query).

### 5.4: Interactive REPL and Jupyter Kernel

First-class interactive surface. **v0 → v1 transition:** the MVP REPL shipped 2026-04-28 on top of the tree-walk interpreter; the v62 lock (2026-05-06) moved the runtime backend to **always-JIT via LLJIT** for v1, with tree-walk retained only as a dev/debug tool. See `design.md § Execution Model and Compilation Targets` and the LLJIT integration entry in `phase-7-codegen.md` for the migration work; the user-facing surface (meta-commands, session model, cross-cell semantics) is unchanged by the backend swap. **Delivery split:** the REPL binary and the browser playground are P0 delivery — both optimize the frictionless first-try path that drives adoption. The Jupyter kernel is P0 priority (committed, designed, scoped) but P1 delivery — timed to ship once the stdlib is stable enough that a first-time notebook user does not hit "function not found" on common types. Semantics (cell scope, ownership across cells, effect display) are now specified in `docs/design.md § Interactive Evaluation Model`.

**P0 delivery — ships in v1.**

- [~] **`karac repl` binary.** MVP shipped 2026-04-28 — line-based REPL over the tree-walk interpreter with meta-commands `:help`, `:quit` (`/`:q`/`:exit`), `:type <expr>`, `:effects`, `:save <path>`. Items accumulate in `Session.items_source`; statement-style cells run inside a synthetic `fn main()` wrapper. New `Session::evaluate_cell_captured` test API surfaces the interpreter's `captured_output` so tests don't need to wrestle with the process's stdout fd. 13 integration tests + 7 unit tests. Open follow-ups: see the next two entries (persistent `let` bindings, cross-cell item shadowing) plus the existing standalone entries below for `--auto-clone`, the notebook-aware use-after-move diagnostic, and session export.

- [~] **`karac repl` follow-up: persistent statement-level bindings across cells.** Closed 2026-05-01 with the option-(a) source-replay model — `Session.persistent_lets` accumulates verbatim `let` source slices, prepended to every subsequent synthetic `fn main()` body, with shadow-pruning before parse so re-binding the same name across cells works. See WIP block above for landed-implementation details. The `[~]` (vs `[x]`) marker reflects that the spec's "value persists" semantics are only approximated: RHS re-runs each cell (the side-effect caveat documented in `:help` and the module docs). Option-(b) value-snapshot semantics — interpreter exposing an "extend session" entry point so prior `Value`s carry forward instead of being recomputed — is the right long-term shape and still tracked, but the v1 source-replay form covers the common notebook-style `let x = literal; … println(x);` flow without interpreter surgery. Files: `src/repl.rs`, `tests/repl.rs`.

- [x] **`karac repl` follow-up: cross-cell item re-declaration shadowing.** Closed 2026-05-01 with `prune_shadowed_items` — see WIP block above for landed-implementation details. The implementation took the AST-driven path (re-parse the buffer, identify each item's byte range via `item_span`, splice out names re-declared by the new cell) rather than the originally-suggested generalized `strip_main` brace-balance walk. AST-driven is more robust against attribute/visibility/doc-comment placement and handles every named item kind (`fn` / `struct` / `enum` / `trait` / `const` / `extern fn` / `type` alias / `distinct type` / `layout` / `effect resource` / `effect group` / `effect verb`) uniformly; anonymous items (`impl` blocks, `use` / `import`, `independent`, `alias`) have no shadowable name and are never pruned. The previously `#[ignore]`d `redeclaring_item_across_cells_shadows` test is now active.

- [x] **Notebook-aware use-after-move diagnostic.** Closed 2026-05-08. When the REPL detects a use-after-move spanning cells, the diagnostic renders a hint naming the consuming cell and suggesting `.clone()` at the call site — not an auto-clone insertion. Strictness identical to `.kara` files; only the diagnostic presentation differs. See `design.md § Interactive Evaluation Model > Ownership Across Cells`.

- [x] **`--auto-clone` opt-in mode.** Closed 2026-05-08. `karac repl --auto-clone` flag enables 2B-style ergonomics: `.clone()` inserted at the consume site when the binding is referenced in a later cell; emits `perf[auto-clone-in-repl]` note. Never silent. Inserted clones appear verbatim in session export.

- [ ] **Session export — `.kara` fidelity.** `:save session.kara` writes the session's cell history as a single `.kara` file wrapping the history in `fn main() -> Result[Unit, Error]` with declared effects matching the session's accumulated effect set. Guarantee: the exported file compiles with `karac build` and produces identical observable behavior. If auto-clone was enabled, the inserted clones appear in the exported file unchanged.

- [ ] **Cross-cell providers — `:provide R = expr` / `:end-provide R` meta-commands.** Open and close a long-lived `with_provider` scope spanning subsequent cells. Implementation steps: (1) parse the meta-command form (`:provide R = expr` consumes a resource ident + `=` + expr; `:end-provide R` consumes a resource ident); (2) maintain `Session.provider_stack: Vec<(ResourceId, Expr, FirstCellInScope)>` tracking active scopes in nesting order; (3) wrap each subsequent cell body inside an in-memory `with_provider[R](provider, || { cell_body })` when projecting the saved-session form, with one wrap per active stack entry; (4) at `:end-provide R`, pop the innermost matching frame and surface a structured error if `R` doesn't match the top of stack (LIFO close); (5) when a cell after `:end-provide` references a binding declared inside the closed scope, surface "cannot find value `X`" with a notebook-aware hint naming the provider scope that closed and the cell where `X` was declared (mirroring the use-after-move diagnostic shape from `Notebook-aware use-after-move diagnostic`); (6) construct the provider expr in the synthetic `:provide` cell — if construction panics, the scope is not opened and the panic surfaces in the cell output. Closure-capture-and-escape becomes a special case of the binding-scope rule — no separate handling. Saved-session form: each `:provide`/`:end-provide` pair compiles to one `with_provider[R](expr, || { /* cells in scope */ })` block; cell boundaries don't survive export. See `design.md § Interactive Evaluation Model > Cross-Cell Providers` for the full contract.

- [ ] **Browser playground (`play.kara-lang.org` or equivalent).** Zero-install entry point hosting the interpreter behind a web frontend — the adoption lever that does not require a local install. Architecture: server-side `karac repl` behind a minimal HTTP/WebSocket shim, or WASM-compiled interpreter running in the browser. Reach decision during implementation. Minimum UX: text editor, run button, output pane, share-by-URL. No stdlib fetch, no account, no persistence beyond URL sharing.

**P0 priority, P1 delivery — ships with v1.1 alongside stable stdlib.**

- [ ] **Jupyter kernel MVP.** Kāra kernel implementing the `jupyter_client` ZMQ protocol: shell/iopub/stdin/control channels, cell execution returning `text/plain` for the last expression, stderr routing for diagnostics with **clickable source spans in JupyterLab** (diagnostic machinery already produces spans; protocol-level wiring exposes them). Ctrl+C cooperative interrupt wired to the existing cancellation mechanism. Tab completion over current-session identifiers + prelude. Packaging: `pip install karac-kernel` (precedent: `evcxr`, `IJava`) with a Python shim that locates the `karac` binary and registers the kernelspec. Kernel process itself is Rust; the Python package is only launcher + installer.

- [ ] **Jupyter `%magic` surface (MVP subset).** `%effects` (session-wide effect set + per-cell footer display), `%ownership` (current binding table with mode/RC status), `%explain <name>` (wrap `karac explain`), `%set auto-clone on|off` (toggle the opt-in ownership mode), `%provide R = expr` / `%end-provide R` (cross-cell provider scoping — parity with the REPL meta-commands; same compilation path; see `design.md § Cross-Cell Providers`). Per-cell effect footer renders on every cell execution automatically. `%rc` magic is **deferred to post-MVP** — RC fallback analysis is still settling and its introspection surface is not yet stable enough to commit to.

**Stretch (P1+) — post-MVP kernel.**

- [ ] **Rich display for structs and collections.** `text/html` table rendering for `Vec[Struct]` (one row per element, one column per field), `text/plain` pretty-printing for nested data, `image/png` for any stdlib plotting primitive that lands. Reflection-based — uses the type registry already maintained by the type checker. Ships alongside plotting stdlib.

- [ ] **Effect-conflict timeline visualization.** Sidebar or cell-footer rendering showing per-cell effect set and cross-cell dependency arrows (e.g., "cell 3 reads `Files` written by cell 2"). Uses existing effect analysis output; purely a rendering concern in the kernel. Not a correctness concern (cells are sequential), but a teaching tool.

- [ ] **`%rc` magic.** List of RC-fallback decisions with trigger reasoning. Gated on RC-fallback diagnostic surface stabilizing.

- [ ] **Widget protocol (IPython-widgets equivalent).** Deep integration for interactive controls. v2+.

- [ ] **Provider control panel widget.** Sidebar UI showing active `with_provider` scopes (resource name, provider expr, opened-in-cell), with one-click `%end-provide` and per-cell-effect timeline annotations. Builds on the widget protocol above. Saved-session export ignores widget actions — the underlying `:provide`/`:end-provide` log is what survives. Tracked separately because it uses the cross-cell-provider mechanism specifically and is the "data-science differentiator" UI for the v1.1+ kernel.

**Book coverage — P0 prose (v1).**

- [ ] **"Getting Started, Part 2: Two Surfaces" chapter.** Dedicated chapter positioned right after "Getting Started / Installation." Shows the `.kara` file and `karac repl` terminal side by side on the same binary-search example, teaches the session model (cell scope, re-declaration, ownership across cells), and introduces the `:effects` / `:save` meta-commands. Browser playground gets a sidebar callout ("try without installing"). Ownership is taught honestly from day one — the diagnostic-softening from Q2 means no retraction later when the reader graduates to compiled files. v1 surfaces only; notebook / Jupyter content lands in v1.1 either by extending this chapter to a third surface or by adding a standalone "Notebooks" chapter.

### 5.5: Package Manager (v1.1)

All entries here are v1.1 work — v1 ships with the current parsed-but-ignored `[dependencies]` posture; this section flips it to load-bearing. Decisions are recorded in `design.md § Package System`.

- [ ] **PubGrub resolver.** Port `pubgrub-rs` or roll a Kāra-side equivalent. Inputs: `[dependencies]` + `[dev-dependencies]` + `[target.X.dependencies]` constraints across the dependency graph; output: a concrete version per package or a structured conflict diagnostic naming the constraint chain. Conflict diagnostics show the full chain ("`A` requires `C >=1.0`; `B` requires `C >=2.0`"), not a single "no solution" message. Honors the MSRV constraint via `[package].kara-version` (see toolchain entry).

- [ ] **Lockfile (`kara.lock`) reader/writer.** Schema: package name, exact version, source URL (registry-proxy mirror or git URL), BLAKE3 content hash, resolver-output dependency tree. Single lockfile across all build targets. Writer is invoked by the resolver after a successful resolve; reader is consulted on every build to pin versions. Library-vs-binary commitment is encoded by which projects check the file in (no compiler-side enforcement).

- [ ] **`karac update` and `karac update <pkg>`.** Bare form bumps every dep to the newest version compatible with declared semver constraints; surgical form bumps a single package (and any deps newly required by its update). Both rewrite `kara.lock`.

- [ ] **Registry proxy client.** HTTP client that fetches packages through `proxy.kara-lang.org` (or equivalent configured proxy) by default. Records both the original git URL (for human readability) and the proxy mirror reference (for fetch reproducibility) into `kara.lock`. `--no-proxy` flag for direct-from-source fetches in development workflows. The proxy itself is separate infrastructure (not part of `karac`); this entry is the client side.

- [ ] **Build artifact cache (`~/.kara/cache/`).** Global cache of compiled deps keyed on `(compiler-version, package-version, edition, profile, target-triple)`. Two projects with the same dep version under the same compiler / edition / profile / target share a cached object. Per-project `dist/` is already in place. Auto-invalidate on compiler upgrade (cache key includes version); never invalidate on time.

- [x] **`karac clean` and `karac clean --global`.** Bare form removes the project `dist/`; `--global` removes the user-wide `~/.kara/cache/`. Both idempotent — a missing directory is reported and treated as success. `--global` resolves the cache path from `$HOME` / `$USERPROFILE`. Commit `a5a516c`; tests in `tests/cli.rs` (`test_clean_bare_idempotent_when_no_dist`, `test_clean_bare_removes_existing_dist`, `test_clean_global_targets_kara_cache`).

- [ ] **`karac install <bin-spec>`.** Build a binary package and install it into `~/.kara/bin/`. Spec accepts `path = ...`, `git = ...`, or a registry-proxy reference. Useful pre-registry for path/git deps.
  - [x] Subcommand wired: parses `<bin-spec>` positional + help text; missing-spec errors; "not yet wired" diagnostic exits non-zero so CI scripts notice the gap — commit `a5a516c`
  - [ ] Spec resolution against the manifest dependency-entry shape (`path = "..."` / `git = "..."` / bare registry-proxy reference / `name@version`)
  - [ ] Binary build through the existing build pipeline + install into `~/.kara/bin/` (depends on dep-resolution slice)

- [ ] **`karac vendor` and `karac build --offline`.** `karac vendor` copies all resolved dependencies into a `vendor/` directory at the project root. `karac build --offline` reads dependencies only from `vendor/` and refuses any network access. Air-gap workflow for regulated environments and offline CI.
  - [x] `karac vendor` subcommand wired: parses cleanly, rejects extra args, emits "not yet wired" diagnostic + non-zero exit — commit `a5a516c`
  - [x] `--offline` flag added to existing `Build` / `BuildProject`; parses cleanly + emits "not yet wired" notice before falling through to normal behavior — commit `a5a516c`
  - [ ] `karac vendor` actually copies resolved dependencies into `./vendor/` (depends on dep-resolution slice)
  - [ ] `karac build --offline` consults only `./vendor/` and refuses any network access (depends on dep-resolution slice + resolver hookpoint)

- [ ] **`[target.X.dependencies]` and `[target.X.profile]` parsing.** Extend `manifest.rs` to recognize per-target dependency and profile blocks. Resolver consults the active target triple (from `karac build --target X` or `[build].target` default) to merge the relevant target block into the dep graph.

- [ ] **`[dev-dependencies]` excluded from non-test builds.** Resolver and build pipeline already separate test compilation from non-test compilation; ensure `[dev-dependencies]` participate only in test-mode resolution. No new infrastructure — wiring in the existing test/non-test split.

- [x] **`[package].kara-version` MSRV constraint — parser slice shipped 2026-05-17.** Parser-side field capture lands the `kara-version` field on the manifest; downstream consumers can read the declared MSRV from the parsed manifest today. Enforcement (the diagnostic-emitting half) is a separate slice tracked below.

  - [->] **Resolver enforcement against the active toolchain version.** **Reason for deferral.** Blocked on the dependency resolver landing (line 493 PubGrub) — without a resolution pipeline there's nothing to report the constraint chain against. **Reopen condition.** PubGrub resolver lands; at that point this sub-bullet flips to `[~]` and the enforcement work attaches.

  - [x] **Parser slice 1 — `kara-version` field capture shipped 2026-05-17.** Spec sentence honoured for the parser half: *"Parser accepts the field"*. **Manifest extension** in `src/manifest.rs`: `Manifest.kara_version: Option<String>` field, populated from `[package].kara-version` in `kara.toml`. The field stores the raw version string verbatim — no parsing-time interpretation of constraint syntax (`^1.0`, `>=1.2.3`, etc.) since the constraint comparator lives in the resolver alongside the active-toolchain lookup. `kara-version` is added to `KNOWN_PACKAGE_KEYS` so the unknown-key warning doesn't fire when the manifest declares it. **Validation at parse time:** wrong-type values (`kara-version = 1.0` — TOML float) are rejected with `ManifestError::InvalidFieldType { key: "kara-version", expected: "a string version constraint" }`. Empty / whitespace-only strings (`kara-version = ""`, `kara-version = "   "`) are rejected with the same error kind but a more specific `expected` message — an empty version string is more likely a mistake than an intentional "no constraint", and the no-constraint case is expressed by *omitting* the field. **Test surface (8 manifest tests in `src/manifest.rs::tests`)**: `kara_version_absent_is_none` (regression pin — absent field stays `None`); `kara_version_captured_when_present` (positive — basic `"1.0"` is captured verbatim with no warnings); `kara_version_accepts_semver_triple` (positive — `"1.2.3"`); `kara_version_accepts_caret_constraint` (positive — `"^1.0"`, pinning that the raw constraint syntax passes through unmolested for the resolver to interpret later); `kara_version_wrong_type_is_hard_error` (negative — TOML float rejected); `kara_version_empty_string_is_hard_error` and `kara_version_whitespace_only_is_hard_error` (negative — both flagged as InvalidFieldType); `kara_version_recognised_key_does_not_warn` (regression pin against a future refactor that drops `kara-version` from `KNOWN_PACKAGE_KEYS` — would silently start emitting the unknown-key warning otherwise). **What slice 1 does *not* do.** No constraint-syntax parsing — `"^1.0"` is stored as a raw string, not parsed into a structured `VersionReq`. No active-toolchain lookup — the resolver doesn't yet read this field. No diagnostic when the constraint exceeds the active compiler version (the headline behavior the spec promises). All three land alongside the resolver work at line 493.

- [ ] **`karac-toolchain.toml` reader.** `karac` parses the file from project (or workspace) root and either delegates to `karaup` (when it exists) to switch toolchain, or — if running standalone — emits a diagnostic indicating the version mismatch and the recommended action. v1 schema: `version` (required), `targets` (optional list). Channels / components / install profiles deferred.

- [x] **`:dep` REPL meta-command — syntax + registry slice closed 2026-05-01.** Parses `:dep name = "..."` (same right-hand side shape as a `[dependencies]` entry); the session's in-memory manifest accumulates pending deps; failures surface in the cell output and leave session state unchanged. State is in-memory only — no implicit persistence. New `Session.pending_deps: BTreeMap<String, String>` accumulates `name → normalized TOML value`; new `add_dep` parses the RHS by wrapping it as `[__kara_repl_dep__]\n{rest}\n` and leans on the `toml` crate to validate the shape (bare semver string OR inline table — `{ git = ... }` / `{ path = ... }` / `{ version = ... }`); failures surface `error: invalid \`:dep\` syntax — ...` and leave state unchanged; success prints the recorded entry plus a v1.1 caveat note that the package's symbols are not yet in scope; `Session::pending_deps()` accessor exposed for the future package-manager wiring; `:help` updated. 9 tests in `tests/repl.rs`.

  - [->] **Resolver / fetch / symbol-bring-into-scope plumbing.** **Reason for deferral.** Gated on the package-manager work (registry-proxy + resolver + lock-file, not yet shipped); aligns with design.md's v1.1 tag for `:dep`. **Reopen condition.** Package-manager work lands; at that point this sub-bullet flips to `[~]` and the resolve / fetch / bring-into-scope work attaches.

- [ ] **`karac run <script>` script-dir manifest discovery.** Walk upward from the *script's own directory*, not cwd, looking for `kara.toml`. Implementation: factor the existing project-root walk in `cli.rs` to accept a starting path parameter; `karac run path/to/foo.kara` passes `dirname(path/to/foo.kara)` instead of cwd. `--manifest path/to/kara.toml` overrides; `--no-manifest` forces stdlib-only.

- [x] **`karac fix` CLI wrapper.** CLI subcommand that applies machine-applicable diagnostic fixes to disk. Closed 2026-05-03; rolled out across seven rounds. Initial dispatcher (2026-05-01) — new `TextEdit { offset, length, replacement }` struct on `ResolveError` (boxed for `result_large_err` headroom), populated for E0228 (UndefinedName) and E0229 (UndefinedType); `cmd_fix` re-runs the resolver and applies edits in reverse-offset order with overlap dedupe; `--dry-run` preview; JSON envelope payload for IDE consumers. **Round 12.28** added E0225 (UnknownItemInModule). **Round 12.29** added E0223 (UnknownModule) — required new `path_spans: Vec<Span>` on `ImportDecl` so the edit targets the misspelled prefix without disturbing the import's trailing item or `as alias` clause. **Round 12.30** wired `replacement` through the multi-file JSON / JSONL paths (`resolve_errors_json`, `resolve_errors_jsonl`); E0223 / E0225 only fire in multi-file mode, so the IDE-facing payload was previously unreachable for `karac build --output=json` / `karac test` consumers. **Round 12.31** extended `replacement` to the first non-resolver class (ownership N0507, UnusedMutCaptureNote, `mut ref` → `ref` rewrite over the closure prefix) — required new `prefix_span: Option<Span>` on `ExprKind::Closure` and a `replacement` field on `OwnershipError`. **Round 12.32** swapped `cmd_fix` from a standalone resolver invocation to `Pipeline::run_all_checks()`, harvesting edits from resolver errors + ownership errors + ownership notes in one pass. The implementation diverged from the original "reads jsonl from a build invocation" sketch — the in-process path is self-contained but emits the same JSON / JSONL payload externally. Original gating note honored (not v1.1-blocked, landed opportunistically). Remaining typechecker / effectchecker tagging tracked as a P2 entry in `deferred.md § Machine-Applicable Replacement Metadata on Typechecker / Effectchecker Diagnostics`.
